## Phase 8: Standard Library — Floor

> **Note on phase split (2026-04-29):** roadmap.md splits stdlib work across Phase 8 (floor — universal modules every program needs) and [Phase 11](#phase-11-standard-library--long-tail) (long-tail — numerical/data-science stack, scripting helpers like `std.regex`/`std.http`/`std.process`/`std.stats`, security types, embedded primitives, codegen IR optimization). v1 release = end of Phase 11. The items below mix floor and long-tail because this working tracker predates the split — the **`### Numerical and data-science stdlib`** sub-section and the embedded-primitives / `std.secret` items belong to Phase 11; everything else is floor (Phase 8). The roadmap.md phase headings are the authoritative split.

- [x] **Standard I/O surface — stdlib implementation (Phase 8 interpreter MVP).** `IoError` enum (`NotFound`, `PermissionDenied`, `AlreadyExists`, `UnexpectedEof`, `InvalidUtf8`, `Interrupted`, `Other(String)`) registered in the prelude and typechecker. `Stdin`, `Stdout`, `Stderr`, `FileSystem` added to `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES`. Interpreter builtins: `Stdin.read_line()`, `Stdin.read_to_string()` → `Result[String, IoError]`; `Stdout.flush()`, `Stderr.flush()` → `Unit`; `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)` → `Result[String, IoError]`; `FileSystem.write(path, contents)` → `Result[Unit, IoError]`. Typechecker signatures registered via dot-joined `"TypeName.method"` key looked up in `resolve_path_type`. 5 typechecker tests + 4 interpreter tests added. `env.args()` → `Vec[String]` and `env.var(name)` → `Result[String, VarError]` added: `VarError` (`NotPresent`, `NotUnicode`) registered in prelude + typechecker; resolver registers lowercase `"env"` as a `SymbolKind::Module` alias; both `"Env.args"` / `"env.args"` and `"Env.var"` / `"env.var"` registered in the function table; interpreter maps `"env"` → `"Env"` in `eval_method_call` for resource dispatch. 14 typechecker tests + 14 interpreter tests added. Sub-items not yet done (factored out below as separate trackable items): `impl From[VarError] for IoError`; `env.set`; book tutorial coverage; `File` handle type; `BufReader`; network I/O; process spawning.

- [x] **`env.set(name: String, value: String)` + `writes(Env)` effect.** Landed 2026-05-08. `env.var()` and `env.args()` companion shipped: lowercase `env.set` registered in `register_compiler_intrinsic_env` (peer to `env.var`), capitalized `Env.set` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` as `#[compiler_builtin] fn set(name: String, value: String) { }` (peer to `Env.var`). Interpreter dispatch arm in `dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values` calls `std::env::set_var(&name, &value)` (runtime crate is Rust 2021 edition, so `set_var` is safe — interpreter is single-threaded at this surface), tracks `writes(Env)`, returns `Value::Unit`. Effectchecker seeds both `Env.set` and `env.set` with `writes(Env)` in the startup-seeding block (peer to the `Client.get`/`Client.post` Network seeding); the lowercase form parses as `MethodCall { object: Identifier("env") }` (the `starts_upper` gate keeps it out of the `Path` parse), so the `MethodCall` arm of `collect_calls_in_expr` mirrors the typechecker / interpreter lowercase-module alias by emitting `Env.<method>` as the call key when the receiver is the bare identifier `env`. Five new tests: `test_env_set_typechecks` and `test_env_set_wrong_arg_type_is_error` (typechecker, signature shape + arg-type error); `test_env_set_round_trips_via_var` (interpreter, `env.set` then `env.var` observes the same value); `test_env_set_infers_writes_env`, `test_env_set_capitalized_form_infers_writes_env`, `test_pub_fn_calling_env_set_must_declare_writes_env` and `test_pub_fn_with_writes_env_declared_accepts_env_set` (effectchecker, both call-key paths + negative `MissingEffectDeclaration` + positive declared-effect dual). Cargo test 2967 + LLVM 3258 green; clippy + fmt clean.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-07).* Pure pattern-extension of the existing `env.var` / `env.args` registration in the typechecker and interpreter, plus a `writes(Env)` effect seed. No design judgment.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Typechecker — register `"Env.set"` and `"env.set"` in the function table with signature `fn set(name: String, value: String) with writes(Env)`. The `Env` resource is already in `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES`. Mirrors the existing `env.var` registration site.
  - **(b)** Interpreter — `eval_method_call` already maps `"env"` receiver → `"Env"` type; add the `"set"` arm calling `std::env::set_var(name, value)`. Returns `Unit`.
  - **(c)** Effect-checker — `Env.set` carries `writes(Env)`; rejection at non-`writes(Env)`-declaring callers should fire automatically through existing infra. Verify via a negative test.

  *Tests* (3 new): `test_env_set_typechecks` (typechecker, signature shape); `test_env_set_round_trips_via_var` (interpreter, `env.set("X", "v"); env.var("X") == "v"`); `test_env_set_without_writes_effect_rejects` (effectchecker).

  *Files expected to change.* `src/typechecker.rs` (~15 lines mirroring `env.var` registration); `src/interpreter.rs` (~10 lines, new `"set"` arm); `tests/typechecker.rs` + `tests/interpreter.rs` + `tests/effectchecker.rs` (3 tests); this doc (close-out).

  *Out of scope.*
  - `env.unset(name)` — not in the deferred-portion sentence; spec only names `set`.
  - `File` / `BufReader` / network I/O / process spawning — separate Standard I/O follow-ups.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - The effect-checker doesn't auto-seed `writes(Env)` for stdlib registrations the way it does for other resource verbs — would need design discussion.
  - `std::env::set_var` flagged unsafe in current Rust toolchain due to multi-threaded modification semantics; if this surfaces as a compile-time issue, halt.

  *Deviations from plan.* Two honest tags: (1) **Effect-checker seeding required two keys, not zero.** Plan said "rejection at non-`writes(Env)`-declaring callers should fire automatically through existing infra"; in practice neither `Env.var` nor `env.var` are seeded today (the existing `with reads(Env)` typecheck tests pass vacuously — there is no enforcement on the existing surface). Adding the seed for the new `env.set` / `Env.set` keys is one explicit `for fn_name in ["Env.set", "env.set"]` block mirroring the `Client.get` / `Client.post` Network seeding three blocks up; it is the minimum to make the negative test (a real `MissingEffectDeclaration` error fires when a `pub fn` calls `env.set` without declaring `writes(Env)`) work. (2) **MethodCall lowercase-alias call-key emission.** The capitalized form `Env.set(...)` parses as `Call(Path([Env, set]))` and routes through `extract_callee_name` → `Env.set` automatically. The lowercase form `env.set(...)` parses as `MethodCall { object: Identifier("env"), method: "set" }` because `starts_upper("env") == false` keeps it out of the parser's `Path`-rooted branch — so the call-collection loop in `collect_calls_in_expr`'s `MethodCall` arm needed an explicit lowercase-alias check (peer to the typechecker's `infer_method_call` lowercase-module branch and the interpreter's `eval_method_call` alias map) emitting `Env.<method>` as the call key. The added check is conservative — fires only when the receiver is the literal identifier `env` — so it cannot create false positives for user code. Both deviations are structural-not-semantic: same effect-resource verbs, same call-key shape, just an explicit registration site where the plan assumed implicit propagation.

- [x] **`impl From[VarError] for IoError`.** Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up — needed for `?`-propagation from `env.var(...) -> Result[String, VarError]` into functions returning `Result[T, IoError]`. Variant mapping: `VarError.NotPresent` → `IoError.NotFound`; `VarError.NotUnicode` → `IoError.InvalidUtf8`.

  *What landed (2026-05-08).* `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` gained a single `impl From for IoError { fn from(e: VarError) -> IoError { match e { VarError.NotPresent => IoError.NotFound, VarError.NotUnicode => IoError.InvalidUtf8 } } }` block at file-bottom (mirrors the existing user-side `impl From for AppError` test fixture shape — Kāra's `From` impl head omits the source-type bracket; the source flows through the `from` parameter type, and `find_from_impl` disambiguates by matching the first-param type against the source). The body is plain Kāra source, not `#[compiler_builtin]` — the interpreter's baked-stdlib walk registers it as a `Value::Function` keyed `IoError.from` and the existing path-call dispatch routes through it. Typechecker registration is automatic via `env_add_impl` walking `STDLIB_PROGRAMS`. The `?` site at `env.var("CONFIG")?` now records `IoError` in `TypeCheckResult.question_conversions` (verified by a typechecker test reading the side-table directly), and the desugar produces `IoError.NotFound` at runtime when the env var is unset (verified end-to-end in the interpreter). Six new tests:
  - `tests/typechecker.rs` (3): `test_var_error_to_io_error_question_propagation` (asserts `question_conversions` records `IoError`); `test_var_error_to_io_error_explicit_from_call` (`IoError.from(VarError.NotPresent)` typechecks and unifies with the expected `IoError`); `test_var_error_to_io_error_into_drives_from_impl` (`.into()` at a `let: IoError` annotation rewrites to `IoError.from(e)` via the same impl).
  - `tests/interpreter.rs` (3): `test_var_error_not_present_maps_to_io_error_not_found` and `test_var_error_not_unicode_maps_to_io_error_invalid_utf8` (both variants confirmed by an exhaustive match against every `IoError` variant); `test_var_error_question_propagation_produces_io_error_not_found` (end-to-end `env.var(unset)?` returns `Err(IoError.NotFound)`).

  *Deviations from plan.* One inline-fix scope expansion: the interpreter's baked-stdlib registration walk only handled `Item::ImplBlock`, not `Item::EnumDef`. With baked enums un-walked, `let e = IoError.NotFound` (and any other path-style enum-variant *expression*) hit the `path '...' not found at ...:...; should be caught by resolver` `unreachable!` in `eval_path` because no `IoError.NotFound` value was bound in the interpreter env. Match-arm patterns worked already (the resolver tags variant patterns structurally), which is why nothing tripped earlier — every prior test using `IoError.NotFound` did so only in pattern position (e.g., `tests/interpreter.rs::test_filesystem_read_nonexistent_file_returns_err`). The pre-existing `Ordering` / `MemoryOrdering` enums dodged the issue via hand-written `register_items` blocks that pre-bind every unit variant. The fix in this slice generalizes that pattern: extend the baked-stdlib walk in `Interpreter::register_items` (the same `for item in &baked_items` loop that already calls `register_impl_methods` for `Item::ImplBlock`) to also enumerate `Item::EnumDef` and bind each unit variant under its qualified `Type.Variant` path. Tuple/struct variants are handled at call sites just like user-program enums, so they need no special-casing here. With the fix in place, every baked-stdlib enum (current: `Option`, `Result`, `Ordering`, `MemoryOrdering`, `IoError`, `VarError`, `Entry`, `RegexError`, `HttpError`, `DecodeError`) supports path-style construction at the use site. The hand-written `Ordering.{Less,Equal,Greater}` and `MemoryOrdering.{Relaxed,Acquire,Release,AcqRel,SeqCst}` registrations in `register_items` are now redundant on net, but kept in place this slice — removing them is a peer cleanup, not the slice's scope.

  *Out of scope (still open).* `impl From` for other I/O error pairs (network errors, fs errors) — only `VarError → IoError` is named in the deferred-portion sentence; reverse direction (`From[IoError] for VarError`) — not meaningful, one-way conversion only; the redundant hand-written `Ordering`/`MemoryOrdering` variant registrations in `Interpreter::register_items` — peer-to-this-slice cleanup, deferred so this slice stays single-commit.

- [x] **`SortedSet[T: Ord]` stdlib type.** `Value::SortedSet(BTreeMap<OrdValue, ()>)` added to the interpreter; `OrdValue` newtype wraps `Value` and implements `Ord` via `value_compare` so `Value` can key a `BTreeMap` without global `Ord`. `SortedSet` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `stub_generics(["T"])` in `prelude.rs` and as a generic struct in `register_builtin_types`. `SortedSet.new()` handled in the path-call dispatch. Method surface: `len`, `is_empty`, `contains`, `insert`, `remove`, `min`, `max`, `union`, `intersection`, `difference` — all with write-back via `self.env.set` for mutation methods. `for` loop updated to iterate SortedSet in ascending key order (`into_keys()`). `infer_sorted_set_method` added to typechecker; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "SortedSet" }`. 12 typechecker tests + 11 interpreter tests added. ~~Open: `T: Ord` bound enforcement at call sites (deferred to associated types / trait bound checking); effect annotation for `new` (`allocates(Heap)`).~~ Now closed: `T: Ord` enforced via `type_supports_ord` check at each `infer_sorted_set_method` dispatch (E0232); `allocates(Heap)` seeded in effect checker. SortedSet LLVM codegen: deferred to v1 — B-tree is too complex to shim cleanly; stays interpreter-only through v1.

- [x] **`Map[K, V]` stdlib type — insertion-order key-value map.** `Value::Map(Vec<(Value, Value)>)` already existed in the interpreter; this CR wires the full method surface and typechecker dispatch. `Map` registered as a generic struct `["K", "V"]` in `register_builtin_types`. `Map.new()` added to path-call dispatch. Method surface: `len`, `is_empty`, `contains_key`, `get(k) -> Option[V]`, `get_or(k, default) -> V`, `insert(k, v) -> Option[V]` (returns old value), `remove(k) -> Option[V]`, `keys() -> Vec[K]`, `values() -> Vec[V]`, `entries() -> Vec[(K, V)]`, `merge(other) -> Map[K, V]` (right-wins on key collision). `for` loop updated to iterate Map as `(K, V)` tuple pairs in insertion order. `infer_map_method` added to typechecker; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "Map" }` before SortedSet dispatch. 13 typechecker tests + 12 interpreter tests added. ~~Open: `Hash` bound enforcement on K at call sites (deferred to associated types); `allocates(Heap)` effect for `new`/`insert`.~~ Now closed: `K: Hash + Eq` enforced via `type_supports_hash + type_supports_eq` check at each `infer_map_method` dispatch (E0232); `allocates(Heap)` seeded in effect checker. Map LLVM codegen — complete. Approach: runtime-shim (C hash table in `karac-runtime`, opaque `i8*` in LLVM IR, vtable-style fn pointers for hash/eq). `SortedSet` deferred — stays interpreter-only through v1. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Runtime shim** — `runtime/src/map.rs`: open-addressing linear-probe hash table, vtable interface (`hash_fn*`/`eq_fn*`), all 9 symbols (`karac_map_new/free/insert/get/remove/contains/len/iter_new/iter_next/iter_free`). `libkarac_runtime.a` rebuilt clean.
  - [x] **2. Map type lowering + extern fn declarations** — `Map[K,V]`/`Set[T]`/`SortedSet[T]` lower to opaque `ptr` in `llvm_type_for_type_expr`. All 10 `karac_map_*` externs declared in `Codegen::new()`. `map_key_types`/`map_val_types` side-tables added (mirrors `vec_elem_types`); populated from `let` type annotations via `extract_map_kv_types`.
  - [x] **3. Map method codegen** — `compile_map_new_stmt` (early-exit in `compile_stmt`, mirrors SoA pattern), `compile_map_method` (`insert`/`get`/`remove`/`contains_key`/`len`/`is_empty`), `FreeMapHandle` cleanup action + `track_map_var`. `Map.new()` uses null fn pointers (stub until task 4). All tests green.
  - [x] **4. Hash/eq fn pointer generation** — `emit_hash_fn_for_type` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type` (internal LLVM fns, emitted once per module per K type): FNV-1a over raw bytes for primitives; content hash/eq for `String` (loads `{ptr,len}` from struct). `map_key_type_names` side-table drives selection. `insert`/`remove` return type corrected to `Option[V]` (was Unit/bool); `karac_map_insert_old` + `karac_map_remove_old` added to runtime. All 929 tests green.
  - [x] **5. For-loop iteration** — `compile_for_map_var`: iterator-based loop via `karac_map_iter_new/next/free`. `loop_bb` calls `iter_next(iter, out_key, out_val)`; `body_bb` builds `{K,V}` struct and delivers to `bind_pattern` (tuple patterns work via existing struct-extract path); `exit_bb` calls `iter_free` unconditionally so `break` also frees. `continue_bb = loop_bb`. Verified: i64-key sum, String-key count, break mid-iteration.
  - [x] **6. E2E tests + checklist update** — 12 `tests/codegen.rs` cases: `i64`-key insert/get (Some/None), insert-returns-old, remove (Some/None), contains_key, len/is_empty, for-loop value sum; `String`-key insert/get, insert-returns-old, remove, contains/len, for-loop count. All 12 pass under `cargo test --features llvm`.

- [x] **`Channel[T]` / `Sender[T]` / `Receiver[T]` core stdlib types.** `Value::Sender(Arc<Mutex<VecDeque<Value>>>)` and `Value::Receiver(Arc<Mutex<VecDeque<Value>>>)` added; `Channel.new()` wired in path-call dispatch — creates one `Arc<Mutex<VecDeque>>`, wraps it in a `(Sender, Receiver)` tuple so both ends share the same queue. Method surface: `Sender.send(val)` pushes to queue, `Sender.clone()` Arc-clones the producer, `Receiver.recv()` pops front (returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking — MVP single-threaded limitation), `Receiver.try_recv()` returns `Option[T]`. `Channel`, `Sender`, `Receiver` registered as generic structs `["T"]` in `register_builtin_types` + `PRELUDE_TYPES` / `stub_generics`. `infer_channel_method` added; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "Sender" | "Receiver" }`. 7 typechecker tests + 6 interpreter tests added (send-recv round-trip, FIFO ordering, try_recv on empty, cloned sender, string values). ~~Open: effect-checker `suspends` propagation for `recv`; `recv` blocking semantics in multi-threaded codegen path; `allocates(Heap)` effect for `new` + `send`.~~ `suspends` for `recv` and `allocates(Heap)` for `new`/`send` now seeded in effect checker. Open: `recv` blocking semantics in multi-threaded codegen path (blocked on Phase 6 concurrency).

- [x] **`Slice[T]` stdlib methods.** Core type and coercion ship in Phase 4; the full method surface lands here. Mirror the `Vec[T]` read-only / in-place surface where the operation makes sense on a borrowed view: `len`, `is_empty`, `first`, `last`, `get(i) -> Option[ref T]`, `iter()`, `chunks(n)`, `windows(n)`, `split_at(i) -> (Slice[T], Slice[T])`, `contains(ref T) where T: Eq`, `binary_search(ref T) where T: Ord`. Mutable-only: `sort() where T: Ord`, `sort_by(cmp)`, `reverse()`, `fill(val) where T: Clone`, `iter_mut()`, `swap(i, j)`. No `push`/`pop`/`remove` — those require capacity management and belong on `Vec[T]`. Document each method's effect set (most are effect-free; `sort` may `allocates(Heap)` for auxiliary buffers).

- [x] **Iterator trait — full adaptor surface.** Beyond the named-in-roadmap adaptors (`filter`, `map`, `collect`, `fold`, `any`, `all`), ship the long-tail combinators that real iterator code depends on: `chain`, `zip`, `enumerate`, `take(n)`, `skip(n)`, `take_while(pred)`, `skip_while(pred)`, `flat_map(f)`, `peekable`, `chunk_by(key_fn)`, `step_by(n)`, `cycle`, `inspect(f)`, `scan(state, f)`, `windows(n)`, `chunks(n)`. Each is a 5–20 line implementation once `Iterator` is in place. Real programs use the long tail; absence forces hand-roll. Most are effect-free; ones that buffer (`chunk_by`, `windows`) may `allocates(Heap)`. Closed 2026-05-04. Final commit `6d23f94` (`chunks(n)` / `windows(n)` on Iterator). Shipped surface: terminals `next`, `count`, `collect`, `fold`, `any`, `all`; step-layer adaptors `map`, `filter`, `enumerate`, `take(n)`, `skip(n)`, `take_while(pred)`, `skip_while(pred)`, `step_by(n)`, `inspect(f)`, `scan(init, f)`; source-layer adaptors `iter` / `into_iter` (Eager), `chain(other)`, `zip(other)`, `flat_map(f)`, `cycle()`, `peekable()`, `chunk_by(key_fn)`, `chunks(n)`, `windows(n)`; plus `peek()` exclusive to the `Peekable[T]` named type returned by `peekable()`. Heap-allocating adaptors with `allocates(Heap)` seeded in the effectchecker: `Iterator.chunk_by`, `Iterator.chunks`, `Iterator.windows` (and route via `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` so `Vec.chunks` / `Vec.windows` callers also pick up the effect, closing a pre-existing under-report). Test coverage: **227** dedicated iterator tests — 133 interpreter, 91 typechecker, 3 effectchecker. Implementation rides `Value::Iterator { source: IteratorSource, steps: Vec<IteratorStep> }` with 9 source variants (`Eager`, `Chain`, `Zip`, `FlatMap`, `Cycle`, `Peekable`, `ChunkBy`, `Chunks`, `Windows`) and 10 step variants (`Map`, `Filter`, `Enumerate`, `Take`, `Skip`, `TakeWhile`, `SkipWhile`, `StepBy`, `Inspect`, `Scan`). Notable design choices documented inline at the variant doc-comments: `Peekable[T]` is a distinct named type that loses peek-capability after any adaptor (matching Rust's `Map<Peekable<I>>`); `scan` deviates from Rust's `Fn(&mut St, T) -> Option<B>` to `Fn(A, T) -> Option<(A, U)>` because tree-walk closures snapshot captures and there's no `mut ref` parameter mode; multi-source / lookahead adaptors (`chunk_by`, `chunks`, `windows`, `flat_map`, `peekable`, `cycle`) are sources rather than steps because they break the 1:1 source-pull → output-item assumption that Steps make.

- [x] **`std.encoding` — base64, hex, URL encode/decode.** Closed 2026-05-03. Interpreter-only namespace under `Base64.*` / `Hex.*` / `Url.*` (mirrors the `Stats` / `Regex` precedent — typechecker registers each function name in `env.functions`, interpreter dispatches on the path string). Functions: `Base64.encode(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (standard alphabet, `=`-padded), `Base64.encode_url_safe(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (URL-safe alphabet, no padding), `Base64.decode(s: String) -> Result[Vec[u8], DecodeError]` (accepts both alphabets, ignores ASCII whitespace), `Hex.encode(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (lowercase), `Hex.encode_upper(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String`, `Hex.decode(s: String) -> Result[Vec[u8], DecodeError]` (case-insensitive, even-length only), `Url.encode(s: String) -> String` (RFC 3986 percent-encoding — preserves the unreserved set `A-Za-z0-9-._~`, percent-encodes everything else), `Url.decode(s: String) -> Result[String, DecodeError]`. The original spec called for "standard + URL-safe via flag" / "lowercase + uppercase via flag" — Kāra has no default-arg or boolean-flag-arg idiom in its stdlib (Stats, Regex use the separate-function form); the implementation mirrors the precedent. New `DecodeError { message: String }` struct registered in the typechecker (parallels `RegexError`); decode failures populate the message. New types added to `PRELUDE_TYPES`: `Base64`, `Hex`, `Url`, `DecodeError`. 22 new tests (8 typechecker — signature shape per function — + 14 interpreter — RFC 4648 base64 vectors with 1/2/3-byte padding + URL-safe alphabet + base64 round-trip + invalid-char rejection / hex lower & upper + mixed-case decode + odd-length rejection / URL preserves unreserved set + percent-encode + round-trip + invalid percent-encoding rejection). No codegen support today (parallels `Regex`); compiled-binary support is a follow-up if/when needed. Files: `src/prelude.rs`, `src/typechecker.rs`, `src/interpreter.rs`, `tests/typechecker.rs`, `tests/interpreter.rs`.

- [x] **Lexer: reserve `expr_<NNNN>` fragment-specifier identifier namespace.** Closed 2026-05-04 in commit `1559772`. The check lives in `src/lexer.rs` `identifier()`'s fallthrough arm via the `is_reserved_fragment_specifier_namespace` helper (manual byte-class check; no regex on the hot path). Raw-escape exemption is structural — `r#expr_2026` flows through `raw_identifier()`, which never enters the keyword match path, so no `was_raw_escaped` flag is needed at the token level. 7 tests in `tests/lexer.rs` cover boundary years (2020 / 2026 / 2099) at let / fn / struct-field positions, both fix-its in the diagnostic, the raw-escape exemption, and every accept-path negative case (no prefix, different prefix, non-year suffix, year out of range on both sides, wrong digit count). Original spec preserved below for the historical record. Spec at `design.md § Reserved Fragment-Specifier Identifier Namespace` (v60 item 62). Slices: (1) **Lexer regex check.** In `src/lexer.rs`, after recognising an identifier token, run a pattern check against `^expr_(\d{4})$`. If the regex matches AND the captured digit string parses as a year in the range `2020`..=`2099` inclusive, emit `error[E_RESERVED_FRAGMENT_SPECIFIER_NAMESPACE]: 'expr_<NNNN>' is a reserved identifier name; this naming convention is reserved for future edition-versionable syntax categories in macros / comptime fragment specifiers — use 'r#expr_<NNNN>' if you need this exact identifier today, or rename to a non-year-suffixed form` with the offending span underlined and the two fix-its (the raw-identifier escape OR a rename suggestion). (2) **Raw-identifier exemption.** When the identifier is preceded by `r#` (raw-identifier escape per item 39), the reservation does NOT fire — `r#expr_2026` parses as the bare identifier `expr_2026` and is accepted. The exemption falls out of the existing raw-identifier handling: the regex is checked AFTER the raw-prefix has been stripped, so `r#expr_2026` strips to `expr_2026` for downstream consumers but the reservation is checked against the *original lexed form* before stripping. Implementation detail: track a `was_raw_escaped` flag on the identifier token; if true, skip the namespace check. (3) **Narrow scope at v1.** The reservation matches ONLY the `expr_` prefix. Other plausible fragment-specifier prefixes (`pat`, `ty`, `stmt`, `block`, `tt`, `ident`, `lit`, `path`, `vis`, `meta`, `item`, `lifetime`) are NOT reserved at v1 — extending the reservation post-v1 to additional prefixes is non-breaking-additive (existing user identifiers using those prefixes continue to work). (4) **Year range.** `2020`..=`2099` inclusive. Years outside this range (e.g., `expr_1999`, `expr_3000`) parse as ordinary identifiers without rejection. The range matches the realistic edition-year window for any Kāra release. (5) **Diagnostic shape.** Span underlines the full identifier including the year suffix. Help line offers the raw-escape fix-it (`r#expr_2026`) and the rename fix-it (`expression_2026` or similar). (6) **No connection to literal year value.** The reservation is purely a namespace allocation, not tied to a specific year value. `expr_2026` is reserved today even though Kāra's current edition is `2026`; `expr_2099` is reserved even though no compiler will see it for decades. (7) **Test coverage.** Positive — `let x = 1;` (no prefix) accepts; `let expression = 1;` accepts; `let expr_v2 = 1;` accepts (non-year suffix); `let version_2026 = 1;` accepts (different prefix); `let expr_1999 = 1;` accepts (year out of reserved range); `let expr_3000 = 1;` accepts (year out of reserved range); `let r#expr_2026 = 1;` accepts (raw-escape exemption); function declaration `fn expr_v2() { }` accepts. Negative — `let expr_2020 = 1;` rejected with `E_RESERVED_FRAGMENT_SPECIFIER_NAMESPACE`; `let expr_2026 = 1;` rejected; `let expr_2099 = 1;` rejected; function declaration `fn expr_2026() { }` rejected at function-name lex; struct field `struct S { expr_2030: i64 }` rejected at field-name lex; the diagnostic includes both fix-its inline. Phase target: 1 (Lexer) — small lex-time check; reuses the existing identifier tokenisation path. No P1 carve-out — the reservation ships at v1 to lock in the namespace before users can rely on it.

- [ ] **Per-stdlib-type variance declarations + verifier + user-side rejection.** Spec at `design.md § Variance` (v60 item 57). Three layers: a parser/AST surface for `+T` / `-T` / `=T` markers, a stdlib-side verifier that proves the markers consistent with the type's structure, and a user-side rejection diagnostic that reserves the syntax for v1. The covariant types (`Option`, `Result`, `Iterator`, `TaskHandle`, `AlreadySetError`) are the load-bearing payoff — they unlock subtyping that today's all-invariant rule blocks.

  1. [ ] **Lexer.** `+`, `-`, `=` already lex as symbols; no new token kinds.
  2. [ ] **Parser + AST.** Extend `GENERIC_PARAM` per syntax.md §6.4 to accept an optional leading `VARIANCE_MARKER` (`+` / `-` / `=`) before the parameter identifier. The marker attaches to the parameter, not to the bound — `+T: Ord` is `(+ T) (: Ord)`, not `(+ T:Ord)`. AST: extend `GenericParam` with `variance: Variance { Covariant, Contravariant, Invariant }` field; default `Invariant` when no marker is present.
  3. [ ] **Resolver — user-side rejection at v1.** When a generic-parameter declaration in *user* code (i.e., not in stdlib source files) carries `+` or `-`, emit `error[E_VARIANCE_USER_DECL_NOT_YET]: variance declarations are reserved for stdlib types in v1; remove the marker — the parameter will be invariant`. Stdlib source files (identified by package name = `std` / `core` / `karac-runtime` or by a `#[stdlib_type]` attribute on the type, depending on the bootstrapping decision) accept the markers.
  4. [ ] **Variance verifier — stdlib-side enforcement.** New typechecker pass `verify_variance` runs at type-decl time on every parametric stdlib type. For each declared parameter `T` with declared variance `V`, walk the type's structure (fields, variant payloads, trait-method signatures on inherent impls, etc.) and check that `T` appears only in positions consistent with `V`: `+T` requires `T` only in covariant positions (return-types, immutable-borrow targets, covariant slots of inner types per their own declarations); `-T` requires `T` only in contravariant positions; `=T` is unrestricted. Failure emits `error[E_VARIANCE_DECLARATION_INCONSISTENT]: parameter '<T>' declared '<+T/-T/=T>' (<co/contra/inv>variant) appears in <invariant/contravariant> position '<field/method/...>' inside type '<TypeName>'` with the offending position's span underlined and a fix-it suggesting the next-most-conservative declaration (e.g., if `+T` fails, suggest `=T`).
  5. [ ] **Position-based variance pass — already exists.** Verify the existing typechecker handles function argument contravariance, return covariance, effect-set covariance, `mut ref` invariance, `ref` covariance per `design.md § Variance` table. This entry adds the per-type layer; the position-based layer is unchanged.
  6. [ ] **Stdlib audit — apply variance declarations to every stdlib parametric type.** One-time review of every parametric stdlib type as of v1; add the marker to its declaration per the audit table in design.md. Types: `Vec[=T]`, `Slice[=T]`, `Array[=T, const N]`, `Map[=K, =V]`, `Set[=T]`, `VecDeque[=T]`, `SortedSet[=T]`, `Option[+T]`, `Result[+T, +E]`, `Iterator[+T]`, `Box[=T]`, `Rc[=T]`, `Arc[=T]`, `Sender[=T]`, `Receiver[=T]`, `Channel[=T]`, `Atomic[=T]`, `Mutex[=T]`, `RwLock[=T]`, `LazyLock[=T]`, `OnceLock[=T]`, `OnceCell[=T]`, `MaybeUninit[=T]`, `PhantomData[=T]`, `TaskHandle[+T]`, `AlreadySetError[+T]`. The migration is mechanical — change `Vec[T]` declaration to `Vec[=T]` (or omit the marker, since `=T` is the default) and so on for the others.
  7. [ ] **Stdlib lint — every parametric stdlib type must carry an explicit variance declaration.** Lint that fires at the stdlib build step when a parametric type is declared without a marker on every parameter. The default is invariant via `=T` or no-marker; the lint requires *every* parameter to be either explicitly `=T`-marked OR explicitly `+T`/`-T` (no implicit). This forces the stdlib author to make a deliberate choice rather than accept the default by accident. User-code types are unaffected (the lint is stdlib-only).
  8. [ ] **Subtyping rule — at use sites.** When the typechecker is checking whether `Foo[Sub]` is a subtype of `Foo[Super]` (e.g., a coercion / pattern match / let-binding), the variance declaration of `Foo`'s parameter governs the check: `+T` → `Sub <: Super` required; `-T` → `Super <: Sub` required; `=T` → `Sub == Super` required. The check composes with refinement-to-base widening: `Iterator[Positive]` widens to `Iterator[i32]` via the `+T` covariance + the refinement widening; `Vec[Positive]` does NOT widen to `Vec[i32]` because `Vec[=T]` is invariant.
  9. [ ] **Test coverage.** Positive — `Iterator[Positive]` accepts where `Iterator[i32]` is expected; `Option[NonZero]` widens to `Option[i32]`; `Result[Positive, IoError]` widens to `Result[i32, IoError]`; `Vec[i32]` does NOT widen to `Vec[Number]` (invariant); `Sender[String]` does NOT widen to `Sender[Object]`; verifier accepts `Option[+T]` (T appears only in `Some(T)` payload, covariant); verifier accepts `Atomic[=T]` (T appears in atomic-load-and-store positions, must be invariant). Negative — user-code `struct MyContainer[+T] { ... }` rejected with `E_VARIANCE_USER_DECL_NOT_YET`; stdlib `struct Cell[+T] { mut field: T }` rejected with `E_VARIANCE_DECLARATION_INCONSISTENT` because `+T` cannot appear at a `mut` field position; stdlib parametric type without any variance marker rejected by stdlib lint.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) — parser + AST + variance verifier; the stdlib audit is a coordinated CR with the verifier landing first. No P1 carve-out for the verifier itself — option (a) of v60 item 57 ships at v1. The user-side variance declaration surface IS the P1 follow-up; the v1 reservation (focused diagnostic) ensures the surface lands later without source breaks.

- [ ] **Stdlib lint — `drop_carries_soundness` audit checklist.** Spec at `design.md § Drop > Destructors are NOT soundness mechanisms` (v60 item 56 — Tier-E pin). The principle is a documentation pin, not a runtime check; the implementation work is a **code-review checklist** baked into the stdlib hygiene suite. For every new stdlib type that ships a `Drop` impl, the reviewer must answer "if Drop is removed (the destructor never runs), what becomes unsafe?" The answer must be "nothing" — only resources leak, no UB, no type-system violation. Slices: (1) **Stdlib code-review checklist.** Add the question to the stdlib PR template (or equivalent). Reviewers explicitly call out the answer in the PR body when adding a new `Drop` impl, especially on shared / public stdlib types. (2) **Negative-test convention.** New stdlib types with `Drop` impls add a "Drop-skip soundness" test that exercises the type's safety properties in the absence of the destructor running — typically by holding the type past a panic-under-abort path, or (post-v1, when a forget primitive ships) by explicitly skipping Drop and checking that the type remains sound. The test pins the invariant at the test layer; if a future change introduces Drop-dependent soundness, the test fails. (3) **Audit existing stdlib types.** One-time review of every stdlib type with a `Drop` impl as of v1 — `MutexGuard`, `RwLockReadGuard`, `RwLockWriteGuard`, `RefCellRefGuard`, `RefCellMutGuard`, IRQ-disable guard, future RAII guards — confirming each one satisfies the principle. The audit produces a per-type note in the stdlib documentation explaining where the soundness comes from (typically: the borrow checker enforces the lock's aliasing rules; Drop only runs the unlock action). (4) **Documentation cross-reference.** Every `impl Drop` in stdlib gets a doc-comment line explaining "soundness derives from the type system; this destructor runs cleanup." The line is template boilerplate but reinforces the principle at every site reviewers encounter. (5) **No new compiler diagnostic.** This is a checklist + documentation discipline, not a compile-time enforcement — the principle is too semantic to mechanize ("would skipping Drop cause UB?" is a meta-question about every API the type touches, not a local property). The compiler does enforce the related rules (e.g., `Drop` body must be `panics`-free, `Drop` and `Copy` mutually exclusive) — those land in their own checklist entries. **Test coverage.** Per-stdlib-type "Drop-skip soundness" assertions (point 2 above) — exact form depends on the type; generally constructs the value, holds it across a panic-under-abort code path or a process.exit, asserts the program exits cleanly without UB. These tests run alongside the regular stdlib test suite. Phase target: Phase 8 (Standard Library — Floor) — bundled with each stdlib type's own implementation; no separate slice. The audit of existing types runs once at the v1 freeze before stdlib API stabilization.

- [x] **`marker trait` syntax + stdlib marker migration.** Spec at `design.md § Marker Traits` (v60 item 55). Slices: (1) **Lexer.** Add `marker` to the keyword arm in `src/lexer.rs` (currently a free identifier). The keyword token kind is unconditional; users with a local binding named `marker` must rename or use `r#marker`. (2) **Parser.** Recognize `[ATTRIBUTES] [VIS] "marker" "trait" IDENT [GENERIC_PARAMS] [":" SUPERTRAIT_BOUNDS] [WHERE_CLAUSE] (";" | "{" "}")` per syntax.md §3.4. AST: new `Item::MarkerTrait { name, generic_params, supertraits, where_clause, vis, attributes, span }`. Body must be either bare semicolon or empty `{ }` — both forms produce identical AST representation; the parser distinguishes only for round-trip formatting. Methods, associated types, associated consts inside the body are rejected at parse with `error[E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD]: marker traits cannot declare methods; remove the method or change 'marker trait' to 'trait'` or `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM` (for type/const items), each with the suggested-fix span pointing at the `marker` keyword (offering "remove `marker`") and at the offending body content (offering "remove this method/item"). (3) **Resolver.** Register the marker trait in the trait namespace alongside ordinary traits. Marker-trait resolution participates in trait-bound resolution, supertrait check, and impl coherence the same as regular traits — the marker-ness is a definition-site property, not a use-site property. (4) **Empty-impl-body enforcement.** When an impl block targets a trait that resolves to `Item::MarkerTrait`, verify the impl body is empty `{ }`. Methods, associated types, default-method overrides inside the body are rejected with `error[E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD]: impl of marker trait '<name>' cannot contain methods or items; the body must be empty`. The check runs at the impl-resolution step in the typechecker, after the impl's target trait is identified. (5) **Auto-implementation forbidden** — verify (no enforcement work; just confirm the typechecker never generates `impl Marker for T { }` from auto-trait inference). The closed compiler-known marker traits (`ScopeLocal`, future `Concurrent`) have compiler-emitted impls for a small fixed set of types; users cannot manually implement them (sealed). (6) **Stdlib migration — convert existing markers to `marker trait`.** Touch the source declarations of `Eq`, `Pod`, `ScopeLocal`, `Sealed`, future `Concurrent`. The migration is mechanical: change `trait Name { }` to `marker trait Name;` (or `marker trait Name: Supertrait;`). All existing impl blocks (which are already empty by construction) require no changes. Verify the migration in stdlib tests. (7) **Diagnostics on misuse.** `marker trait Foo { fn method(); }` rejected at parse with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD`; `marker trait Foo { type Item; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `impl Pod for u8 { fn extra() { } }` rejected with `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD` after the impl's target trait `Pod` resolves to a marker. (8) **Formatter.** Round-trips `marker trait Foo;` and `marker trait Foo { }` to canonical form (`marker trait Foo;` is the canonical short shape; `{ }` form is preserved if the user wrote it explicitly). (9) **Test coverage.** Positive — `marker trait Pod;` parses and registers; `marker trait Concurrent: Sized;` parses with supertrait; `marker trait Sealed[T];` parses with generics; `marker trait Storeable[T: Clone] where T: Default;` parses with where-clause; `impl Pod for u8 { }` accepted; `impl[T: Clone] Storeable[T] for Box[T] { }` accepted (conditional impl); generic bound `fn f[T: Pod](x: T) { }` accepts; impl-of-marker-trait coherence rejects duplicate impls; orphan rule applies (impl of foreign marker for foreign type rejected). Negative — `marker trait Foo { fn bar(); }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD` and both fix-its; `marker trait Foo { type Item; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `marker trait Foo { const N: usize; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `impl Pod for u8 { fn x() { } }` rejected with `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD`; user-side `impl ScopeLocal for MyType { }` rejected (sealed marker — separate diagnostic). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) — lexer + parser + AST + resolver + typechecker + formatter; stdlib migration is a coordinated CR with the language work landing first. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 55 ships the full surface at v1; user-extensible auto-marker derivation is permanently rejected per item 61.

- [ ] **Raw-pointer method dispatch requires known pointee — `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE`.** Spec at `design.md § Method Resolution > Method dispatch on raw pointers requires a known pointee` (v60 item 54). Slices: (1) **Typechecker check at method dispatch.** When method resolution evaluates `expr.method(args)` and `expr` has type `*const T` or `*mut T`, check whether `T` contains an unresolved type metavariable. If yes, emit `error[E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE]: method '<name>' on raw pointer requires a known pointee type` with the pointer expression's span underlined and the two fix-it suggestions: (a) annotate the binding's declared type (`let p: *const u8 = ...`), (b) use turbofish on the originating constructor when identifiable (`ptr.null[u8]()`). If the originating constructor cannot be identified syntactically (e.g., the pointer flowed in through a function argument), only the binding-annotation fix-it is offered. (2) **Constructor identification helper.** Walk back from the pointer expression through the binding's initializer (one level — not a full DFA). If the initializer is a direct call to `ptr.null()` / `ptr.null_mut()` / `ptr.dangling()` / `ptr.dangling_mut()`, identify it as the originating constructor and offer the turbofish fix-it pointing at its call site. Otherwise fall through to the binding-annotation-only fix-it. (3) **`unsafe { }` orthogonality.** The check fires regardless of whether the call is inside an `unsafe { }` block — the diagnostic is about type-system tractability, not safety contract. Verify the existing `unsafe`-required check still fires on raw-pointer method calls separately; the two diagnostics are independent and can both fire on the same expression. (4) **Generic-parameter case.** When the pointer's element type is a generic parameter `T` in scope (not a metavariable), the check passes — `T` will be resolved at monomorphization, and the dispatch is checked against `T` symbolically. The distinction is between "type metavariable awaiting solving" and "generic type parameter" — the typechecker's existing infrastructure already distinguishes these. (5) **No autoref / auto-deref through raw pointers — verify.** Method-resolution Step 1 builds the receiver candidate list from `T`, `ref T`, `mut ref T`, plus `shared struct` / Rc / Arc deref steps. Raw pointers are NOT part of the chain — verify the existing implementation does not accidentally include them. A method declared on the pointee type `T` is not reachable via `p: *const T` without an explicit `*p` dereference; the call resolves only against inherent methods on `*const T` / `*mut T` themselves. (6) **Test coverage.** Positive — `let p: *const u8 = ptr.const(some_byte); unsafe { p.read(); }` accepts (T pinned by binding annotation); `let p = ptr.null[u32](); unsafe { p.read(); }` accepts (T pinned by turbofish); `fn f[T](p: *const T) { unsafe { p.read(); } }` accepts (T is a generic param, resolved at mono); pointer arithmetic `p.offset(4)` follows the same rule; `p.is_null()` accepts even with unresolved T (no read of the pointee, no T-dependent lowering). Negative — `let p = ptr.null(); unsafe { p.read(); }` rejected with `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE`, span on `p`, both fix-its offered (binding annotation + turbofish on `ptr.null`); `let p = ptr.dangling(); unsafe { p.write(0); }` rejected, both fix-its offered; pointer flowing through a function argument with no annotation rejected with binding-annotation fix-it only; pointer in a `Vec[*const _T]` whose element type is unsolved rejected at the `.read()` site. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; reuses the existing metavariable / generic-parameter distinction infrastructure. No P1 carve-out — the rule is a single typechecker check; the diagnostic + fix-it are the only new compiler emission.

- [x] **Trait method parameters require names — focused diagnostic for anonymous-parameter form.** Spec at `design.md § Trait method parameter names — required` (v60 item 53). The grammar already enforces this — `PARAM = IDENT ":" TYPE | PATTERN ":" TYPE` per syntax.md §3.1, no anonymous alternative — so the rule fires automatically as a generic parse error today. This entry's work is the **focused diagnostic upgrade**: when the parser sees a type token in parameter position with no preceding name, recognize the user intent and emit `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` (or `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` for free functions) with the type-only span underlined and the `_: i32` / `arg: i32` fix-it suggestion inline. Slices: (1) **Parser recognition.** In `parse_param` (or wherever parameters parse), detect the case where the token sequence starts with a type-class-looking IDENT not followed by `:` (or, more broadly, any token sequence that would form a valid TYPE in this position without a preceding name+colon). When this pattern matches, recover the type from the token stream as if a name had been provided, then emit the focused diagnostic naming the missing-name span and the type. (2) **Diagnostic shape.** `error[E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM]: trait method parameters require a name` (or `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` for free functions, which fall under the same rule but a slightly different help line — the trait diagnostic mentions "trait method", the free-fn one says "function"). Span underlines the offending type-only token range. Help line: `write '_: <type>' for an unused parameter, or 'arg: <type>' for a meaningful name`. The `<type>` placeholder is filled with the recovered type so the fix-it is exactly applicable. (3) **Recovery — keep parsing.** After emitting the diagnostic, recover by treating the missing-name case as if `_` had been written; the parser produces a `_`-pattern parameter and continues. This lets the rest of the trait method (and the rest of the file) parse so the user sees every error in one pass rather than cascading parse failures. (4) **Distinguish from other parse errors.** When a parameter genuinely has malformed syntax (unbalanced parens, missing comma, etc.), the focused anonymous-param diagnostic must NOT fire — it should only fire on the specific shape "valid type in parameter position, no preceding name+colon, would parse as a type if positioned in a return-type slot." The detection is: peek ahead, attempt a type parse; if it succeeds and consumes tokens up to a `,` or `)`, the user wrote a type-only parameter — emit `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`. Otherwise fall through to the generic parse-error path. (5) **Test coverage.** Positive — `trait V { fn visit(ref self, node: Node); }` parses; `trait V { fn visit(ref self, _: Node); }` parses; `trait V { fn visit(ref self, _: i32, _: i32); }` parses (multiple `_` in the same signature accepted); `fn free(_: i32) { }` parses (free-fn equivalent); `impl V for X { fn visit(ref self, n: Node) { ... } }` accepts the impl using a different parameter name than the trait declared (names are local). Negative — `trait V { fn visit(ref self, Node); }` rejected with `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`, span on `Node`, help line offering `_: Node` and `node: Node`; `fn free(i32) { 0 }` rejected with `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`; multiple anonymous params in one signature emit one diagnostic per occurrence. Phase target: Phase 2 (Parser & AST) — parser diagnostic upgrade. Verify the existing parser already produces *some* error on the type-only form (it should, via the generic "expected `:` after identifier" path); this entry replaces that with the focused diagnostic. No P1 carve-out — the change is parser-local; the grammar-level rule is already in place, only the diagnostic needs sharpening.

- [~] **`@` binding semantics — match-arm-mode propagation + composition checks.** Spec at `design.md § @ Bindings` (v60 item 52). Phase 2 parser already supports `@` bindings (`PatternKind::AtBinding` recognized in `parse_pattern`); this entry covers the typechecker semantics and composition rules. Slices 1–3, 5–8 verified or shipped (drive-by refutable-let fix: `let PAT = expr;` previously accepted refutable patterns silently — now rejects via `is_irrefutable_param_pattern`, which `AtBinding` inherits transparently from its inner pattern). 7 new parser tests + 5 new typechecker tests cover positive shapes, refutable-let rejection (including the `@`-bound-with-refutable-inner case), and per-form regression. Slice 4 (`E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME`) is the only remaining work — needs ownership-pass integration to detect overlapping consume claims between outer name and inner sub-patterns.

  1. [x] **Verify parser handles all positions.** `IDENT @ PATTERN` parses at top level (match arm), nested inside struct/tuple-variant patterns (`Response { status: code @ 500..=599, body }`), inside or-patterns (`x @ A | x @ B`), and inside `let` patterns (`let x @ Foo { a } = foo`). The existing parser already covers these; each case has a parser test.
  2. [x] **Typechecker — type assignment.** The `@` binding's `IDENT` takes the type of the scrutinee at its position in the pattern tree. For top-level `x @ pattern`, `x` has the scrutinee type; for nested `Response { status: code @ ... }`, `code` has the field type. Existing pattern-typechecking machinery handles this; the AtBinding arm in `infer_pattern` propagates the type correctly.
  3. [x] **Match-arm binding mode propagation.** Tie the `@` binding into the existing scrutinee-mode-propagation pass (`design.md § Match Arm Binding Modes`): owned scrutinee → `@` binding consumes; `ref T` scrutinee → `@` binding is `ref T`; `ref IDENT @ PATTERN` annotation → borrows even under owned scrutinee. The propagation pass already runs over all bindings; AtBinding nodes participate the same as regular IDENT bindings.
  4. [ ] **Cannot-double-consume rule (`E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME`).** When the scrutinee is owned and an `@` binding's outer IDENT would consume the value while a sub-pattern binding inside it would also consume the same field, reject with `error[E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME]: cannot bind both '<outer>' and '<inner>' as owned — '<outer>' would consume the whole value while '<inner>' would consume a field; use 'ref <outer>' to borrow, or omit one of the two bindings`. The check runs as part of the existing partial-move analysis on match arms — when the outer binding's claim is "consume whole" and an inner binding's claim is "consume sub-field", the conflict surfaces at the existing partial-move check site with an enriched diagnostic for the `@`-binding-specific case. **This is the only remaining slice.**
  5. [x] **Refutability for `let` patterns.** Drive-by fix: existing irrefutable-pattern check on `let` and `let ... else` now handles `@` bindings transparently — the `@` itself is irrefutable, so the inner pattern's refutability determines the whole pattern's refutability. `let x @ Some(y) = opt;` is rejected by the refutability check; `let x @ Foo { a } = foo;` is accepted.
  6. [x] **Or-pattern alignment.** `x @ Some(_) | x @ None` accepts (same name, same type); `x @ Some(_) | y @ None` rejects with the existing or-pattern "every alternation must introduce the same set of names" diagnostic enriched to mention the `@`-binding sites.
  7. [x] **`mut` rejection inside patterns.** `mut x @ pattern` rejected at parse with the existing "mut not valid inside patterns" diagnostic; suggested fix-it points at `let mut x = ...` rebind in the arm body.
  8. [x] **Nested `@` bindings.** `outer @ Foo { field: inner @ Bar(value) }` binds three names with correct types; the partial-move check fires at the right granularity if both `outer` and `inner` would consume an overlapping subtree.

  **Test coverage** (mirrored against the slices above). Positive — `match val { x @ Some(_) => ... }` binds `x: Option[T]`; `match val { Response { status: code @ 500..=599, body } => ... }` binds `code: i32` and `body: ...`; `match val: ref Foo { x @ Foo { field } => ... }` binds `x: ref Foo` and `field: ref FieldType` (via match-ergonomics); `ref x @ Some(y) => ...` over an owned scrutinee binds `x: ref Option[T]` without consuming; nested `outer @ Foo { field: inner @ Bar(v) }` binds three names; `x @ Some(_) | x @ None` accepts (same name + same type); `let x @ Foo { a } = foo` accepts (irrefutable); `n @ MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE` accepts with const-expression range bound (composition with item 51). Negative — `x @ Some(y)` with owned scrutinee where `y` would consume a field that `x` already owns rejected with `E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME` (slice 4); `let x @ Some(y) = opt` rejected with refutability diagnostic; `mut x @ pattern` rejected at parse; `x @ Some(_) | y @ None` rejected with or-pattern same-names diagnostic; `x @ Some(_) | x @ Some(true)` (different inner types in alternation reaching the same name) rejected.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; the parser already supports the form and the existing match-arm-binding-mode pass handles the propagation. No P1 carve-out — option uniform-with-existing-rules ships the full surface at v1.

- [~] **Half-open range patterns + const-expression bounds.** Spec at `design.md § Range Patterns` (v60 item 51). The five-form coverage and exhaustiveness rules are already specced; this entry covers verifying the parser/typechecker for half-open forms and adding the const-expression-bound extension. Slice 1 shipped with two real fixes — bounded-exclusive `lo..hi` was missing from integer/char range arms (parse path now disambiguates `lo..` vs `lo..hi` by peeking for a literal after `..`); and `match value_class_var { ..lit => ... }` previously misparsed as struct-update because `looks_like_struct_literal` matched `{ ..ident }` for any identifier (now gated on `starts_upper(name)`). Interpreter `try_match_pattern` for `RangePattern` was also a "simplified" stub returning true unconditionally; replaced with proper `value_in_range_pattern` handling all five forms via i128 keys. 4 parser + 1 typechecker + 3 interpreter tests. Slices 2–7 (const-expression bounds via `QUALIFIED_PATH`) remain — needs a new `RangeBound { Literal | Path }` AST split + const resolution in the typechecker.

  1. [x] **Verify parser already accepts all five forms.** The grammar in `syntax.md §5.6` covers `CONST_PAT_BOUND ".." CONST_PAT_BOUND`, `CONST_PAT_BOUND "..=" CONST_PAT_BOUND`, `CONST_PAT_BOUND ".."` (unbounded above), `".." CONST_PAT_BOUND` (exclusive end), `"..=" CONST_PAT_BOUND` (inclusive end). All five forms now recognized in `parse_pattern`; the bounded-exclusive and value-class-scrutinee fixes shipped here.
  2. [ ] **AST representation for range patterns.** `Pattern::Range { lo: Option<RangeBound>, hi: Option<RangeBound>, inclusive: bool, span: Span }` with `RangeBound { kind: Literal | Path, ... }`. The `Option`s capture the half-open variants (`None` for the missing bound).
  3. [ ] **Const-expression-bound resolution at typecheck.** When a range pattern's bound is a `QUALIFIED_PATH`, the typechecker resolves it via the existing module-level-const lookup machinery (the same one that powers const-eval for default parameter values, refinement-type bounds, and module-level-binding initializers). On resolution success, the const value is folded into the AST as a literal-equivalent for downstream exhaustiveness and bound-ordering checks. On resolution failure: emit `error[E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST]: range pattern bound '<path>' must resolve to a module-level integer or char const` with the specific failure mode (path not found / resolves to a non-const / wrong type / not at module scope).
  4. [ ] **Bound-ordering check after resolution.** Existing rule (`9..=0` rejected) applies after const-resolution — bounds named via `QUALIFIED_PATH` are compared by their resolved values, so `MAX..=MIN` (where MAX < MIN) is rejected with the same diagnostic the literal form produces.
  5. [ ] **Type-matching check after resolution.** Existing rule applies — both bounds must resolve to the same primitive type (integer width or `char`). Mixed-type bounds (one literal-typed `i32`, one path-resolved `i64`) rejected with the existing same-type diagnostic enriched to name both resolved types.
  6. [ ] **Exhaustiveness — no change beyond existing rule.** Range patterns count toward exhaustiveness only by their resolved-value span; the existing Maranget-style algorithm already operates on resolved literal values, so const-expression bounds slot in transparently after the resolution step.
  7. [ ] **No function-call expressions in pattern position (`E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE`).** Reject anything more complex than `LITERAL` or `QUALIFIED_PATH` in pattern position with `error[E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE]: range pattern bound must be a literal or a path to a module-level const; arbitrary expressions are not accepted at pattern position`. The check runs at parse — the grammar production limits the shape upfront.

  **Test coverage.** Positive — bounded `0..=9` accepts; bounded `'a'..='z'` accepts; half-open `..0`, `0..`, `..=0`, `0..=10` all parse and match (slice 1 ✓); const-bound `match age { MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE => ... }` resolves and matches (slice 3); const-bound + or-pattern `0..=9 | TEEN_MIN..=TEEN_MAX => ...`; const-bound + `@` binding `n @ MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE => ...` (composition with item 52); mixed literal + const `0..=MAX_AGE` resolves correctly. Negative — `MAX..=MIN` (where MAX < MIN as resolved values) rejected with bound-ordering diagnostic (slice 4); mixed-type `0i32..=MAX_I64` (where MAX_I64: i64) rejected with same-type diagnostic naming both resolved types (slice 5); non-const path `match age { local_var..=10 => ... }` rejected with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST` (slice 3); arbitrary expression `match age { (10 + 5)..=20 => ... }` rejected at parse with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE` (slice 7); float bounds `match x { 1.0..=2.0 => ... }` rejected (existing rule); bare `..` as a pattern rejected with the existing "use `_`" diagnostic.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; reuses existing const-evaluation machinery for path resolution. No P1 carve-out — option (b) of v60 item 51 ships the const-expression-bound extension at v1; refinement and distinct-type range patterns (option c of the decision matrix) are intentionally not in v1 and are additive-later if a workload demands them.

- [ ] **Type alias bounds enforced at use sites.** Spec at `design.md § Type Aliases` (v60 item 50). Slices: (1) **Parser — already accepts bound forms.** The `GENERIC_PARAMS` rule in `syntax.md §3.12` shares grammar with struct/fn declarations, so `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]` already parses. AST: ensure `Item::TypeAlias { generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>, ... }` records the bounds; verify the existing AST representation captures them (it should, since the same `GenericParam` shape is used elsewhere). (2) **Typechecker — bound substitution and check at use sites.** The existing alias-expansion machinery already substitutes the alias's body when a use site is type-checked. Extend the substitution to walk the alias's generic-parameter bounds in the same pass: for each `GenericParam { name, bounds }`, after binding `name` to the use-site's concrete argument, check each bound against the bound argument via the existing trait-resolution machinery (the same code path that handles `fn foo[T: Ord]` use-site bound checks). On failure, emit `error[E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED]: '<arg>' does not satisfy '<bound>' required by alias '<alias_name>'` with the use-site span as the primary, the alias declaration's span as the note, and the standard "type does not implement trait" help line. (3) **Redundant-bound lint.** When the typechecker resolves the alias body and discovers that a declared bound is already implied by the underlying type's existing bounds (e.g., `type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` — TreeMap already requires K: Ord), emit `warning[redundant_alias_bound]: bound '<bound>' on alias '<alias_name>' is implied by the underlying type '<body>'; consider removing` with a fix-it removing the bound. The lint is suppressible via `#[allow(redundant_alias_bound)]` on the alias declaration. (4) **Composition with refinement `where`.** The existing refinement-predicate check at `where REFINEMENT_PRED` is value-level and orthogonal; the new bound check is type-level. Both run at independent times: bound check at use-site type-resolution, refinement at construction. No interaction beyond co-existence on the same alias declaration. (5) **Cross-package surface.** `pub type` alias bounds are part of the API contract — verify the exporter pass records the bounds in the package's interface descriptor so downstream consumers see them; weakening a bound is non-breaking, tightening is breaking (same rule as `pub fn` signatures). (6) **TAIT interaction.** Bounds on a type-alias-`impl Trait` declaration (`type IterOf[T: Display] = impl Iterator[Item = T]`) are checked at every use-site of `IterOf[U]` against `U`; the check is independent of the witness-inference machinery (which is P1). The v1 stub for TAIT (per item 41) already produces the `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` diagnostic at witness-dependent use sites; bounds on the alias's generic parameters fire the bound check first, then the TAIT stub if the bound passes. (7) **Test coverage.** Positive — `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]; let x: Index[String] = HashMap.new();` accepts `String` (satisfies `Eq + Hash`); `type SortedVec[T: Ord] = Vec[T]; let v: SortedVec[i32] = Vec.new();` accepts `i32` (satisfies `Ord`); generic alias with multi-bound `type Cache[K: Eq + Hash, V: Clone] = Map[K, V]; let c: Cache[String, Vec[i32]] = Map.new();` accepts when both bounds hold; aliases without bounds (`type UserId = i64`, `type Callback = Fn(Event) -> Result[(), Error] with _`) continue to work unchanged; bound-on-alias composition with refinement (`type SortedNonEmpty[T: Ord] = Vec[T] where self.len() > 0`) parses, and use-site `SortedNonEmpty.try_from(some_vec)` runs both the bound check (compile-time) and the refinement (run-time). Negative — `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]; let x: Index[Vec[i32]] = HashMap.new();` rejected at the use site with `E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` naming `Vec[i32]` and the missing `Hash` bound; redundant `type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` emits `warning[redundant_alias_bound]` (suppressible); cross-package — exporter declares `pub type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]`, downstream consumer's use site fails the bound check with the alias-declaration span surfaced in the diagnostic note. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; reuses existing trait-resolution machinery for bound checking. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 50 ships the full surface at v1; the spec is a single typechecker rule, not a multi-phase rollout.

- [~] **Saturating float→int + every-`as`-cast-pair fully defined.** Spec at `design.md § Numeric Semantics > as-cast semantics` (v60 item 49). Two halves: typechecker cast-pair rules (which pairs are accepted/rejected and with which fix-its) and codegen lowering (saturating LLVM intrinsics + four method families on `f32`/`f64`). Slice 1 shipped — bool→int and char→{i32,u32,wider} now accepted; the four rejection diagnostics fire as specced. Slices 2 (stdlib method families) and 4 (codegen lowering) remain; slices 5–9 are existing-behavior verifications.

  1. [x] **Typechecker — cast-pair rejection rules.** Four new error codes for the rejected forms specced in design.md: `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` (rejected at `char as u8/u16/i8/i16` — fix-it suggests `c as u32 as uN` for explicit truncation OR `c.encode_utf8(buf)` for proper UTF-8 encoding), `E_INT_AS_CHAR` (rejected at `iN/uN as char` — fix-it suggests `char.try_from(n)`), `E_INT_AS_BOOL` (rejected at `iN/uN as bool` — fix-it suggests `n != 0`), `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL` (rejected at `f32/f64 as bool` — meaningless). Each rejection runs at the typechecker's cast-resolution step; the existing redundant-cast lint (`bool as bool` etc.) is preserved.
  2. [ ] **Stdlib — float→int method families.** `f.saturating_to_iN()` / `f.wrapping_to_iN()` / `f.checked_to_iN() -> Option[iN]` / `f.trunc_to_iN()` on every `f32` / `f64` × every signed (`i8`..`i128`) and unsigned (`u8`..`u128`, `usize`, `isize`) target type. Plus the symmetric `i.to_f32()` / `i.to_f64()` for all integer types (the implicit-widening cases work without `as` already; method versions ship for code-style consistency). The four-method family parallels the existing integer arithmetic `checked_*`/`wrapping_*`/`saturating_*`/`overflowing_*` family at the spec level. Methods register in the typechecker's primitive-method table; effect-free except `trunc_to_iN()` which carries `panics` (the trapping-on-out-of-range form).
  3. [x] **`AllocError`-style not-needed.** Out-of-range float→int conversions saturate at the `as` site, so no error type is required for the default form. The `checked_to_iN()` method returns `Option[iN]` (using the existing `Option` type) for users who want the explicit-failure form; no new error type. Decision recorded; no implementation work.
  4. [ ] **Codegen — Phase 7 lowering.** `f as iN` lowers to LLVM `fptosi.sat` (signed target) or `fptoui.sat` (unsigned target) — single instruction per call, available since LLVM 12 on every supported target. `f.saturating_to_iN()` lowers to the same intrinsic — alias-method optimization folds the call to the same IR. `f.wrapping_to_iN()` lowers to `fptosi`/`fptoui` (the un-saturated raw instructions); on targets where the raw instruction's modular-overflow semantics deviate from the documented Kāra rule (currently only some legacy ARM cores per LLVM's documentation), emit a software polyfill that performs the conversion via integer-bit-manipulation to ensure target-independent semantics. `f.checked_to_iN()` emits a pre-check (`fcmp` against the integer's representable range, plus `fcmp uno` for NaN detection) and selects `None` or `Some(saturating-cast-result)` via a `phi` node. `f.trunc_to_iN()` emits the same pre-check and panics on out-of-range or NaN; the panic carries `#[track_caller]` and produces a "float-to-int out of range" message in the panic record.
  5. [ ] **Int→int casts** (existing — verify spec compliance). Bitwise truncation of low M bits on narrowing; sign-extend on signed-source widening (already implicit, not via `as`); zero-extend on unsigned-source widening. Verify codegen emits `trunc` / `sext` / `zext` LLVM instructions matching the documented behavior.
  6. [ ] **Int→float casts** (existing — verify). IEEE 754 round-to-nearest-even via `sitofp` / `uitofp`; integer source > 2^53 may round; never panic.
  7. [ ] **Float→float casts** (existing — verify). Widening is implicit (no `as` required); narrowing via `as` uses `fptrunc` (round-to-nearest-even); overflow produces `±Infinity` per IEEE 754.
  8. [x] **Bool→int casts.** `false as iN/uN` produces `0`; `true as iN/uN` produces `1`. Codegen emits `zext` from `i1` (the LLVM bool type). Accepted as of slice 1.
  9. [x] **Char→int casts (wide targets).** `char as u32` and `char as i32` produce the Unicode scalar value (range `0..=0x10FFFF`, fits in 21 bits); codegen emits `zext` from the `i32`-internal char representation. Wide-target casts accepted as of slice 1; narrow-target casts (`char as u8/u16/i8/i16`) rejected via `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` (slice 1).

  **Test coverage.** Positive — `f64.NAN as i32 == 0`; `f64.INFINITY as i32 == i32.MAX`; `f64.NEG_INFINITY as i32 == i32.MIN`; `1e30f64 as i32 == i32.MAX`; `(-1e30f64) as i32 == i32.MIN`; `1e30f64 as u8 == 255`; `(-1.0f64) as u8 == 0`; `3.7f64 as i32 == 3`; `(-3.7f64) as i32 == -3`; `(2_i64.pow(60)) as f64` rounds to nearest; `i64.MAX as f64` rounds upward past i64.MAX; `0x1FFi32 as u8 == 0xFFu8`; `(-1i32) as u8 == 0xFFu8`; `300i32 as i8 == 44i8`; `(-1i8) as u8 == 255`; `'A' as u32 == 65`; `'A' as i32 == 65`; `false as u8 == 0`; `true as u8 == 1`; `f.saturating_to_i32() == f as i32`; `f.NaN.checked_to_i32() == None`; `1e30f64.checked_to_i32() == None`; `1.5f64.checked_to_i32() == Some(1)`. Negative — `'A' as u8` rejected with `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` and the two fix-its; `'A' as i16` rejected; `65u8 as char` rejected with `E_INT_AS_CHAR` and the `char.try_from` fix-it; `1i32 as bool` rejected with `E_INT_AS_BOOL` and the `n != 0` fix-it; `1.0f64 as bool` rejected with `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL`; `f.NaN.trunc_to_i32()` panics with the "float-to-int out of range" message and a `#[track_caller]` source location at the call site, not inside the stdlib.

  **Phase target:** Phase 5.2 (typechecker rejection rules + new error codes — slice 1 shipped); Phase 7 (codegen `fptosi.sat` / `fptoui.sat` lowering + the four method families — slices 2/4). No P1 carve-out — v60 item 49 ships the full saturating + every-pair-defined surface at v1; the additional method families on `f32` / `f64` parallel existing integer method-family ergonomics and require no new infrastructure beyond the codegen step.

- [ ] **Fallible-allocation API split — `try_*` companions on every alloc-bearing method + `panic_on_alloc_failure` profile flag.** Spec at `design.md § Fallible Allocation API and OOM Handling` (v60 item 46). Full v1 implementation. Two parallel surfaces: (a) the `try_*` companion methods on every alloc-bearing stdlib type, available always; (b) a profile flag that, when `false`, rejects every panicking-alloc call site at typecheck. Hard mode for embedded/kernel-adjacent profiles; opt-in elsewhere.

  1. [ ] **`AllocError` prelude type.** Register two-variant enum `enum AllocError { OutOfMemory { requested_bytes: usize }, CapacityOverflow }` in the typechecker prelude (parallel to `IoError`, `VarError`, `AlreadySetError`). Implements `Debug`, `Display`, `Eq`, `Copy`. Available everywhere without import; `Result[(), AllocError]` and `Result[T, AllocError]` need no qualification.
  2. [ ] **`try_*` companion methods on every alloc-bearing collection type.** `Vec`: `try_with_capacity`, `try_push`, `try_insert`, `try_extend`, `try_reserve`, `try_reserve_exact`, `try_append`, `try_resize`, `try_clone`, `try_from_iter`. `String`: `try_push`, `try_push_str`, `try_with_capacity`, `try_reserve`, `try_clone`. `Map`/`Set`/`VecDeque`/`SortedSet`: `try_with_capacity` (where applicable), `try_insert`, `try_reserve`, `try_clone`. `Box`/`Rc`/`Arc`: `try_new`. Interpreter implementation reuses the existing alloc paths and wraps with `Result`-on-null at the host-allocator layer (the interpreter rarely actually OOMs; tests can inject failure via a `with_provider`-style allocator hook scheduled with the codegen runtime work below). Typechecker dispatch added to each per-collection `infer_*_method` function. Methods carry the same `allocates(Heap)` effect as their panicking counterparts; the only signature difference is the return type.
  3. [ ] **Profile flag — `panic_on_alloc_failure`.** New field in `[profile]` table parsed by `src/manifest.rs`; `bool`, default `true`. Threaded through `Pipeline.profile` to the typechecker like the existing per-profile knobs (`bounds_checks`, etc.). The flag is rejected (parse error) on profiles that already forbid heap entirely (`embedded`, `kernel`, `isr` — i.e., profiles whose `no_effects` contains `allocates(Heap)`); the diagnostic explains that the flag is moot when heap is forbidden.
  4. [ ] **Panicking-allocator rejection check (`E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED`).** Typechecker pass under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` walks every call site, operator site, and collection-literal site against a hardcoded **panicking-alloc registry**: every entry of the table in design.md (Vec.push / Vec.with_capacity / String.push / Box.new / etc.) plus the lowering primitives behind `+= on String`, `f"..."` interpolation, `[1, 2, 3]` Vec-literal, `{ k: v }` Map-literal, `Vec.collect`, `Clone.clone` synthesized bodies. Each rejection emits `error[E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED]: 'Vec.push' may panic on allocation failure; use 'Vec.try_push' instead under panic_on_alloc_failure = false` with the type-swap fix-it inline. The registry is constructed at typechecker init time and keyed by fully-qualified method/operator/lowering name.
  5. [ ] **`#[derive(Clone)]` rejection under fallible-alloc (`E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`).** When `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, the derive validator walks each derived `clone` body's call sites; if any reach a panicking allocator (anything in the registry), reject with `error[E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES]: '#[derive(Clone)]' on type 'T' generates a 'clone' that may panic on allocation failure (field 'name' of type 'F' allocates); write a manual 'try_clone' method instead, or suppress with '#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]' if you accept the panic`. Pure-`Copy` types and types whose fields all impl `Clone` infallibly (primitives, refs, single-field newtypes around primitives) are unaffected.
  6. [ ] **Auto-RC fallback rejection (`E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE`).** The ownership pass already records `RcEntry` records at sites where the compiler would emit `Rc.new(...)` per Part 4. Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, the diagnostic kit converts each `RcEntry` into `error[E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE]: auto-RC fallback at this site emits 'Rc.new(...)' which may panic on allocation failure; restructure to remove the fallback or use 'Rc.try_new(...)?' with explicit '?'-propagation` with the standard restructuring menu (`shared struct`, lifetime adjustment, ownership reshape) inlined into the help line. The check piggybacks on the existing RC-fallback recording pass — no new dataflow is needed; the rejection is a profile-flag-gated diagnostic transformation at the cost-summary emission step.
  7. [ ] **`?`-propagation through `AllocError`.** `AllocError` participates in the standard `From`-chain; user code that calls `try_*` and uses `?` must include `AllocError` in the function's error type's `From` arm or use a top-level `Result[T, AllocError]` return type. No new mechanism — same rule as every other propagated error.
  8. [ ] **Codegen — runtime allocator wrappers.** Phase 7 work — runtime allocator wrapper exposes `kara_alloc_fallible` returning a non-null `*mut u8` on success and `null` on failure; the panicking variant is `kara_alloc_or_panic` which calls the fallible variant and panics on `null` via a `#[track_caller]` helper. Both are emitted into `karac-runtime`. Stdlib generic code is parameterized once and the two API entry points dispatch to the appropriate runtime symbol.
  9. [ ] **`#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` lint suppression.** Registered as a structured per-binding allow attribute (parallels existing `#[allow(rc_fallback)]`). User opts in to "I'm fine with the derived clone panicking on OOM here" at the type definition; the suppression is per-type, not project-wide.

  **Test coverage** (typechecker + interpreter + codegen, Phase 8 stdlib + Phase 7 runtime). Positive — under `panic_on_alloc_failure = true` (default), `Vec.push(42)` and `Vec.try_push(42)?` both type-check and run; `AllocError` is in the prelude scope without import; `try_with_capacity(usize.MAX)` returns `Err(AllocError.CapacityOverflow)`; `try_clone` available on every alloc-bearing collection. Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` — `Vec.try_push(42)?` accepted; `Vec.push(42)` rejected with `E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED` and the fix-it; `s += other` on String rejected; `let v: Vec[i64] = [1, 2, 3]` collection literal rejected; `f"hello {name}"` rejected; `Box.new(x)` rejected; `let v: Vec[i64] = (0..1024).collect()` rejected; `#[derive(Clone)] struct S { v: Vec[i64] }` rejected with `E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`; auto-RC fallback site rejected with `E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE`; same struct under `#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` accepted with the lint suppression visible in `karac query lint-suppressions`. Profile-flag interaction — `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` on the `embedded` profile (which forbids heap) rejected at manifest parse with the moot-flag diagnostic.

  **Phase target:** Phase 8 (stdlib types + diagnostics + manifest flag); Phase 7 (runtime allocator wrapper). No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 46 ships the full surface at v1; the optional future `#[derive(TryClone)]` companion derive (a sibling that produces fallible `try_clone`) is non-breaking-additive and is not on the v1 critical path.

- [ ] **`panic = "unwind" | "abort"` profile flag + per-profile defaults + abort-mode codegen.** Spec at `design.md § Panic Strategy: panic = "unwind" | "abort"` (v60 item 47). The narrative spec already exists across 6+ scattered references in design.md; this entry consolidates the implementation work behind the new dedicated section. Slices: (1) **Manifest parsing.** `src/manifest.rs` recognizes `panic = "unwind" | "abort"` in `[profile]` blocks. Default value is profile-dependent: `app`/`lib` → `unwind`; `embedded`/`kernel`/`isr`/`gpu` → `abort`. Custom profiles default to `unwind` unless explicitly set. Unknown values produce `error[E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY]` naming the valid set. The setting is threaded through `Pipeline.profile` to the typechecker, effect checker, and codegen. (2) **Panic-strategy threading at compilation entry.** `Compilation.panic_strategy: PanicStrategy { Unwind, Abort }` field populated at pipeline init from the active profile. Available to every downstream phase via the existing `Pipeline` reference. (3) **Library-vs-binary advisory check.** When linking a library whose declared `panic` differs from the leaf binary's setting, emit `warning[W_PANIC_STRATEGY_MISMATCH]: package 'foo' declares panic = "...", this build uses panic = "..."` with the library's name and both settings. The library is recompiled under the binary's setting; the warning is informational. Detection happens at the build-system layer (`cmd_build_project`), not at the typechecker — it requires multi-package context. (4) **`catch_panic` rejection under abort** — already specced at `design.md § Catching Panics`; the typechecker check that gates `catch_panic` calls reads `Compilation.panic_strategy` and rejects with `E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND` under `Abort`. (5) **`extern "C-unwind"` rejection under abort** — already specced at `design.md § FFI`; both declarations and calls are rejected at parse with `E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE` under `Abort`. (6) **Effect-checker pass — drop-body panic-freedom enforcement** is unchanged (`Drop` body must be `panics`-free regardless of strategy; the existing rule already covers this). (7) **Custom panic handler attribute.** `#[panic_handler]` on a free function is recognized when `panic_handler = "custom"` is set in the active profile. The handler signature is fixed: `fn(info: ref PanicInfo) -> ()` (or `Never`).
