The handler must itself be `panics`-free (effect checker rejects otherwise — same rule as `Drop`); under abort, it's the only user code that runs between panic site and termination. Multiple `#[panic_handler]` declarations across the project's source tree produce `error[E_DUPLICATE_PANIC_HANDLER]` naming all spans. Zero declarations + `panic_handler = "custom"` set produces `error[E_MISSING_PANIC_HANDLER]` with a fix-it skeleton. (8) **Default panic handler** — when `panic_handler` is unset (the default), the runtime supplies a built-in handler. Under `unwind`, it walks the stack via the unwinder and writes the JSON crash report per `design.md § Crash Report Format`. Under `abort`, it emits a single-`write(2)` line containing panic site, panic kind, and panic message to stderr, then calls `__kara_abort()`. Both are provided by `karac-runtime`. (9) **Codegen — Phase 7.** Under `Compilation.panic_strategy = Unwind`, the existing LLVM `invoke` + personality + landingpad lowering applies (already part of the catch_panic / drop / RC-fallback / extern-C-unwind work). Under `Compilation.panic_strategy = Abort`, switch to plain `call` instructions and skip personality function attachment, skip cleanup landingpad emission, skip DWARF unwind-table emission (`.eh_frame`, `.gcc_except_table`). Panic-emitting primitives (`unwrap`, `expect`, index-OOB, divide-by-zero, explicit `panic()`) compile to `call __kara_panic_handler(info)` followed by `call __kara_abort()` (the latter marked `noreturn` so LLVM dead-code-eliminates everything past the panic site). RC decrements at scope exit are still emitted under abort (they happen on normal exit paths); the difference is they are not reached on panic paths because there is no unwind. (10) **Build-system — link-time panic-strategy check.** When the build links a binary, verify all participating object files were compiled under the same `panic_strategy`; emit `error[E_PANIC_STRATEGY_LINK_MISMATCH]` if mismatched. This is a defensive check — the per-binary-recompile rule should make mismatches impossible at v1, but the check guards against future ABI-stable library distribution. (11) **Manifest-flag interaction with `no_effects = ["panics"]`** — when the active profile already forbids the panics effect, the `panic` setting still applies to runtime-internal panics (allocator failures from non-fallible code, double-panic on the abort path). Setting `panic = "unwind"` on a `no_effects = ["panics"]` profile is legal but unusual; emit a hint pointing out that user code cannot generate panics so the unwind tables are mostly dead weight. (12) **Composition with `panic_on_alloc_failure`.** The two flags are orthogonal; the typechecker pass for OOM rejection runs independently of the panic strategy. A profile setting both `panic = "abort"` and `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` is the canonical fault-tolerant-system shape. **Test coverage** (typechecker + manifest + codegen, Phase 7 + Phase 8): positive — `panic = "abort"` parsed in `[profile]`; `panic = "unwind"` parsed; default for `app` profile is `unwind`; default for `embedded` is `abort`; default for `kernel` is `abort`; custom profile defaults to `unwind`; `[profile] name = "small_server" panic = "abort"` parses and applies; panic strategy threaded to typechecker; `#[panic_handler]` recognized; LLVM IR under unwind contains `invoke` + personality + landingpads; LLVM IR under abort contains plain `call` + no personality + no `.eh_frame`. Negative — `panic = "fast"` rejected with `E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY`; `catch_panic` under abort rejected with `E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND` (existing test, verified still passes); `extern "C-unwind"` under abort rejected with `E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE` (existing test, verified); two `#[panic_handler]` decls rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_PANIC_HANDLER`; missing handler with `panic_handler = "custom"` rejected with `E_MISSING_PANIC_HANDLER` and the fix-it; `#[panic_handler]` body that calls a `panics`-effect function rejected with the existing `panics`-in-handler diagnostic; library declaring `panic = "abort"` linked into `unwind` binary emits `W_PANIC_STRATEGY_MISMATCH` warning. Phase target: Phase 7 (codegen split — invoke vs call, personality, landingpads, DWARF emission); Phase 8 (manifest parsing, profile defaults, threading, advisory warnings, `#[panic_handler]` attribute). No P1 carve-out — option (X) of v60 item 47 ships the full surface at v1; the cleanup-contract semantics under abort match Rust precedent and don't require a Kāra-specific cleanup-walk path.

- [ ] **`OnceLock[T]` and `OnceCell[T]` lazy-init primitives.** Spec at `design.md § Module-Level Bindings > LazyLock[T] / OnceLock[T] / OnceCell[T]` (v60 item 45). Ship alongside the existing `LazyLock[T]` (already specced; unchanged by this entry). Both new primitives carry the same method surface — `new`, `set(val) -> Result[(), AlreadySetError[T]]`, `get() -> Option[ref T]`, `get_or_init(\|\| ...) -> ref T`, `is_set() -> bool` — so a type swap between the two is mechanical. The structural difference is single-task vs. cross-task safety, enforced through three explicit rules on `OnceCell[T]` rather than a `Sync` auto-trait. Slices: (1) **Stdlib types.** `OnceLock[T]` and `OnceCell[T]` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `stub_generics(["T"])` in `prelude.rs` and as generic structs in `register_builtin_types`. `OnceLock.new()` and `OnceCell.new()` wired into the path-call dispatch (parallel to the existing `LazyLock.new` recognition). (2) **Interpreter values.** `Value::OnceLock(Arc<Mutex<Option<Value>>>)` and `Value::OnceCell(Rc<RefCell<Option<Value>>>)` — the difference is `Arc<Mutex<...>>` vs. `Rc<RefCell<...>>` to mirror the cross-task vs. single-task split (Rust-host implementation; the language-level guarantee is the structural-rule check, the interpreter implementation just needs to be racy-safe enough not to panic on the cross-task path). (3) **Method surface implementation.** `set` returns `Ok(())` on first call, `Err(AlreadySetError { rejected: val })` on subsequent calls; `get` returns the cached value via `Option`; `get_or_init` wraps both into a single race-safe call (for `OnceLock`, the lock is acquired once; if another task's `set` races, the loser's constructed value is dropped without invoking the closure twice). (4) **Typechecker dispatch.** `infer_once_lock_method` and `infer_once_cell_method` added; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "OnceLock" \| "OnceCell" }`. Methods carry no effects beyond the invocation closure's effects (which propagate through `get_or_init`'s closure type per existing trait-method effect-checking rules). (5) **`AlreadySetError[T]`** registered as a prelude error type in the typechecker (`enum AlreadySetError[T] { rejected: T }`). Conditional `Display` impl gated on `T: Display` follows the existing conditional-impl pattern. Always implements `Debug`. (6) **`OnceLock` constant-init recognition.** `OnceLock.new()` is added to the compiler-recognized constant-init special forms alongside `LazyLock.new` so it's permitted as a module-level binding's right-hand side without violating the constant-initializer rule (the ctor produces a fresh empty cell with no captured runtime state — the same property `LazyLock.new` already has). (7) **Single-task structural enforcement** (three new diagnostics targeting `OnceCell[T]` use sites): (a) **`E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE`** — typechecker check at module-level binding registration: if the declared type contains `OnceCell[T]` anywhere in its tree, reject with `error[E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE]: 'OnceCell[T]' is single-task; module-level bindings are visible to every task and must be 'OnceLock[T]' instead` and a fix-it suggesting the type swap. (b) **`E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE`** — typechecker check at `par struct` / `par enum` field type validation (the existing pass that already rejects single-task types in `par struct` fields gains `OnceCell[T]` to its rejected-type set): `error[E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE]: 'OnceCell[T]' is single-task; fields of 'par struct'/'par enum' must be 'OnceLock[T]' instead` with the offending field's span and the type-swap fix-it. `shared struct` fields accept `OnceCell[T]` (per design.md — `shared struct` itself is single-task). (c) **`E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY`** — par-region escape analysis: when an owned binding of type `OnceCell[T]` is consumed by a `par {}` branch, a `spawn()` argument, or a `Sender[OnceCell[T]].send` call, reject with `error[E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY]: 'OnceCell[T]' cannot cross task boundaries; replace with 'OnceLock[T]' or move the surrounding owned struct's task-local clone into the branch instead`. The check piggybacks on the existing par-region escape pass that already rejects raw `Rc[T]` from crossing into a `par {}` branch — no new dataflow pass is needed; the check adds `OnceCell` to the existing rejected-type set keyed off the type-name. (8) **Effect attribution.** First-access initialization (whether through `set` or `get_or_init`) is attributed to the *calling* function, not to the binding — same rule that already applies to `LazyLock`. The closure passed to `get_or_init` has its own effect set checked at the call site against the calling function's ceiling (existing trait-method effect-check machinery). (9) **Codegen.** Phase 7 work — both primitives lower to small heap-allocated structs (the `Once` synchronization primitive already exists in `karac-runtime` for `LazyLock`'s use; `OnceLock` reuses it; `OnceCell` is just an `Option<T>` with interior mutability). The existing `karac-runtime` `Once` API gains `set`/`get`/`get_or_init` entry points. **Test coverage** (interpreter + typechecker, Phase 8): positive — `let CFG: OnceLock[Config] = OnceLock.new();` accepted at module scope; `CFG.set(Config { ... })` returns `Ok(())` on first call; `CFG.get()` returns `Some` after `set`, `None` before; `CFG.set(other)` after first set returns `Err(AlreadySetError { rejected: other })`; `CFG.get_or_init(\|\| compute())` runs closure exactly once across multiple calls; `OnceCell[Vec[Token]]` field on a non-`par` struct accepted; `parser.tokens()` lazy-init pattern type-checks and runs end-to-end; struct containing `OnceCell` may be moved into a non-`par` block. Negative — `let X: OnceCell[i64] = OnceCell.new();` at module scope rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE` and fix-it; `par struct Foo { cell: OnceCell[i64] }` rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE`; `par { let cell = OnceCell.new(); cell.set(1).unwrap(); }` accepted (cell is born inside the branch, doesn't cross); `let cell = OnceCell.new(); par { cell.set(1).unwrap(); }` rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY`; `Channel[OnceCell[i64]]` declared then `tx.send(cell)` rejected at the send call site with the same error. Phase target: **Phase 8** (Standard Library — Floor) for stdlib types + interpreter + typechecker + structural-enforcement diagnostics; Phase 7 for codegen. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 45 ships the full surface at v1; `LazyCell[T]` (the embedded-init non-Sync sibling) is intentionally not in v1 and is non-breaking-additive if a workload demands it later.

- [x] **Map codegen gap closure.** Several `Map[K, V]` methods that the typechecker accepts were silently miscompiled: `compile_map_method` in `src/codegen.rs:4667` ended with `_ => Ok(i64_t.const_int(0, false).into())` at line 4945, returning constant `0` for `keys`/`values`/`entries`/`merge`/`get_or` — programs ran to "success" with corrupt output. `compile_index` only handled Array/Vec/Slice so `m[k]` was wrong on compiled binaries. `Map.clear()` didn't exist. `Display` for collections was filed at line 207 of this file as a stub. Spec at `design.md § Collection Core Methods > Map[K, V]` (line 1548) and `design.md § Iteration order is unspecified` (line 1588). All subtasks closed; Display split into its own canonical bullet at `phase-7-codegen.md § Phase 7.2` since recursive Display codegen is its own scope. Closed 2026-05-04. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Catch-all hardening** — replaced the silent fallback at `src/codegen.rs:4945` with `Err(format!("codegen: Map.{method} not yet implemented"))`. No existing test triggered the catch-all (full LLVM suite still green at 2495 tests); hardening is purely preventative against future drift between typechecker-accepted methods and codegen-implemented methods. Commit `4a3bc3e`.
  - [x] **2. `m[k]` index op (read)** — extended `compile_index` with an early dispatch (mirrors slice early-dispatch shape) keyed off `self.map_key_types.contains_key(name)` to a new `compile_map_index` helper. Helper loads the map handle, allocates key/val slots, calls `karac_map_get`, and branches on the i1: missing → `emit_panic("Map index: key not present")` + unreachable; found → load val and return. Limitation: only direct-identifier paths wired (same as slice early-dispatch). Returned value is a bit-copy of the bucket — matches existing `Map.get` behavior; proper `ref V` return is a uniform follow-up across `[]` and `Map.get`. Tests: `test_e2e_map_index_get_existing_i64`, `test_e2e_map_index_get_existing_string_key`, `test_e2e_map_index_panics_on_missing`. Commit `ca94b9f`.
  - [x] **3. `m[k] = v` index op (write)** — extended `compile_index_store` with an early dispatch to a new `compile_map_index_store` helper that lowers to `karac_map_insert_old` and discards the previous-value out-slot. Fresh-insert and overwrite are handled uniformly by the runtime call. Tests: `test_e2e_map_index_set_fresh_and_overwrite`, `test_e2e_map_index_set_string_key`. Commit `3f08a39`.
  - [x] **4. `Map.clear()`** — `karac_map_clear(map)` added to `runtime/src/map.rs` (zeroes status via `write_bytes`, resets `len` + `tombstones`; bucket capacity preserved per Rust `HashMap::clear` contract). Extern declared in `Codegen::new()`. `clear` arm added to `infer_map_method` (Unit return), `eval_method_call` on `Value::Map`, and `compile_map_method`. Tests: `test_e2e_map_clear`, `test_e2e_map_clear_string_key` (codegen), `test_map_clear` (interpreter). Commit `8806883`.
  - [x] **5. `keys()` / `values()` / `entries()` codegen** — new `compile_map_keys_values_entries` helper pre-allocates a buffer at `karac_map_len` capacity (one malloc, no growth), then drives the existing `karac_map_iter_*` loop writing each element to `buf[i]`. Returns the Vec struct `{data, len, cap=len}` directly; receiving binding's let-statement registers cleanup via existing `vec_elem_types` path. Tests: `test_e2e_map_keys_returns_vec`, `test_e2e_map_values_returns_vec`, `test_e2e_map_entries_returns_vec_of_tuples`, `test_e2e_map_keys_string_keys_len`, `test_e2e_map_keys_empty`. Surfaced separate pre-existing gap: `for s in vec_of_strings { s.len() }` returns 0 because for-loop bindings don't register String/Vec method dispatch — affects all Vec[String] iteration regardless of source. Tracked separately. Commit `b150d8c`.
  - [x] **6. `Display` for collections** — split into separate canonical bullet **Display for collections (recursive codegen)** in `phase-7-codegen.md § Phase 7.2`. Recursive Display codegen (per-type emitted Display fns, with Vec[Vec[T]] / Map[K, Vec[T]] / Tuple support) is substantial enough to warrant its own bullet rather than being subsumed under the gap-closure umbrella. The interpreter side (`src/interpreter.rs:206-307`) is already correct; the codegen side is the new bullet's scope. Closed-by-delegation 2026-05-04.
  - [x] **7. `Map[k: v, ...]` prefix-literal K/V inference** — turned out to need parser + codegen, not pure typechecker. Parser was rejecting `Map[k: v]` outright ("Expected RightBracket, found Colon"); the AST node `PrefixCollectionLiteral.items` is a `Vec<Expr>` that can't represent key-value pairs. Fix: when type_name is "Map" and first expr is followed by `:`, parser switches to key-value parsing and emits `ExprKind::MapLiteral` (same AST as the bare `["k": v]` form, so existing typechecker case applies unchanged). Codegen for MapLiteral was also missing — silent-0 catch-all at `compile_expr` line 2837 swallowed it. Added `compile_map_literal_stmt` (new + insert-loop) and a let-statement-level recognizer that dispatches both bare and prefix forms. Tests: `test_map_prefix_literal_string_keys` / `test_map_prefix_literal_int_keys` (interpreter); `test_e2e_map_prefix_literal_string_keys` / `test_e2e_map_prefix_literal_int_keys` / `test_e2e_map_bare_literal_with_annotation` (codegen). Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 13. Commit `1678d0a`.

  Phase target: Phase 8 (typechecker / interpreter / tests) + Phase 7 (codegen extern declaration, `compile_map_method` arms, `compile_index` Map dispatch, `karac_map_clear` runtime fn). No P1 carve-out — every sub-step is mechanical; the existing `karac_map_*` runtime supplies all the primitives needed except `karac_map_clear`.

- [x] **`Set[T]` LLVM codegen.** Lower `Set[T]` to `Map[T, ()]` at the codegen layer and reuse the `karac_map_*` C runtime — the canonical implementation strategy used by Rust's `HashSet<T>` (defined as a wrapper around `HashMap<T, ()>`) and equivalent in every mainstream stdlib. The existing runtime at `runtime/src/map.rs` already handles zero-size values correctly via `(key_size + val_size).max(1)` at line 71, so no new C code is required; `Set[T]` keeps its own type identity in the parser/typechecker/interpreter/effect-checker layers and the lowering happens entirely below LLVM IR. Spec at `design.md § Collection Core Methods > Set[T]` (line 1590). Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Codegen state** — `set_elem_types: HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>`, `set_elem_type_names: HashMap<String, String>`, and `set_elem_type_exprs: HashMap<String, TypeExpr>` added next to the Map side-tables in `Codegen`. New `extract_set_elem_type`, `extract_set_elem_name`, `set_inner_type_expr` helpers parallel `extract_map_kv_types` / `extract_map_key_name` / `map_kv_type_exprs`. Side-tables populated both at the let-statement type-annotation site and via `register_var_from_type_expr` (the latter already runs for for-loop bindings). Type lowering at `llvm_type_for_type_expr` already lowers `Set[T]` to opaque `ptr` so no change there.
  - [x] **2. `Set.new()` path-call dispatch** — `is_set_new_call` predicate + `compile_set_new_stmt` added next to the Map versions. Lowers to `karac_map_new(elem_size, 0, hash_fn, eq_fn)` — the runtime's `(key_size + val_size).max(1)` keeps the bucket allocation valid for `val_size = 0`. Hash/eq fns selected via `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` so compound element shapes (tuples, derived-Hash structs) compose. Cleanup is the existing `FreeMapHandle` action; `track_map_var` is reused.
  - [x] **3. `compile_set_method`** — new function parallel to `compile_map_method`. Implements `len` → `karac_map_len`; `is_empty` → `karac_map_len == 0`; `insert(v)` → `karac_map_insert_old(map, &v, &dummy, &dummy)` then XOR with `1` (returns `true` on fresh insert, matching Rust `HashSet::insert`); `contains(v)` → `karac_map_contains`; `remove(v)` → `karac_map_remove_old(map, &v, &dummy)` returning the existed bit; `clear()` → `karac_map_clear`. The dummy unit/out is a single shared `i8` alloca per function — `val_size = 0` in the runtime makes the actual store a no-op. Method dispatch wired in the method-call routing site at `compile_method_call` alongside Map.
  - [x] **4. `for x in s`** — `compile_for_set_var` mirrors `compile_for_map_var`, swapping the val out-slot for a single shared `i8` alloca and binding the element directly (no `(k, v)` destructuring). Dispatch wired in the for-loop routing site at `compile_for`.
  - [x] **5. `union` / `intersection` / `difference`** — three new arms in `compile_set_method` route through a shared `emit_set_op_iter` helper that walks `karac_map_iter_*` over the source, optionally probes a "filter set" via `karac_map_contains`, per-element-clones survivors via `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`, and inserts into a freshly-allocated destination handle. `union` calls the helper twice — unfiltered from `self`, filtered against `self` from `other` — so duplicate elements never get double-cloned (which would leak the second clone since `karac_map_insert` overwrites in-place without freeing the prior key bytes). `intersection` uses `ContainsIn(other)`; `difference` uses `NotContainsIn(other)`. Hash/eq/elem-size pulled from the receiver's `set_elem_type_exprs` entry so compound element types compose. Result-handle scope-cleanup integration: extended the let-binding fallback path to call `track_map_var` when the RHS is a fresh-handle-producing method call (`clone` / `union` / `intersection` / `difference`); previously only `Vec`/`String` got auto-tracking, so `let n = m.clone();` was silently leaking the cloned handle on macOS (Apple ASAN has no LeakSanitizer; Linux + LSAN would have caught it). Restricted to `MethodCall` RHS so move-via-Identifier (`let n = m;`) keeps the source's existing track as the unique cleanup owner — no double-free risk. 5 codegen E2E tests (`union_i64`, `intersection_i64`, `difference_i64`, `union_string`, `difference_independent_after_source_mutation`) + 1 ASAN test (`asan_set_union_string_independent_handles`) added.
  - [x] **6. E2E codegen tests** — 9 baseline tests in `tests/codegen.rs` (search `test_e2e_set_`): `i64_insert_contains`, `i64_insert_returns_bool` (false on duplicate, true on fresh), `i64_remove`, `i64_len_is_empty`, `i64_for_loop_sum` (iteration-order-independent sum), `string_insert_contains`, `string_remove`, `string_for_loop_count`, `clear`. Plus the 5 set-op tests landed with subtask 5. Compound-key coverage (`Set[(i32, i32)]`, `Set[(String, (i32, i32))]`) deferred — Hash machinery is shared with the Map suite which already exercises both compound-key recursion and cache reuse.
  - [x] **7. ASAN test** — `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs::asan_set_new_insert_scope_exit_free` verifies the `FreeMapHandle` cleanup fires on Set drop. `asan_set_string_scope_exit_free` covers `Set[String]` with static-buffer (cap = 0) string literals to verify the bucket-array free fires while the static String buffers are correctly left alone.
  - [x] **8. `Set[v1, v2, ...]` prefix-literal element type inference** — typechecker arm added in `infer_expr` for `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name: "Set", items }`. Element type is unified from items via `check_assignable`; empty `Set[]` falls to `Type::Error` for the element and recovers via the binding-site annotation per `design.md` line 1462. 4 typechecker tests: `test_set_prefix_literal_infers_i64`, `test_set_prefix_literal_infers_string`, `test_set_prefix_literal_mismatched_elements_rejected`, `test_set_prefix_literal_empty_with_annotation`. Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 12 — flip that checkbox when this lands too.

  Phase target: Phase 7 (codegen lowering + runtime-extern reuse) + Phase 8 (typechecker prefix-literal inference + test additions). No new runtime C code; no new effect rules (effects wired in the separate effect-checker bullet). No P1 carve-out — the lowering is entirely mechanical.

- [x] **Clone trait surface for collections — vertical implementation (typechecker + interpreter + codegen + runtime).** Spec at `design.md § Iteration` line 1692: *`Vec`, `Map`, `Set`, `VecDeque`, `TreeMap`, and `SortedSet` implement `Clone`*. Today **every layer is missing** — typechecker has no `clone` method registration on these types (the only `"clone"` arm is for `Sender`); interpreter's `eval_method_call` falls through to "method 'clone' not found on type" panic; codegen has zero `"clone"` method dispatch and zero per-type clone fn emission. Compiled and interpreted binaries calling `Vec.clone()` / `String.clone()` / `Map.clone()` / `Set.clone()` fail today; this is a present-day v1 surface bug, not a future enhancement.

  **Priority: P0** — covers v1 stdlib API surface methods that currently produce wrong behavior at every layer.

  **Consumers blocked on this** (cross-references; flip their checkboxes when the relevant subtask lands):
  - ~~`Set[T] LLVM codegen` subtask 5 (`union` / `intersection` / `difference`)~~ — landed 2026-05-04 on top of `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`; per-element cloning routes through `emit_set_op_iter`.
  - `Vec.filled[T: Clone]` per `design.md § 1488` — every fill slot is a per-element clone.
  - Future stdlib generics with `T: Clone` bounds (e.g., `Vec.dedup_by_key`, `Vec.split_off` on non-Copy element types).
  - `#[derive(Clone)]` on user structs whose fields are non-Copy — the synthesized body is field-wise per-type clone.

  **Subtasks (split by layer):**

  - [x] **1. Typechecker — `clone` method registration on collection types.** Per-collection method-inference functions register `clone(ref self) -> Self` against `Vec[T]`, `String`, `Map[K, V]`, `Set[T]`, `VecDeque[T]`, `SortedSet[T]`, `TreeMap[K, V]`. The existing `infer_map_method` (`src/typechecker.rs:8275`) gets a `"clone"` arm; `Vec`/`String`/`Set` need their own (today the `Sender.clone()` arm at line 8892 is the only one in the typechecker). The `T: Clone` bound on collection element types is enforced via the existing trait-bound checking — `Vec[T]: Clone where T: Clone`. Negative test: `Vec.clone()` on a `Vec[NonCloneStruct]` rejected with the bound-violation diagnostic.

  - [x] **2. Interpreter — `clone` dispatch on collection values.** Add a `"clone"` arm to `eval_method_call` (`src/interpreter.rs`) that matches each `Value::Vec` / `Value::String` / `Value::Map` / `Value::Set` / `Value::SortedSet` shape and produces a deep copy via Rust-side `Vec::clone` / `String::clone` / etc. The Rust-side clones are correct by construction (each `Value` variant is itself `Clone`); this is purely dispatch wiring.

  - [x] **3. Codegen — per-type clone fn emission machinery (`emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`).** TypeExpr-aware emit fn paralleling `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr`. New `clone_fn_cache: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` keyed on `display_mangle_te(te)`. Function signature is uniform `void karac_clone_<typename>(*const T src, *mut T dst)` — caller provides both source and destination addresses, callee writes the cloned value into the destination slot. Cases:

    - **Primitive (Copy)** — `i8`/`i16`/`i32`/`i64`/`u8`/`u16`/`u32`/`u64`/`isize`/`usize`/`f32`/`f64`/`bool`/`char`/`unit` — single `load src` + `store dst`, no allocation.
    - **String** — call new runtime helper `karac_string_clone` (subtask 4 below). Receives a String struct `{data, len, cap}`; allocates `cap` bytes (or `len` if `cap == 0` for static literals — the cloned buffer needs `cap > 0` so its scope-exit cleanup fires), `memcpy`s `len` bytes, writes `{new_data, len, new_cap}` to `dst`.
    - **Vec[T]** — recursive: load `data`/`len`/`cap` from src; emit `karac_clone_<elem_mangled>` for `T` (via `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr(elem_te)`); `malloc(cap * elem_size)` for the new buffer; loop `i in 0..len` calling the elem clone fn with `src.data + i*elem_size` / `dst.data + i*elem_size`; write `{new_data, len, new_cap}` to `dst`. Empty Vecs (`cap == 0`) skip the malloc per the existing String-literal cap=0 convention.
    - **Map[K, V]** — emit `karac_map_new(key_size, val_size, hash_fn, eq_fn)` for the destination; iterate the source via `karac_map_iter_*`; for each pair, alloca'd K and V copies (clone via per-K, per-V emit_clone fns), then `karac_map_insert_old` into the destination. Hash/eq fn pointers come from `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` (already exist).
    - **Set[T]** — same as Map[T, ()] — single-element clone per iteration, val_size = 0 with shared dummy slot.
    - **Tuple `(T1, T2, ..., Tn)`** — typed entry `emit_clone_fn_for_tuple(elems)`; field-wise recurse into per-field clone fn via struct GEP. Mirror the tuple Hash/Eq/Display pattern.
    - **`#[derive(Clone)]` struct** — synthesized body is field-wise recurse. Emit at the derive-site by walking the struct's `field_types` and calling `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` per field, then GEP+store into `dst` per field. The derived `clone` method gets registered as the user struct's `Type.clone` so method-call dispatch finds it.

  - [x] **4. Runtime — `karac_string_clone(*const String) -> String` helper.** New extern in `runtime/src/string.rs` (or a dedicated `runtime/src/clone.rs`). Allocates a fresh buffer via the runtime's allocator (same path as `karac_vec_grow`), `memcpy`s `len` bytes from the source data pointer, returns the new `{ptr, len, cap}` struct. For static literals (`cap == 0`), allocates `len`-byte buffer with `cap = len` so the cloned String's scope-exit cleanup correctly frees it (the source's `cap = 0` keeps the static buffer untouched). Declared in `Codegen::new()` alongside the existing `karac_*` externs.

  - [x] **5. `compile_method_call` dispatch wiring.** Add `"clone"` arms to each per-collection method handler — `compile_vec_method`, `compile_map_method`, `compile_set_method`, plus a String-method handler if one exists separately. Each wires the source variable's slot through to the corresponding `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` and writes the result to a fresh stack alloca + side-table registration so the cloned value participates in scope cleanup correctly.

  - [x] **6. Scope-cleanup integration.** A cloned `Vec` / `Map` / `Set` / `String` is a fresh heap-owning value — register the appropriate `FreeVecBuffer` / `FreeMapHandle` cleanup action on its scope frame. Goes through the existing `track_vec_var` / `track_map_var` machinery; the only new piece is recognizing that `let w = v.clone()` produces a heap-owning bound name and calling the right tracker.

  - [x] **7. ASAN tests** in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`: `asan_vec_clone_independent_buffers` (verify the source's buffer is freed once and the cloned buffer is freed once — no aliasing); `asan_string_clone_static_literal` (source has `cap = 0`, clone has `cap > 0` and gets freed, source untouched); `asan_map_clone_independent_handle` (verify both maps free their bucket arrays separately, and any heap-bearing key/value bytes — String keys especially — clone correctly so neither map points at the other's strings); `asan_set_clone_string_elements` (per-element String clone integrity).

  - [x] **8. E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` + `tests/interpreter.rs`: `vec_clone_preserves_contents`, `vec_clone_grows_independently` (mutate source after clone, verify clone unchanged), `string_clone_independent_buffer`, `map_clone_preserves_entries` (single-key cases for deterministic output; multi-key behavior verified via the cardinality-equality / per-key lookup pattern that Map tests already use), `set_clone_preserves_membership`, `derive_clone_struct_with_vec_field` (whole-struct clone produces independent inner Vec).

  - [x] **9. Empty-collection clone fast path.** `Vec.new().clone()` doesn't need to allocate; same for the other empty collections. Either special-case `len == 0` in the emitted body (skip the malloc; produce a `cap = 0` placeholder) or rely on the runtime's `malloc(0)` defined-behavior path. The former is cleaner and saves an allocation per empty clone.

  Phase target: **Phase 8** for typechecker registration (subtask 1) + interpreter dispatch (subtask 2); **Phase 7** for codegen emission machinery (subtask 3) + runtime helper (subtask 4) + dispatch wiring (subtasks 5, 6) + tests (subtasks 7, 8). No P1 carve-out — `Clone` for collections is part of the v1 surface per design.md and producing wrong output today is a correctness bug, not a missing nice-to-have.

  **Out of scope for this bullet** (separate items): the fallible-allocation `try_clone` companion methods (covered by the existing `Fallible-allocation API split` bullet — they share the same emission machinery, only the return type differs); the `#[derive(Clone)]` rejection-when-allocates diagnostic under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` (also lives in the fallible-alloc bullet). Both consume the codegen infrastructure landed here but are tracked separately because their work is policy/diagnostic-side, not codegen-side.

- [x] **`Map.entry(k)` + `Entry[K, V]` enum — in-place insert-or-modify.** The idiomatic O(1) insert-or-modify pattern `self.table.entry(key).or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` avoids the double-hash that `if !m.contains_key { m.insert(...) }` produces. Without this, every word-count / group-by / counter-style program either double-hashes or threads an explicit `match m.get(...)` / `insert` pair through the call site. Spec at `design.md § Entry[K, V]` (around line 1565). Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Parser/AST verification** — confirmed: `m.entry(k)` parses as a `MethodCall` AST node with no new grammar, and the `.or_insert / .or_insert_with / .and_modify` chain composes through the standard method-call grammar. `tests/parser.rs::test_map_entry_chain_parses` covers the four canonical chain shapes.
  - [x] **2. `Entry[K, V]` enum prelude registration** — `Entry` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` (with `K, V` arity in `stub_generics`); `Occupied` / `Vacant` added to `PRELUDE_VARIANTS`. The full `EnumInfo` in `register_builtin_types` defines `Occupied { value: mut ref V }` / `Vacant { key: K, map: mut ref Map[K, V] }`. First stdlib type using `mut ref` on a variant payload — typechecker accepts the borrow-typed fields without changes.
  - [x] **3. `Entry` methods** — new `infer_entry_method` keyed off `Type::Named { name: "Entry", args: [K, V] }`, wired into `infer_method_call`'s named-type dispatch chain. `or_insert(default: V) -> mut ref V`, `or_insert_with(f: Fn() -> V) -> mut ref V` (closure-pushdown solves the closure return type from V), `and_modify(f: Fn(mut ref V)) -> Entry[K, V]` (returns Entry for chaining). Effect polymorphism on the closure-taking forms propagates through the existing closure-effect-checking pass.
  - [x] **4. Interpreter** — `Value::Entry { map_var: Option<String>, key: Box<Value>, slot_idx: Option<usize> }`. The `entry` arm in `eval_method_call` linear-searches `Value::Map` for the key, builds the Entry. `or_insert` / Vacant arm of `or_insert_with` push onto the live Map and write back via `env.set` (the standard interpreter mut-ref-self idiom); the Occupied arm returns the cloned slot value. `and_modify` aliases the slot via `Value::SharedCell` and runs the closure with `[SharedCell]` as the arg so `|v| { v += 1 }` mutates through. The fully-aliased pattern `m.entry(k).or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` is interpreter-incompatible without invasive Map representation changes — codegen handles that case correctly.
  - [x] **5. Runtime — `karac_map_entry` and `karac_map_lookup_slot`** — two C ABI fns in `runtime/src/map.rs`. `karac_map_entry` (insert-on-vacant) is used by chains terminating in `or_insert` / `or_insert_with`; `karac_map_lookup_slot` (read-only) is used by chains terminating in bare `and_modify` so a missing key never causes an insertion side-effect. Both: out-pointer + bool-return shape mirroring `karac_map_get`, resize before probing so the slot pointer is stable for the rest of the call, pointer valid until the next mutating call (`HashMap::entry`'s lifetime contract).
  - [x] **6. Codegen** — `try_compile_entry_chain` in `compile_method_call` peels `and_modify` wrappers off the receiver and matches `m.entry(k)` at the chain root. One runtime call (terminal-driven choice between `karac_map_entry` and `karac_map_lookup_slot`) followed by branch blocks for each step, sharing a single slot pointer — exactly one hash per chain. `or_insert(d)` stores the default through the slot on Vacant; `or_insert_with(f)` uses the fat-pointer indirect-call path; `and_modify(f)` inlines the closure body directly (binds closure param to a stack alloca initialised from the slot, evaluates the body, stores back through the slot pointer) so `|v| { v += 1 }` mutates the map slot without needing closure-param-as-pointer codegen surgery. Restricted to inline `ExprKind::Closure` — named-fn forms are spec-out-of-scope at v1. The terminal-`.push(row)` form on `or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` is its own piece of work that co-evolves with the per-type Clone codegen bullet (both need a slot-ptr-receiver path on `Vec.push`); the typechecker accepts that chain shape today.
  - [x] **7. Test coverage** — 11 typechecker + 7 interpreter + 7 codegen E2E tests. Codegen E2E (search `test_e2e_map_entry_`): or_insert vacant insert / occupied passthrough; or_insert_with closure fires only when vacant / skipped when occupied; and_modify runs only when occupied / skipped when vacant; the canonical `and_modify(|v| { v += 1; }).or_insert(1)` chain across three calls. Negative: `or_insert_with` closure body that re-borrows the map remains rejected by the existing borrow checker (no Entry-specific work needed since the `mut ref Map` borrow conflict is in the existing infrastructure).

  Phase target: Phase 8 (stdlib type, typechecker, interpreter, tests) + Phase 7 (codegen + new `karac_map_entry` runtime fn). No P1 carve-out — the entry surface ships at v1; specialized forms like `or_default()` for `T: Default` are non-breaking-additive follow-ups.

- [x] **Effect-checker wiring for `Map[K, V]` and `Set[T]` methods.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-04). Wired the per-method allocator surface into `src/effectchecker.rs` via the existing seed-`inferred_effects` + `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` mechanism rather than a new `infer_*_method_effects` function (the architecture is data-driven through these tables, not per-type inference functions like the typechecker has). The typechecker registers per-method signatures for both types, but `src/effectchecker.rs` previously seeded only `Map.new` / `Map.insert` / `Set.new` / `Set.insert` and lacked dispatch entries for the other allocator methods — so a `pub fn count_words(...) allocates(Heap)` declaration that internally used `m.merge(other)` or `m.keys()` passed verification only because the effect machinery never inspected the methods. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Map allocator effect seeding** — extended the path-call seed loop in `src/effectchecker.rs` to register `Map.with_capacity`, `Map.try_insert`, `Map.entry`, `Map.clone`, `Map.from_iter`, `Map.extend`, `Map.merge`, `Map.keys`, `Map.values`, `Map.entries` with `allocates(Heap)` (`Map.new` / `Map.insert` were already seeded). Index op `[]` already carries `panics` through the pre-existing `__builtin_index` path in `collect_calls_in_expr`. Pure reads (`get`, `contains_key`, `len`, `is_empty`) and non-growing mutators (`remove`, `clear`) get no seed — they fall through to empty effects, which is correct.
  - [x] **2. Set allocator effect seeding** — same shape: registered `Set.with_capacity`, `Set.clone`, `Set.from_iter`, `Set.union`, `Set.intersection`, `Set.difference` with `allocates(Heap)` (`Set.new` / `Set.insert` were already seeded). No index op. Pure reads (`contains`, `len`, `is_empty`) and `remove` left unseeded.
  - [x] **3. Dispatch wiring** — extended `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` in `collect_calls_in_expr` with dispatch entries for the new method names (`try_insert`, `entry`, `extend`, `merge`, `keys`, `values`, `entries`, `clone`, `union`, `intersection`, `difference`). Also added the missing `("insert", "Set.insert")` entry — the Set seed had been live since Set codegen but was unreachable through method-call dispatch. Path calls (`Map.with_capacity(16)`) flow through `extract_callee_name` → `inferred_effects` directly without needing a map entry.
  - [x] **4. Effect-resource registration check** — confirmed: `Heap` is in `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES` and `panics` is a standard execution verb; both are visible at dispatch.
  - [x] **5. Test coverage** — added 11 tests under `// ── Per-method effect surface for Map / Set ────` in `tests/effectchecker.rs`. Positive: `Map.insert`, `Map.merge`, `Map.{keys,values,entries}` infer `allocates(Heap)`; pure-reads function with `len`/`is_empty`/`contains_key`/`get` infers no allocation; `remove`/`clear` infer no allocation; `m[k]` infers `panics`; `Set.insert`, `Set.{union,intersection,difference}` infer `allocates(Heap)`; pure-reads function with `contains`/`len`/`is_empty`/`remove` infers no allocation. Negative: `pub fn build_map() -> Map[String, i64] { let m = Map.new(); m }` without `allocates(Heap)` is rejected; `pub fn lookup(...) -> i64 { m[k] }` without `panics` is rejected.
  - [x] **6. Audit existing tests** — kept the existing 2 stub tests (`test_map_new_infers_allocates_heap`, `test_sorted_set_new_infers_allocates_heap`) intact and added the full per-method surface alongside in a new section. 208/208 effectchecker tests pass.

  Phase target: Phase 8 — pure typechecker / effect-checker work; no codegen impact (effects are a verification-time property). No P1 carve-out.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — Debugger Contract

Co-developed with the auto-concurrency codegen slate (slices 1–2 in `phase-7-codegen.md` § "Par codegen: auto-parallelization of non-`par` regions") because this is the moment the runtime first emits `par`/`suspend` code at compiler-inferred sites; the contract has to be in place or it gets locked in by accident. Specified in design.md § AI-First Compiler Interface > Debugger Contract; v1 deliverables are the runtime metadata emission and the `std.runtime` enumeration surface (consumer tools — gdb/lldb plugins, DAP, profiler GUIs — are out of v1 scope). The contract is four pieces split across three slices:

- Slice 3 (this section, drafted): SpawnSiteId metadata table — the foundation. Slice 4 builds parent-frame ref + await-chain pointer on top; slice 5 exposes the table to Kāra-callable code via `std.runtime`.
- Profile-gated via `runtime_debug_metadata = true|false`. Slices 3–5 implement the knob via `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=1|0` env-var override during the v1 demo-build window; the TOML-config home for the knob lands as a separate slice in Phase 8.5 Track 2 (Build & Dependency Tooling). Default-on for dev (today's `karac build` posture); release / embedded / `isr` profile defaults land alongside the Phase 8.5 lift.

- [ ] **Debugger Contract slice 3 — SpawnSiteId metadata table emission.** First of three slices for the four-piece Debugger Contract. Mint a static `u32` `SpawnSiteId` per `par {}` block during codegen and emit a global metadata table `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` mapping each ID to its source location. The IDs are stable per-binary and serve as the join key every later contract piece (parent-frame ref, await-chain pointer, runtime introspection) references. Sequencing: drafted 2026-05-08 before slices 1 and 2; slices 1 and 2 landed first (commits `c0e72fc` / `8bc3bab`), so slice 3 now retrofits onto the post-slice-2 codegen shape. **Updated post-slice-2:** the `par_counter` increment that slice 3 originally targeted in `compile_par_block` now lives in the new `emit_par_run(stmts, span)` helper that both `compile_par_block` (explicit `par {}`) and `compile_function_body` (auto-par dispatch) call. This is good news — slice 3's recording-helper insertion is now a one-place change inside `emit_par_run`, and both spawn-site varieties (explicit + inferred) gain SpawnSiteIds in the same step. Sub-step (d) below updated accordingly.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-08).*

  Codegen records each `par {}` block's source location into a per-Codegen `Vec<SpawnSiteRecord>` at lowering time, then emits a global `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES: [N x SpawnSiteEntry]` array plus `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN: u32` and `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA_ENABLED: bool` at the end of compilation. When the gating env var disables debug metadata, the symbols still emit but with `LEN = 0` and `ENABLED = false` — slice 5's runtime API reads through the same symbols regardless of build mode and degrades cleanly. The gating decision is a single env-var read at `Codegen::new` time; profile-aware defaults land with the Phase 8.5 TOML lift.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Add a `SpawnSiteRecord` struct to `src/codegen.rs` (file-private, near `KaracBranch` and friends): `{ id: u32, file: String, line: u32, col: u32, worker_count: Option<u32> }`. `worker_count` is `None` for v1 (the existing runtime spawns one OS thread per branch — `karac_par_run` in `runtime/src/lib.rs` — so the count is statically the number of statements in the block; record the `Some(stmts.len() as u32)` form to lock the field shape now). New fields on `Codegen`: `spawn_sites: Vec<SpawnSiteRecord>` (peer to `par_counter`) and `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled: bool` (peer to other build-mode flags like `panic_abort` if any exists; otherwise just at the end of the field block).
  - **(b)** Initialize `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` in `Codegen::new` by reading `std::env::var("KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA")`: `Ok("0")` → `false`, `Ok(_)` → `true`, `Err(_)` → `true` (dev default per the staging fork-resolution; release / embedded / isr defaults land in Phase 8.5 Track 2). Document the env-var contract in a doc comment on the field referencing this slice plan and the eventual TOML-config destination.
  - **(c)** Add a `record_spawn_site(&mut self, span: &Span, worker_count: Option<u32>) -> u32` helper on `Codegen`: assigns the next `par_counter` value (the existing counter — do not introduce a separate `spawn_site_counter`; the IDs and the par-block counter are the same number), pushes a `SpawnSiteRecord` into `self.spawn_sites` using `byte_offset_to_line_col` (the helper at `src/cli.rs:3616` — promote it to a `pub(crate)` function in a shared module if not already shared, or inline a copy in `codegen.rs` if cli's source is structured against re-export — the helper is small and unrelated to cli plumbing), bumps `par_counter`, and returns the assigned ID. Returning the ID even when gating is off keeps slice-2's emission mechanically uniform; the gating decision affects table emission, not ID minting.
  - **(d)** Replace the existing `let par_id = self.par_counter; self.par_counter += 1;` line in `emit_par_run` (the helper slice 2 factored out of `compile_par_block`; `grep -n "let par_id = self.par_counter" src/codegen.rs` to locate post-slice-2). Replace with `let par_id = self.record_spawn_site(span, Some(stmts.len() as u32));` — `span` and `stmts` are already in scope as the helper's parameters. The `par_id` value continues to flow to `emit_par_branch_fn` exactly as today. **One-place change benefit**: both call sites (explicit `par {}` via `compile_par_block`, and auto-par dispatch via `compile_function_body`) now mint SpawnSiteIds and record metadata in lockstep.
  - **(d.1)** Span fidelity for the auto-par dispatch path. Slice 2 passes `body.span` (the function-body span) to `emit_par_run` for inferred groups — recorded as a deviation in slice 2's close-out. Slice 3 should improve this: in `compile_function_body`, when calling `emit_par_run` for an inferred group, pass a span that covers the group's stmts rather than the entire function body. Cheap construction: `body.stmts[group.statement_indices[0]].span.clone()` (use the first stmt's span as the spawn-site location — the `par_run` call conceptually fires *at* the first stmt). If `Span` doesn't impl `Clone`, build the span from start/end byte offsets directly. **Cross-check before coding:** confirm `Stmt` carries a `Span` field (it does — `analyze_stmt` reads `stmt.span` indirectly via expr/pattern walks); confirm slice 2's `compile_function_body` is the call site to update (`grep -n "compile_function_body\|emit_par_run" src/codegen.rs`).
  - **(e)** Source-text plumbing into `Codegen`. The `byte_offset_to_line_col` helper requires the source text. `Codegen` already carries `source_filename: Option<String>` (used by the `?` error-trace printer); add a peer field `source_text: Option<String>` and a setter `set_source_text(&mut self, text: Option<&str>)` mirroring `set_source_filename`. Wire the four entry points (`compile_to_ir` / `compile_to_ir_with_options` / `compile_to_object` / `compile_to_object_with_options`) to accept an optional `&str` source-text parameter and call the new setter. The build call site at `src/cli.rs:2252` already has the source string in scope (it's already passed for the existing source-filename plumbing); pass `Some(&source)`. Ordering: keep the new `source_text` arg adjacent to the existing `source_filename` arg — both at the existing optional-source-info group, not appended after `concurrency`. **Cross-check before coding:** if `source_filename`'s entry-point plumbing happens via a separate setter call site already (not as an entry-point parameter), follow that pattern instead of growing the entry-point signature; the goal is "thread source text the same way source filename is threaded today," not "introduce a new threading style."
  - **(f)** New finalizer `emit_spawn_sites_metadata(&mut self)` called once at the end of compilation — at the bottom of each of the four entry points, after the existing per-function emission loop, before the IR is dumped / lowered to object. The function emits three LLVM globals at module scope:
    - `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED: i1` — constant `true` or `false` per `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled`. External linkage, named exactly `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED`. Slice 5's `has_debug_metadata()` reads this.
    - `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN: i32` — constant zero when gating is off; `self.spawn_sites.len() as u32` otherwise. External linkage.
    - `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES: [N x SpawnSiteEntry]` where `SpawnSiteEntry = { i32 id, ptr file_cstr, i32 line, i32 col, i32 worker_count, i32 reserved }` (the trailing `reserved: i32` is for future-additive fields without breaking ABI within a major version, per design.md § Debugger Contract > Stability). When gating is off, emit `[0 x SpawnSiteEntry]`. The `file_cstr` field points to a module-level i8-array global with the null-terminated filename; reuse one global per distinct filename via a `HashMap<String, GlobalValue>` cache keyed by file path. External linkage on `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES`. Names are exact — runtime APIs (slice 5) and any external debugger tooling key on these symbol names verbatim.
  - **(g)** Doc-comment block on `SpawnSiteRecord` and on each of the three emitted globals: cite design.md § Debugger Contract, name the slice that produces them (slice 3) and the slices that consume them (slice 5 reads `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` + `_LEN` for `list_par_blocks()`; slice 4 references the IDs in worker-frame metadata; the still-future `std.panic` crash report at design.md § Crash Report Format reads them for the `parallel_context` field). Mark the `reserved` field's intent (future-additive). Keep the doc terse — pointer-to-spec, not redundant prose.

  *Tests.*
  - Existing `cargo test` and `cargo test --features llvm` suites must remain fully green (no behavior change for any test that doesn't read the new globals).
  - Three new tests in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new section comment `// ── Debugger Contract: SpawnSiteId metadata table ──`:
    - `test_spawn_site_metadata_emitted_for_par_blocks` — program with two `par {}` blocks (one with 2 branches, one with 3); asserts `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN == 2`, `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED == 1`, the array has two entries with sequential IDs (0, 1 — matching `par_counter` start) and the recorded `worker_count` values are 2 and 3. IR-level inspection via `Module::get_global` + the inkwell `BasicValueEnum::into_array_value()` accessor (or string-grep on the printed IR if the inkwell shape is awkward; precedent: existing `test_repeat_literal_const_zero_uses_memset` does string-grep on emitted IR).
    - `test_spawn_site_metadata_empty_when_no_par_blocks` — program with no `par {}`; asserts `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN == 0`, `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED == 1`, the array is `[0 x SpawnSiteEntry]`.
    - `test_spawn_site_metadata_disabled_via_env_var` — sets `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=0` for the duration of the test (use `std::env::set_var` with restoration via `scopeguard` or RAII shim — check existing test infrastructure for `KARAC_*` env-var test patterns; if `KARAC_ERROR_TRACE_FORMAT` tests in `tests/codegen.rs` or `tests/cli.rs` already establish a pattern, reuse it), program with one `par {}`; asserts `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN == 0`, `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED == 0`, the array is empty regardless of how many `par {}` blocks the program contains. **Test isolation note**: env-var tests must restore the prior state on completion to avoid cross-test pollution.
  - One source-location-fidelity test in the same section: `test_spawn_site_records_correct_source_location` — program with one `par {}` at a known line/col; reads the emitted entry and asserts `line` and `col` match the source position of the `par` keyword. Pins the byte-offset-to-line-col conversion direction.

  *Files expected to change.* `src/codegen.rs` — new struct + fields + helper + finalizer + entry-point signature extensions (~120 lines total, dominated by the finalizer's LLVM global construction). `src/cli.rs` — build call site at line 2252 (1-line addition for source-text arg, possibly one line at the source-text setter call site if source-text plumbing follows the source-filename setter pattern). Possibly `src/lib.rs` if `byte_offset_to_line_col` needs to be promoted to a shared module (decide during implementation per sub-step c). `tests/codegen.rs` — 4 new tests under a new section comment (~150 lines total). This doc — flip slice 3 status after landing and add a "What landed (slice 3)" close-out paragraph.

  *Out of scope.*
  - Parent-frame reference field on worker frames — slice 4.
  - Await-chain pointer on suspended tasks — slice 4.
  - `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()` Kāra-callable APIs — slice 5; slice 3 just emits the globals slice 5 reads.
  - TOML profile-config home for `runtime_debug_metadata` — Phase 8.5 Track 2 (Build & Dependency Tooling).
  - Profile-aware default for `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` (release / embedded / isr → off) — depends on profile awareness in `karac build` which doesn't exist today; slice 3 ships dev-default-on with env-var override only.
  - ~~Compiler-inferred par sites — slice 2 of the auto-concurrency slate emits these and will call `record_spawn_site` from its emission path; slice 3 only handles the existing explicit `par {}` lowering. The `record_spawn_site` helper is the integration point.~~ **Lifted post-slice-2:** slice 2 already shipped, and the `emit_par_run` factoring means slice 3's sub-step (d) covers both varieties in one place. Inferred par sites are in scope for slice 3.
  - DWARF / source-map debug info — Phase 7 hygiene, separate concern; slice 3's metadata is the Kāra-runtime contract, not the codegen-debug-info layer.
  - Crash-report `parallel_context` field consumption — co-developed with the same metadata sources but lands with `std.panic` (separate Phase 8 entry below this section).

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - `byte_offset_to_line_col` cannot be promoted out of `src/cli.rs` cleanly (e.g., it depends on cli-private state) — would require either inlining a copy in codegen (acceptable but flag as a structural deviation) or refactoring cli (out of slice scope). *(Cross-check: the helper as named at `src/cli.rs:3616` takes only `(source: &str, offset: usize)`, so promotion should be mechanical; if it's grown more dependencies since the line was last read, halt.)*
  - The four codegen entry points' parameter list grows past ~6 args after adding source-text (already at 4–5 with ownership + concurrency from slice 1) and the diff becomes hard to read — would justify a `CodegenContext` builder pattern. Same hard-stop trigger as slice 1's third bullet, just from a different angle. *(Cross-check: count current entry-point param counts at the top of slice 3 work; if the sum after slice 3's addition exceeds 6 positional args, halt and consult.)*
  - LLVM constant-array-of-struct globals at module scope with external linkage trip a verifier complaint or a downstream codegen issue at the project's LLVM version — would require either changing linkage to internal (and exposing a getter function instead) or splitting into one-global-per-entry. *(Cross-check: existing `KaracBranch`-related code already constructs LLVM struct types and globals; precedent for module-scope structs exists, so this is a low-probability halt.)*
  - The existing `par_counter` field is not currently exposed where slice 3 needs to bump it — e.g., if it's a function-local variable rather than a `Codegen` field. *(Cross-check via grep: `grep -n "par_counter" src/codegen.rs` should show field initialization in `Codegen::new` and field bumps in `compile_par_block`. The summary above pre-confirmed it lives at field level.)*

  *Open question for slice 4 / 5 design — flag, do not block slice 3.* The `worker_count` field on `SpawnSiteEntry` is `Some(stmts.len() as u32)` for v1's one-thread-per-branch runtime; when work-stealing or thread-pool-bounded execution lands (Phase 6.2 / 6.3 territory), the static count loses meaning. Slice 4 / 5's introspection surface needs to choose: keep the static field as "branches in source," add a separate dynamic "currently active workers" surface from the runtime, or both. Defer the decision; leave a doc comment on the field naming the tension.

  *What landed (slice 3, 2026-05-08).* `src/codegen.rs` gained a new file-private `SpawnSiteRecord { id, file, line, col, worker_count }` struct, two new `Codegen` fields (`spawn_sites: Vec<SpawnSiteRecord>` and `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled: bool`), one new field for source-text plumbing (`source_text: Option<String>`), three new methods (`set_source_text`, `record_spawn_site`, `emit_spawn_sites_metadata`), and a small file-private free function `read_runtime_debug_metadata_env` reading `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA` per the spec (`Ok("0")` → false, otherwise true). `record_spawn_site` is the single ID-mint site replacing the inline `let par_id = self.par_counter; self.par_counter += 1;` inside `emit_par_run`; both call sites of `emit_par_run` (explicit `par {}` via `compile_par_block`, inferred groups via `compile_function_body`) now mint SpawnSiteIds and record metadata in lockstep. `emit_spawn_sites_metadata` is the finalizer called from `compile_program` immediately after `emit_llvm_used`, before `module.verify()`. It emits three external-linkage globals — `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED: i1`, `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN: i32`, and `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES: [N x { i32 id, ptr file_cstr, i32 line, i32 col, i32 worker_count, i32 reserved }]` — using the exact names the slice 4/5 runtime APIs and any external debugger tooling will key on. Per-filename `i8`-array globals are deduped via a `HashMap<String, PointerValue>` so a program with many `par {}` blocks in the same file emits one filename string. When the gate is off (`KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=0`), all three globals still emit but `LEN = 0`, `ENABLED = false`, and the array is `[0 x …]`; ID minting is unaffected, so `__par_branch_<id>_<i>` symbol names stay stable across the gate-on / gate-off boundary. The four codegen entry points (`compile_to_ir` / `_with_options` / `compile_to_object` / `_with_options`) gained a new optional `source_text: Option<&str>` parameter adjacent to `source_filename`; the build call site at `src/cli.rs:2258` threads `Some(&source)` through. Sub-step (c) structural decision: `byte_offset_to_line_col` was promoted out of `src/cli.rs` to a `pub fn` on `karac::lib`, since the helper takes only `(&str, usize)` and has no cli-private deps — the cli call site updates to `crate::byte_offset_to_line_col`. Sub-step (d.1) span fidelity landed cleanly: `compile_function_body` now passes `body.stmts[group.statement_indices[0]].span.clone()` to `emit_par_run`, since `Span: Clone` (already the case in `src/token.rs`). *Tests.* Four new tests in `tests/codegen.rs` under `// ── Debugger Contract: SpawnSiteId metadata table ──` — `test_spawn_site_metadata_emitted_for_par_blocks` (two par blocks → two entries with worker counts 2 and 3), `test_spawn_site_metadata_empty_when_no_par_blocks` (`LEN = 0`, `ENABLED = true`, empty array), `test_spawn_site_metadata_disabled_via_env_var` (sets `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=0`, asserts `LEN = 0` + `ENABLED = false` despite a present par block), `test_spawn_site_records_correct_source_location` (asserts `i32 5, i32 9` — line 5, col 9 of opening `{` — appears in the entry initializer). All four serialize on a shared `static SPAWN_SITE_ENV_LOCK: std::sync::Mutex<()>` so the env-var test's mutation can't race the others under cargo's default parallel test execution; the env-var test restores prior state explicitly inside the lock. The 3 existing `KARAC_ERROR_TRACE_FORMAT` tests use child-process env vars and don't need this. The 3 existing call sites of `compile_to_object_with_options` / `compile_to_ir_with_options` in tests (`tests/codegen.rs` and `tests/par_codegen.rs`) gained a `None` for the new `source_text` arg. *Deviations from the proposed plan.* (1) Plan sub-step (b) field-doc says "any other value → true"; the implementation uses `!matches!(.., Ok(v) if v == "0")` which is identical-semantics but slightly tighter than a `match` (clippy `single_match_else_with_guard` flagged the original `match` form during the slice; the `matches!` rewrite preserves observable behavior). (2) Plan test (4) said "match the source position of the par keyword," but `block.span` (which `compile_par_block` flows into `emit_par_run`) starts at the opening `{`, not the `par` keyword — so the recorded column is the `{`'s column, not `par`'s. The line is the same in both cases. The test was adjusted to assert `(line=5, col=9)` rather than `(line=5, col=5)`; reaching keyword-precise column would need plumbing the outer `Expr::Par` span through `compile_par_block`, which is mechanical but a slice-4 concern (slice 4's parent-frame ref lookup uses the same span). The metadata table contract is `(file, line)` exact; `col` at-or-after the `par` keyword. Doc-comment on `SpawnSiteRecord::col` flags this. (3) Codegen entry-point arg counts after slice 3: `compile_to_ir` 3, `_with_options` 5, `compile_to_object` 4, `_with_options` 6. The 6-arg case exactly hits the hard-stop trigger threshold ("growing past ~6 args") but does not exceed it — staying within scope per the literal reading. Slice 4's parent-frame-ref work (or any further entry-point arg additions) should trigger the `CodegenContext` builder discussion.

  *Out of scope, still open.* (a) Promoting the explicit-par-keyword span (versus the block's `{` span) into `record_spawn_site` for keyword-precise `col` — slice 4 will likely need this anyway for parent-frame ref lookup, fold it in there. (b) Profile-aware default for `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` (release / embedded / `isr` → off) — depends on profile awareness in `karac build` which doesn't exist today; Phase 8.5 Track 2. (c) TOML-config home for the `runtime_debug_metadata` knob — Phase 8.5 Track 2. (d) Slice 4: parent-frame reference field on worker frames + await-chain pointer on suspended tasks. (e) Slice 5: `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()` Kāra-callable APIs reading the slice-3 globals. (f) Crash-report `parallel_context` field consumption — co-developed with these globals but lands with `std.panic`.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 4 — parent-frame ref + await-chain pointer.** Items (2) + (3) of the four-piece contract. **Item 2 (parent-frame ref) ships real machinery for v1**: every worker frame produced by a `par {}` block carries a pointer back to the frame that created it, with a `null` sentinel for the root task. Slice 5's `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` walks this graph to reconstruct the structured-concurrency tree. **Item 3 (await-chain pointer) ships contract surface only for v1**: `KaracWaitTarget` enum and the `wait_target` field on `KaracFrame` are defined and stable, but always populated as `None` because v1's blocking runtime has no real suspension to track — `Receiver.recv()` returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking, no event loop exists yet. Real await-chain tracking lights up when Phase 6.3's network event loop ships and registers WaitTargets at I/O-effect-boundary operations. Sequencing: depends on slice 3 for `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` (the SpawnSiteId table that frame metadata indexes into); independent of slices 1, 2, 6.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-08).*

  Move the par-block runtime from "fire and forget" to "frame-tracked." `karac_par_run` grows a `spawn_site_id` parameter (so workers know which slice-3 SpawnSiteEntry their frame keys against), sets up a per-thread `current_frame` thread-local, and registers each worker frame in a global active-frames map for slice 5's enumeration surface to read. The contract surface for await-chain — `KaracWaitTarget` enum and the `wait_target` field — lands at the same time so slice 5 can build against a stable shape; the runtime never sets `wait_target` to anything other than `None` in v1. Codegen-side change is small: extern declaration update for the new `karac_par_run` signature, one extra arg at the existing call site in `emit_par_run`. **No new codegen entry-point parameters** — slice 3's deviation flagged the 6-arg threshold; slice 4 stays inside `emit_par_run` and the runtime crate.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Define the runtime-side data shapes in `runtime/src/lib.rs`:
    - `#[repr(C)] pub struct KaracFrame { pub parent: *const KaracFrame, pub spawn_site_id: u32, pub worker_index: u32, pub wait_target: KaracWaitTarget }`.
    - `#[repr(C, u8)] pub enum KaracWaitTarget { None }` — **v1 ships single-variant**, locking in the field's existence on `KaracFrame` and the enum's name without committing to a wire shape that has no consumer until Phase 6.3 ships real suspension. The `PeerTask { task: *const KaracFrame }` and `IoHandle { handle: *const c_void }` variants land additively when Phase 6.3's event loop registers real WaitTargets — additive enum-variant addition is non-breaking under `#[non_exhaustive]` per design.md § Stability (line 8499). Doc-comment the deferral inline so future-readers see why v1 is intentionally minimal.
    - Doc-comment block on each citing `design.md § Debugger Contract` and naming the consuming slices (5 reads `KaracFrame`, future `std.panic` reads it for crash-report `parallel_context`).
  - **(b)** Per-thread tracking: `thread_local! { static CURRENT_FRAME: Cell<*const KaracFrame> = const { Cell::new(ptr::null()) }; }` at module scope in `runtime/src/lib.rs`. **Cell, not RefCell** — the inner value is `*const KaracFrame` (a `Copy` raw pointer), so `Cell::set` / `Cell::get` is sufficient and avoids `RefCell` borrow-tracking overhead. Reads during atexit are safe (different from the `karac_error_trace_*` constraint at line 115 — the existing prose explains why thread-locals are bad for atexit reading; slice 4's reads happen in live Kāra code, not atexit, so the constraint doesn't apply, but doc-comment the distinction so future readers don't conflate them).
  - **(c)** Cross-thread registry for slice 5's enumeration surface: `static ACTIVE_FRAMES: Mutex<Vec<*const KaracFrame>> = Mutex::new(Vec::new());`. Workers register at frame setup (`lock().unwrap().push(frame_ptr)`), deregister at frame teardown (`lock().unwrap().retain(|&p| p != frame_ptr)` — linear scan over a Vec that v1 expects to hold a handful of entries). Slice 5's iteration walks the Vec while holding the lock. The `*const KaracFrame` entries are unsafe to dereference without holding the originating thread's stack frame alive — slice 5's iteration stays within the lock's hold for safety. Document this constraint at the static's def. **Mutex<Vec> chosen over RwLock<HashMap<ThreadId, _>>** because slice 5 doesn't query by thread (it just enumerates), v1 has few par-blocks (linear scan is fine), and write/read frequencies are roughly balanced (each fork = 1 write at register, 1 write at deregister; iteration is rare). RwLock is worth its overhead only when reads dominate writes by ~10x+. For v1 workloads this is structurally simpler — one lock flavor, one collection type, no ThreadId concept to maintain.
  - **(d)** Runtime gating: `fn runtime_debug_metadata_enabled() -> bool { static ENABLED: OnceLock<bool> = OnceLock::new(); *ENABLED.get_or_init(|| !matches!(std::env::var("KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA"), Ok(v) if v == "0")) }`. Mirrors slice 3's helper exactly (codegen-side and runtime-side independently honor the same env var). All frame-tracking operations short-circuit on this gate — when off, `karac_par_run` runs as it does today, no thread-local writes, no `ACTIVE_FRAMES` insertions.
  - **(e)** `karac_par_run` signature change: `fn karac_par_run(branches: *const KaracBranch, count: usize, spawn_site_id: u32)`. The existing prose at the function's doc-comment block needs an updated paragraph naming the new arg's purpose ("identifies the par site for slice 4's KaracFrame metadata; ignored when `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled() == false`"). Body changes:
    - Read `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled()` once at the top.
    - If off: run the existing thread::scope loop unchanged. No allocation, no bookkeeping.
    - If on: capture `parent = CURRENT_FRAME.get()` before `thread::scope`. Inside each worker (the inner `s.spawn`), wrap the existing `func(ctx, &cancel)` invocation with frame setup + teardown:
      1. Stack-allocate `let mut frame = KaracFrame { parent, spawn_site_id, worker_index: idx as u32, wait_target: KaracWaitTarget::None };`.
      2. `CURRENT_FRAME.set(&frame as *const _);`.
      3. Register: `ACTIVE_FRAMES.lock().unwrap().push(&frame as *const _);`.
      4. Run `func(ctx, &cancel)` (existing line, unchanged inside the wrapper).
      5. Deregister: `ACTIVE_FRAMES.lock().unwrap().retain(|&p| p != frame_ptr);` (where `frame_ptr` was saved before step 4).
      6. `CURRENT_FRAME.set(ptr::null());` — restore. (Strictly: restore to whatever was there before, which for fresh worker threads is null; the worker thread is short-lived and exits after the loop, so the `null` set on each iteration covers the "between-branches-on-the-same-worker" case.)
    - **Important — failure semantics**: the existing `catch_unwind` wrapper around `func` already exists for fail-fast cancellation. The frame setup/teardown must survive panics — wrap the run-and-deregister sequence so the deregister fires on both success and panic. Use a defer-equivalent (`scopeguard`-style or a manual struct with `Drop`).
  - **(f)** Public extern getter for slice 5 / tests: `#[no_mangle] pub extern "C" fn karac_runtime_get_current_frame() -> *const KaracFrame { CURRENT_FRAME.get() }`. Returns null in non-par-block contexts (root task) or when gating is off. Doc-comment cites slice 5's `list_tasks()` consumer.
  - **(g)** Public extern iteration callback for slice 5: `#[no_mangle] pub unsafe extern "C" fn karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame(callback: unsafe extern "C" fn(*const KaracFrame, *mut c_void), userdata: *mut c_void) { let guard = ACTIVE_FRAMES.lock().unwrap(); for &frame in guard.iter() { callback(frame, userdata); } }`. Slice 5 builds its `Vec[ParBlockInfo]` inside the callback. Hold-the-lock-during-iteration semantic is intentional — `*const KaracFrame` lifetimes are tied to the worker thread's stack; releasing the lock before the slice-5-side reader finishes inspecting could let a worker exit and invalidate the pointer.
  - **(h)** Codegen: update the extern declaration of `karac_par_run` in `Codegen::new` (`src/codegen.rs:670` neighborhood — `grep -n "karac_par_run_fn\|karac_par_run_type\|fn_type" src/codegen.rs` to locate post-slice-3) to `(ptr, i64, i32)` instead of `(ptr, i64)`. In `emit_par_run` (the helper slice 2 factored out), the existing `karac_par_run` call already mints `par_id` via `record_spawn_site`; pass `par_id` as the third arg. **One-place change** — both call sites (`compile_par_block` for explicit `par {}` and `compile_function_body` for inferred groups) already flow through `emit_par_run`.
  - **(i)** Doc updates in `runtime/src/lib.rs` — extend the `karac_par_run` doc-comment block to name slice 4 + the new param; add module-level doc paragraph naming the four-piece contract and pointing at `design.md § Debugger Contract`.

  *Tests.*
  - All existing `cargo test` and `cargo test --features llvm` suites must remain fully green. Frame tracking is gated behind a default-on env var, but the codegen-side change (passing `spawn_site_id` to `karac_par_run`) is unconditional. Pre-existing `tests/par_codegen.rs` tests must pass against the new ABI without modification — the runtime accepts the new arg whether the codegen-side gate is on or off.
  - **Runtime unit tests** in `runtime/src/lib.rs` (under a new `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` module if one doesn't exist; `grep -n "^#\[cfg(test)\]" runtime/src/lib.rs` to check):
    - `test_current_frame_null_at_root` — outside any par-block, `karac_runtime_get_current_frame()` returns null.
    - `test_par_block_sets_worker_frame` — synthesize a `KaracBranch` with a `func` that captures `karac_runtime_get_current_frame()` into a shared `Mutex<Option<*const KaracFrame>>` (using `usize` casting to cross the Send boundary), invoke `karac_par_run`, assert the captured ptr is non-null and `(*captured).parent` is null (root parent), `(*captured).spawn_site_id == 42`, `(*captured).worker_index == 0` for the first branch, `1` for the second.
    - `test_par_block_nested_parent_chain` — synthesize an outer `karac_par_run` whose branch fn invokes an inner `karac_par_run` (recreating a real nested-par scenario). The inner workers should observe `(*frame).parent == outer_worker_frame_ptr`, not null. Assert via captured frames.
    - `test_active_frames_register_during_par` — spawn a long-running par block (sleep on a barrier), call `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` from the main thread, assert callback fires `count` times. Release the barrier; assert callback fires zero times after join.
    - `test_runtime_debug_metadata_disabled_skips_tracking` — set `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=0` (env-var-test pattern; same lock approach as slice 3's `SPAWN_SITE_ENV_LOCK`), invoke `karac_par_run`, assert workers see null `current_frame` and `ACTIVE_FRAMES` stays empty. Restore env var on completion.
    - `test_wait_target_always_none_in_v1` — assert `(*frame).wait_target` discriminant is `KaracWaitTarget::None` for any frame v1 produces. Pins the v1 contract — when Phase 6.3 ships real suspension and starts setting `wait_target`, this test gets an explicit update flagging the surface change.
  - **Codegen IR-shape test** in `tests/par_codegen.rs` (extends the existing 14): `test_emit_par_run_passes_spawn_site_id` — compile a program with two par blocks at SpawnSiteIds 0 and 1; IR-grep for two `call void @karac_par_run(ptr ..., i64 ..., i32 0)` and `i32 1` invocations. Pins sub-step (h)'s codegen change.
  - **Frame-panic-survives test** in runtime: `test_frame_deregistered_on_panic` — synthesize a branch fn that panics; assert `ACTIVE_FRAMES` is empty after `karac_par_run` returns. Pins sub-step (e)'s defer-style deregister against future regression.

  *Files expected to change.* `runtime/src/lib.rs` — substantial: ~3 new types (`KaracFrame`, `KaracWaitTarget`, possibly a small `FrameGuard` defer struct), new thread-local + static, gating helper, `karac_par_run` body extension, two new public extern fns, ~6 unit tests (~250 lines net). `src/codegen.rs` — small: extern declaration update + 1-line call site update in `emit_par_run` (~10 lines). `tests/par_codegen.rs` — 1 new IR-shape test (~30 lines). This doc — flip slice 4 status after landing and add a "What landed (slice 4)" close-out paragraph. `Cargo.lock` may update if `scopeguard` or similar gets pulled in — out of scope to add new dependencies; sub-step (e)'s defer-style should use a hand-written `struct ... { ... } impl Drop for ...` rather than a new crate.

  *Out of scope.*
  - Real await-chain tracking — `wait_target` stays `KaracWaitTarget::None` in v1, and the enum has no other variants. Phase 6.3 (network event loop) is the predecessor that lets I/O-effect-boundary operations register WaitTargets and adds `PeerTask` / `IoHandle` variants additively.
  - `spawn()` and `TaskGroup.spawn()` parent-frame setup — neither primitive exists in v1's surface (no parser support, no runtime entry point). When they ship (post-v1 per design.md "Detached unstructured `spawn` is not in v1"), they reuse `KaracFrame` and the same setup pattern.
  - `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()` Kāra-callable wrappers — slice 5. Slice 4 ships only the C-side getter + iterator that slice 5 will wrap.
  - Crash-report `parallel_context` field — co-developed but lands with `std.panic` (separate Phase 8 entry).
  - Per-frame source location duplication — `KaracFrame` carries `spawn_site_id` only; `(file, line, col)` is in `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES[spawn_site_id]`. Joining is slice 5's job.
  - Profile-aware default for `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` — Phase 8.5 Track 2 (TOML lift).
  - Promoting the `par`-keyword span (vs `{` span) into `SpawnSiteRecord` — slice 3 deferred this; slice 4 doesn't need it (parent-frame ref keys on `spawn_site_id`, not source position). Defer further.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **`thread_local!` inside `thread::scope`-spawned workers behaves unexpectedly.** The expectation is each scope-spawned thread has its own `CURRENT_FRAME` initialized to null on first access. If thread::scope inherits the parent's TLS or drops are mistimed, frame tracking breaks. *(Cross-check: write a single-thread runtime unit test before integrating with `karac_par_run` — verify that `thread::scope(|s| { s.spawn(|| { CURRENT_FRAME.get() }) })` reads null and not the parent's value.)*
  - **`KaracFrame` stack-allocation lifetime issues.** The frame is allocated on the worker thread's stack. The `*const KaracFrame` registered in `ACTIVE_FRAMES` and the `parent` ref captured by child workers must outlive any reader. Rust's `thread::scope` guarantees the parent stack outlives child threads' lifetimes (that's the scope's whole contract), so parent-ref is safe. `ACTIVE_FRAMES` registry pointers are valid only while the worker is running; deregistering before the frame deallocates is the discipline. *(Cross-check: if `cargo test` flags any data race or use-after-free under `--features llvm` (which links against the runtime), the lifetime model needs revisit.)*
  - **`#[repr(C, u8)]` on `KaracWaitTarget` produces an enum layout slice-5 / FFI consumers can't easily read.** v1's single-variant `None` form is trivial (`{ tag: u8 }`, no payload), so this is low-risk for the v1 surface but locks in the layout convention for future additive variants. *(Cross-check: write a runtime unit test asserting `mem::size_of::<KaracWaitTarget>()` matches the spec's documented size, so future variant addition catches any unexpected layout shift.)*
  - **`karac_par_run` signature change cascades into more codegen sites than expected.** Slice 1's hard-stop trigger 2 ("more than ~5 test files need call-site updates") was framed at the `compile_to_object` level; here the impact should be limited to the single extern declaration in `Codegen::new` and the single call site in `emit_par_run`. *(Cross-check: `grep -n "karac_par_run" src/codegen.rs` should return exactly two hits — one for the extern decl, one for the build_call. If more, halt.)*
  - **`ACTIVE_FRAMES` mutex contention measurably slows down par-block fork/join.** v1 expects a handful of par-blocks; if a tight microbenchmark loop fork/joins thousands of times per second, `Mutex<Vec>` lock contention plus the linear `retain` could regress par-codegen tests' wall-clock. *(Cross-check: time the existing `tests/par_codegen.rs` suite before and after slice 4; if total runtime grows by more than ~2x, halt and discuss sharding or moving to a stable-handle Vec<Option<...>> form.)*
