  *Open question for slice 5 design — flag, do not block slice 4.* Slice 5 needs to materialize each `KaracFrame` into a Kāra `ParBlockInfo` struct and join with the slice-3 `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` table to fill in `(file, line, source_loc)`. The join key is `spawn_site_id`. Slice 5's lookup needs to read the slice-3 globals from inside Kāra-runtime code; this means linking the runtime crate against the same compiled binary that emits the globals. **The path:** stdlib code in `std.runtime` declares the globals as extern symbols and reads them. Trivial in C, slightly fiddly in Kāra. Slice 5's plan-drafting should validate that Kāra source can declare extern globals (or use a `#[compiler_builtin]` shim that codegen-side resolves to direct LLVM global reads). Defer the resolution; recording here so slice 5's plan-drafter sees it.

  *Slice 6 plan-drafting note.* Slice 6 (Parallax-lite microbenchmark workload) is the natural next plan-draft once slice 4 lands — slice 6 doesn't depend on slice 5 (introspection APIs are observability infrastructure, not workload prerequisites), and slice 6's demo gravity makes it the higher-priority follow-up. Slice 6's plan lives in the new `### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — Parallax-lite Workload` section below.

  *What landed (slice 4, 2026-05-08).* `runtime/src/lib.rs` gained two new public-extern types (`KaracFrame { parent: *const KaracFrame, spawn_site_id: u32, worker_index: u32, wait_target: KaracWaitTarget }` under `#[repr(C)]`; `KaracWaitTarget` under `#[repr(u8)] #[non_exhaustive]` with a single `None` variant), a thread-local `CURRENT_FRAME: Cell<*const KaracFrame>` (initialized to null per the constraint that `Cell::set/get` is sufficient for `Copy` raw-pointer storage), a cross-thread `static ACTIVE_FRAMES: Mutex<Vec<FramePtr>>` registry, a private `FramePtr(*const KaracFrame)` newtype with `unsafe impl Send + Sync` (raw pointers are `!Send` by default; the soundness comes from `thread::scope`'s lifetime guarantee + `FrameGuard::drop` deregistering before stack frames deallocate), a private `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled() -> bool` gating helper backed by `OnceLock<bool>` (mirrors codegen's slice-3 helper exactly), and a private `FrameGuard` RAII struct whose `Drop` deregisters from `ACTIVE_FRAMES` and restores `CURRENT_FRAME` — the defer-style guard runs on both normal return and panic-unwind paths. `karac_par_run` grew a `spawn_site_id: u32` argument (third position) and now branches on `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled()`: gate-off runs the existing `thread::scope` loop unchanged (no allocation, no bookkeeping); gate-on captures `CURRENT_FRAME.get()` as `parent_addr: usize` before `thread::scope` (the `usize` cast is the Send-boundary trick — children's `parent` field is set from this address), then each worker constructs a stack-allocated `KaracFrame`, wraps it in `FrameGuard::new(&frame)`, calls `func(ctx, &cancel)`, and the guard drops on scope exit. Two new `#[no_mangle] pub extern "C"` symbols ship: `karac_runtime_get_current_frame() -> *const KaracFrame` (returns null in non-par contexts or when gating is off; slice 5's `list_tasks()` consumer) and `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame(callback, userdata)` (callback fires under the `ACTIVE_FRAMES` lock to rule out reading-while-deregistering races; slice 5's `list_par_blocks()` consumer). `src/codegen.rs` extern decl at `Codegen::new` line ~796 grew a third arg type (`(ptr, i64, i32)`); `emit_par_run`'s `karac_par_run` build_call at line ~12749 now passes the slice-3 `par_id` as the third arg. *Tests.* Eight new `runtime::tests` unit tests under a new `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` block (~340 lines): `test_wait_target_size_pinned` (asserts `mem::size_of::<KaracWaitTarget>() == 1` per hard-stop trigger 3), `test_current_frame_null_at_root` (root task observes null), `test_par_block_sets_worker_frame` (synthesized branches capture frame fields; assert non-null, root parent, `spawn_site_id == 42`, worker indices `{0, 1}` as a set since the work-stealing pool doesn't guarantee branch-order dispatch), `test_par_block_nested_parent_chain` (outer-then-inner par; inner workers' `parent` matches outer worker's frame address), `test_active_frames_register_during_par` (3 workers wait on a `Barrier` quartet; main thread enumerates registry mid-run via `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` and sees count=3, then count=0 after join), `test_runtime_debug_metadata_disabled_skips_tracking` (uses a `#[cfg(test)] fn runtime_debug_metadata_enabled_uncached` re-read-each-call helper to bypass the `OnceLock` cache), `test_wait_target_always_none_in_v1` (reads the discriminant byte directly per `#[repr(u8)]` layout — pins the v1 surface), `test_frame_deregistered_on_panic` (tests `FrameGuard::drop` directly inside `catch_unwind` rather than through `karac_par_run`, since panics across `unsafe extern "C"` abort under Rust 1.81+). Env-var-touching tests serialize on a shared `static FRAME_TRACKING_ENV_LOCK: Mutex<()>` per slice 3's pattern. One new `tests/par_codegen.rs` IR-shape test (`test_emit_par_run_passes_spawn_site_id`) verifies the extern decl is `(ptr, i64, i32)` and that two par blocks emit calls with `i32 0` / `i32 1` respectively. The 14 existing par_codegen tests (and all other tests under `--features llvm`) remain green; total: 3003 passed under `cargo test`, 3312 under `cargo test --features llvm`. Wall-clock for `tests/par_codegen.rs` post-slice: 0.54s (baseline 0.52s — within ~4% noise, well under the 2x mutex-contention hard-stop threshold). *Deviations from the proposed plan.* (1) `KaracWaitTarget` ships under `#[repr(u8)]` rather than `#[repr(C, u8)]` because rustc rejects `#[repr(C, u8)]` on no-payload enums (`E0566 conflicting representation hints` — future-incompatible warning that will become a hard error). The single-variant v1 form is `{ tag: u8 }` either way, so the wire shape is identical. When Phase 6.3 adds payload-carrying variants the repr upgrades to `#[repr(C, u8)]` (the standard tagged-union convention), which rustc accepts on multi-variant enums; the existing `None` variant keeps discriminant 0 so the upgrade is wire-compatible. Doc-comment on the enum names this trade-off explicitly. (2) `ACTIVE_FRAMES`'s `Vec` element type is `FramePtr` (a private `Copy + Send + Sync` newtype around `*const KaracFrame`) rather than the plan's literal `*const KaracFrame` — bare raw pointers are `!Send`, and the `Mutex<Vec<*const KaracFrame>>` form fails to satisfy `Sync` for use as a `static`. The newtype's `unsafe impl Send + Sync` documents the `thread::scope`-bounded lifetime invariant once at the type def rather than at every push/iter call site. (3) `test_frame_deregistered_on_panic` tests `FrameGuard` directly inside `std::panic::catch_unwind` rather than synthesizing a panicking `unsafe extern "C" fn` branch — Rust 1.81+ aborts on panics across `extern "C"` (the existing `catch_unwind` in `karac_par_run` only catches Rust-side wrapper panics, not foreign-call panics, which never happen in practice since codegen-emitted Kāra branches use Kāra's own panic protocol). What the test validates is the runtime-internal contract: `FrameGuard`'s `Drop` runs on the unwind path. Doc-comment in the test cites the abort behavior. (4) The `parent` pointer is shuttled across the `thread::scope` Send boundary as a `usize` (cast from `*const KaracFrame`) — the closures pass through scoped threads which `move`-capture the int and reconstitute the pointer inside each worker. Soundness: `thread::scope` guarantees the caller's stack outlives all children, so the address remains valid for the duration of the join; `FrameGuard` deregisters before any worker exits its scope. *Out of scope, still open.* (a) Slice 5: `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()` Kāra-callable wrappers consuming `karac_runtime_get_current_frame` + `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` and joining against `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES`. (b) Real await-chain tracking — `wait_target` stays `KaracWaitTarget::None` in v1 across every code path; Phase 6.3's network event loop ships `PeerTask` / `IoHandle` variants additively. (c) `spawn()` / `TaskGroup.spawn()` parent-frame setup — neither primitive exists in v1's surface; when they ship post-v1 they reuse `KaracFrame` and the same `FrameGuard` pattern. (d) Crash-report `parallel_context` field consumption — co-developed but lands with `std.panic`. (e) Profile-aware default for `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` (release / embedded / `isr` → off) — Phase 8.5 Track 2.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — Parallax-lite Workload

First demo-shaped consumer of slices 1 + 2. A real Kāra program with hand-coded providers, distinct effect resources, and three independent fan-out statements that auto-par lowering parallelizes in compiled output. Validates `karac query cost-summary` against the Cumulative Cost Surface table from `design.md § Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`. Sets up the framework for v1.x cost-model tuning + the `par struct` single-task overhead measurement; both follow-on analyses are explicitly v1.x territory per `roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Parallax-lite — first ground-truth measurement workload`.

**Demo-shape gap, surfaced upfront.** The canonical Parallax demo (`demo_ideas.md § Demo 1`) is *fan-out + join* — four parallel reads, results fed into `build_dashboard(profile, orders, notif, recommended)`. Slice 2's `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate blocks this exact pattern today: bindings defined inside a parallel group that are read by stmts outside the group don't auto-parallelize, because `karac_par_run`'s branch fns capture *into* their env struct but don't propagate let-bindings *out*. Lifting the gate requires the still-open `phase-7-codegen.md:182` entry **"Par codegen: return values"**, which extends the runtime ABI with per-branch return slots. Slice 6 ships the **measurement workload** (effect-only fan-out — three independent `writes(R_i)` calls on distinct resources, no joined return) which IS auto-par-eligible today. The demo workload (canonical fan-out + join) lights up when "Par codegen: return values" lands.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 6 — Parallax-lite microbenchmark workload.** Hand-coded effect-only-fan-out workload exercising slices 1 + 2 on a real program. Three deliverables: (a) a `examples/parallax_lite/` Kāra project with three trait-bound effect resources + `InMemoryMetrics` provider impl + a `process_request` driver function whose three top-level call statements auto-parallelize; (b) `karac query cost-summary` validation against the workload, pinning the output for the Cumulative Cost Surface table from `design.md § Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`; (c) a `--sequential` codegen flag (or env-var equivalent) that disables auto-par dispatch in `compile_function_body`, enabling side-by-side wall-clock benchmarking. Sequencing: depends on slice 2 (auto-par codegen MVP — already landed at `8bc3bab`). Independent of slices 3, 4, 5.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-08).*

  Build a compact Kāra program in `examples/parallax_lite/` that mirrors `examples/db_pipeline/`'s multi-file project shape (`kara.toml` + `src/*.kara`). The program defines three trait-bound effect resources (`MetricsA / MetricsB / MetricsC`) under a shared `MetricsRecorder` trait, an `InMemoryMetrics` provider impl whose `record(value: i64)` method does CPU-bound busy-compute (locking in a measurable runtime cost without depending on `sleep` primitives the runtime doesn't expose today), three small `record_a / record_b / record_c` driver functions each carrying a distinct `writes(R_i)` effect, and a `process_request` aggregator whose body is exactly three call statements with no return-value joining. The aggregator's body is the slice's load-bearing code — auto-par's analyzer must group the three calls (disjoint `writes` resources → no conflict edges), `is_trivial` must classify the group non-trivial (the `writes` effects are non-empty), `compile_function_body` must emit a single `karac_par_run` for the group. Three measurements feed off the same binary: cost-summary static counts, concurrency analysis surface, IR-shape pinning. A wall-clock benchmark (auto-par on/off) ships behind the `--sequential` flag; pass-fail signal is "auto-par version is faster" at a relaxed threshold (≥1.3x) — not a strict speedup ratio, since timing variance from OS scheduling makes tight thresholds flaky.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Create `examples/parallax_lite/` directory mirroring `examples/db_pipeline/`'s structure: `kara.toml` (`[package] name = "parallax_lite"`, no dependencies), `src/main.kara`, `src/resources.kara`, `src/workload.kara`. Optionally `src/metrics.kara` if the provider impl is large enough to warrant separation. Match `db_pipeline`'s `edition = "2026"` and module-import idiom (`import resources.{...};`).
  - **(b)** `src/resources.kara` defines:
    - `pub trait MetricsRecorder { fn record(mut ref self, value: i64); }`
    - `pub effect resource MetricsA: MetricsRecorder;` (and `MetricsB`, `MetricsC` — three distinct resources, each trait-bound to `MetricsRecorder`)
    - `pub struct InMemoryMetrics { count: i64 }` with a `pub fn new() -> InMemoryMetrics` constructor (mirrors `db_pipeline::InMemoryDb`)
    - `impl MetricsRecorder for InMemoryMetrics { fn record(mut ref self, value: i64) { ... } }` whose body does CPU-bound busy-compute over `0..value` (e.g., `let mut sum: i64 = 0; for i in 0..value { sum = sum.wrapping_add(i.wrapping_mul(i)); } self.count = self.count + 1;`). The `wrapping_*` ops are required to avoid overflow panics for large `value`. **Cross-check before coding:** confirm `i64.wrapping_add` / `wrapping_mul` are available in v1 (`grep -n "wrapping_add\|wrapping_mul" runtime/stdlib/`); if not, use plain addition with smaller `value` (e.g., 100_000 instead of 10_000_000).
  - **(c)** `src/workload.kara` defines three driver functions and the aggregator:
    - `fn record_a() with writes(MetricsA) { MetricsA.record(WORK); }` (and `record_b`, `record_c` against `MetricsB`, `MetricsC`).
    - `pub fn process_request() with writes(MetricsA), writes(MetricsB), writes(MetricsC) { record_a(); record_b(); record_c(); }`. The three call statements are top-level, no `let` bindings — the slice 2 `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate doesn't fire (no bindings to consume).
    - Define a module-level `const WORK: i64 = 10_000_000;` — easy to tune for the wall-clock benchmark without recompiling individually.
  - **(d)** `src/main.kara` wires up the providers via three nested `with_provider[R]` invocations (mirroring `db_pipeline::main`):
    ```kara
    fn main() {
        let metrics_a = InMemoryMetrics.new();
        let metrics_b = InMemoryMetrics.new();
        let metrics_c = InMemoryMetrics.new();
        with_provider[MetricsA](metrics_a, || {
            with_provider[MetricsB](metrics_b, || {
                with_provider[MetricsC](metrics_c, || {
                    process_request();
                });
            });
        });
        println("done");  // observable side-effect to confirm completion
    }
    ```
    **Cross-check before coding:** the `with_provider[R]` syntax has GAP-N/O/P comments in `db_pipeline/src/db.kara` — verify the GAPs aren't blocking; if `with_provider` is too gappy to use today, fall back to a simpler entry point that calls `process_request` after manually constructing providers (or doesn't construct providers at all if the provider mechanism isn't load-bearing for what slice 6 measures — pure auto-par lowering doesn't strictly need providers to fire).
  - **(e)** Add `--sequential` flag to `cmd_build` in `src/cli.rs`. Plumbing:
    - Add the flag to the build subcommand's argparse in `src/cli.rs:cmd_build` (precedent: existing flags like `-o`, the `--features` pattern; new flag is a bare bool, no value).
    - Plumb a `disable_auto_par: bool` field through `compile_to_object_with_options` (already at the 6-arg threshold per slice 3's deviation; this addition would push past it, **triggering hard-stop trigger 1**) — alternative: env-var-only gate, mirroring slice 3's `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA` pattern. **Recommended path: env-var only.** `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0` at codegen time; codegen reads it via a new `read_auto_par_env` helper; `compile_function_body` checks `self.auto_par_disabled` and falls through to `compile_block` if true. No new entry-point arg, no CLI flag in slice 6 (the user-facing CLI flag is a Phase 8.5 Track 2 deliverable when the profile system ships). Stretch goal in slice 6: ALSO add a CLI flag that sets the env var for child processes, so `karac build --sequential` becomes a UX nicety. **Cross-check before coding:** count current entry-point args (post slice 4 should still be 6 for `compile_to_object_with_options`); if adding `disable_auto_par` would push past 6, halt the CLI-flag path and ship env-var-only.
  - **(f)** New test `tests/parallax_lite.rs` (gated on `--features llvm` like `tests/codegen.rs`). Tests:
    - `test_parallax_lite_compiles_clean` — load and compile the entire `examples/parallax_lite/` project; assert no errors. Pins the workload as a regression-guard against future codegen changes that break it.
    - `test_parallax_lite_emits_par_run` — compile the workload's `workload.kara`, IR-grep for `call void @karac_par_run` in `process_request`'s body. One call site expected (the auto-par dispatch on the three `record_*` calls).
    - `test_parallax_lite_query_concurrency_groups_three_calls` — run `karac query concurrency examples/parallax_lite/src/workload.kara.process_request` (or whatever the per-function-target path is); assert the JSON output names a `parallel_group` containing three statement indices [0, 1, 2] with reason "no effect conflicts on disjoint resources" or similar.
    - `test_parallax_lite_query_cost_summary` — run `karac query cost-summary examples/parallax_lite/src/workload.kara` (whole-file form per `cost-summary takes a bare file path` at `src/cli.rs:541`); pin the JSON output structure (per-function counts of `rc_ops`, `arc_provider_wraps`, `borrow_flag_fields`, `partition_guard_sites`, `auto_clone_insertions`, plus the existing `perf_notes`). Assertion is structural ("the output has `by_function.process_request`, `totals.rc_ops`, etc."), not numerical (the actual counts depend on what the codegen emits — record observed counts in the close-out for the Cumulative Cost Surface table validation).
    - **Optional / behind feature flag**: `test_parallax_lite_wall_clock_benchmark` — compile the workload twice (once with `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0`, once without), run each binary, time wall-clock via `std::time::Instant`, assert `auto_par_time < sequential_time / 1.3` (relaxed 1.3x speedup threshold). **Mark `#[ignore]` by default** — wall-clock tests are flaky on CI; opt-in via `cargo test --ignored test_parallax_lite_wall_clock_benchmark`. Document the expected speedup range in the test's doc-comment.
  - **(g)** New `examples/parallax_lite/README.md` documenting:
    - **What it demonstrates.** Auto-concurrency on a real workload — `process_request`'s three top-level calls auto-parallelize without explicit `par {}`, just from effect-resource disjointness.
    - **The demo-shape gap.** Why this isn't yet the canonical Parallax demo (return-values needed for join shape).
    - **How to run.** `karac build examples/parallax_lite/` then `./parallax_lite`. With `--sequential` (or `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0`) for sequential baseline.
    - **Ground-truth measurements.** A small table of the cost-summary counts observed for this workload, validating (or flagging discrepancies against) the Cumulative Cost Surface table in `design.md § Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`. If discrepancies surface, file them as edits to the design doc — the spec text says discrepancies "feed back as edits to the table" (see `roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Parallax-lite`).
  - **(h)** Doc updates: append a "What landed (slice 6)" close-out paragraph to this slice in `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md`; add a slice 6 bullet + timing log row to `wip-list1.md`.

  *Tests.* Per sub-step (f). One required test file (`tests/parallax_lite.rs`) with 4 mandatory tests + 1 optional `#[ignore]`-gated wall-clock benchmark. All runs under `--features llvm`. Existing test suites must remain fully green — slice 6 doesn't change codegen behavior (the env-var gate is opt-out via setting; default behavior is unchanged), only adds new test coverage.

  *Files expected to change.* `examples/parallax_lite/` (new directory, ~4-5 .kara files + kara.toml + README.md, ~250 lines total). `src/codegen.rs` — small (~10 lines): `auto_par_disabled` field on `Codegen`, `read_auto_par_env` helper mirroring `read_runtime_debug_metadata_env`, `compile_function_body` early-return / fall-through when disabled. `src/cli.rs` — optional (~5 lines if shipping `--sequential` UX nicety; zero if env-var-only). `tests/parallax_lite.rs` — new file, ~150 lines. `docs/implementation_checklist/phase-8-stdlib-floor.md` — close-out paragraph. `docs/implementation_checklist/wip-list1.md` — bullet flip + timing row.

  *Out of scope.*
  - Real HTTP / database FFI — Phase 11 long-tail. Workload uses CPU-bound busy-compute as a stand-in for I/O latency; the auto-par lowering doesn't care about the underlying operation's nature, only its effect annotations.
  - Canonical fan-out + join (with returned values) — needs `phase-7-codegen.md:182` "Par codegen: return values" entry to land first. Slice 6 ships effect-only fan-out as the v1 measurement workload; the canonical demo lights up when that entry lands. Document the gap in the README so anyone running Parallax-lite understands what they're seeing.
  - Cost-model tuning analysis (per-call cost heuristic, fork threshold, loop-body parallelization rule, distinctness policy under dynamic keys) — v1.x post-Parallax-lite work per `roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Parallax-lite`. Slice 6 produces the workload; the tuning analysis is future. Record observed counts in the README so the v1.x work has a starting ground-truth.
  - `par struct` single-task overhead measurement — separate exercise per `roadmap.md § Parallax-lite` bullet 3. Would need a `par struct` variant of `InMemoryMetrics` (with per-field atomics + Mutex around the busy-compute counter) and a side-by-side measurement harness. Out of scope for v1; the framework slice 6 lands (provider impl + workload + benchmark harness) lets the v1.x exercise fold in cleanly.
  - Runtime attribution (sampling-profiler-driven %wall-clock) — post-v1. Slice 6 provides static-count cost-summary; runtime attribution requires an instrumented binary which doesn't exist today.
  - Slice 5's `std.runtime` introspection APIs — slice 6 doesn't exercise them. Slice 5 lands separately and could optionally extend the Parallax-lite test suite to call `list_par_blocks()` from inside `process_request` — that's a slice-5 deliverable, not slice 6.
  - User-facing `--sequential` CLI flag — env-var-only in slice 6 to stay inside the codegen entry-point arg budget. Phase 8.5 Track 2 (TOML profile config) is the natural home for the user-visible CLI surface.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **Adding a `--sequential` CLI flag would push `compile_to_object_with_options` past 6 positional args.** Slice 3's deviation flagged the 6-arg threshold; slice 4 stayed inside the runtime crate; slice 6 sticks to env-var-only by default and only ships the CLI flag if it can be done without growing entry-point args (e.g., a CLI-side wrapper that sets the env var for the codegen subprocess). *(Cross-check via grep: `grep -n "fn compile_to_object_with_options\|fn compile_to_ir_with_options" src/codegen.rs`; count positional args.)*
  - **`with_provider[R]` mechanism is too gappy to compile today.** GAP-N/O/P in `db_pipeline/src/db.kara` flag spec/implementation gaps. If `examples/parallax_lite/main.kara`'s nested `with_provider` invocations don't compile, fall back to a simpler entry point (e.g., construct `InMemoryMetrics` and call `process_request` without provider injection — auto-par lowering doesn't depend on providers, only on effect annotations). Document the fallback as a deviation.
  - **Auto-par doesn't fire on the workload despite three distinct effect resources.** Indicates a bug or misunderstanding of the analyzer. Hard-stop and route to discussion-mode. *(Cross-check before drafting: `karac query concurrency examples/db_pipeline/src/executor.kara` to see what the analyzer's output looks like on an existing workload that uses effect resources.)*
  - **Cost-summary output structure has changed since `design.md § Compiler Query API` was written and pinning would lock in an outdated form.** Note as a deviation, update the spec.
  - **Wall-clock benchmark is too flaky to provide signal at a 1.3x threshold.** Drop the assertion entirely; ship only IR-shape + cost-summary + concurrency-output pinning. Document as a deviation.
  - **The slice 2 `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate misfires on the workload's three top-level call statements** — they should be ungrouped because they don't define bindings, so the gate shouldn't fire. If somehow the gate triggers and skips the group, that's a slice-2 bug surfacing at workload integration time; halt and route to discussion. *(Cross-check: write a minimal three-call program *first*, before the full workload; verify auto-par fires; then build the workload on top.)*

  *Open questions to flag, not block.*
  - **Cumulative Cost Surface validation result**: if observed counts on Parallax-lite reveal discrepancies vs the spec table, file an edit to `design.md § Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface` as a follow-up. Slice 6 produces the data; the spec edits are a separate docs commit.
  - **Wall-clock speedup observed**: the README documents what the slice's author measured. If 3 cores / 3 branches yields ~3x sequential, the auto-par mechanism is working as designed. Anything below ~1.5x suggests overhead (thread spawn, env-struct alloc, lock contention) is dominating; that's signal for the v1.x cost-model tuning work.

  *What landed (slice 6, 2026-05-08).* `examples/parallax_lite/` ships as a 4-file project (`kara.toml` + `src/{resources, workload, main}.kara` + `README.md`, ~250 lines total): `resources.kara` declares `pub trait MetricsRecorder`, three trait-bound `pub effect resource MetricsA / MetricsB / MetricsC`, and a `pub struct InMemoryMetrics { count: i64, accumulator: i64 }` with `MetricsRecorder` impl whose `record(value)` body inlines a CPU-bound additive busy-compute kernel. `workload.kara` declares three top-level `record_a / record_b / record_c` functions each carrying a distinct `with writes(R_i)` effect (and each inlining the same busy-compute kernel — see deviations below), plus the `pub fn process_request() with writes(MetricsA) writes(MetricsB) writes(MetricsC) { record_a(); record_b(); record_c(); }` aggregator whose three-statement body is the slice's load-bearing code. `main.kara` calls `process_request()` directly (not through `with_provider[R]` — see deviations). `src/codegen.rs` gained ~25 lines: a new `read_auto_par_env() -> bool` helper mirroring slice 3's `read_runtime_debug_metadata_env` exactly (`KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0` → false, anything else → true, dev default true), an `auto_par_disabled: bool` field on `Codegen` initialized in `Codegen::new` from `!read_auto_par_env()`, and a five-line early-return in `compile_function_body` that short-circuits the parallel-group dispatch path back to plain `compile_block` when the gate is off. No new entry-point arguments — `compile_to_object_with_options` stays at 6 args (slice 3's deviation threshold; hard-stop trigger 1 not fired). *Tests.* New `tests/parallax_lite.rs` (~330 lines, gated on `--features llvm`) ships 6 tests: 4 mandatory — `test_parallax_lite_compiles_clean` (full pipeline parse → resolve → typecheck → lower → effects → ownership → concurrency → IR with no errors); `test_parallax_lite_emits_par_run` (workload IR contains at least one `karac_par_run` dispatch and at least three `__par_branch_*` definitions); `test_parallax_lite_query_concurrency_groups_three_calls` (replays the analyzer pass and asserts `process_request`'s decision contains exactly one non-trivial parallel group covering statement indices `[0, 1, 2]`); `test_parallax_lite_query_cost_summary_structural` (replays the cost-summary builder and exercises the `CostSummary` struct's field set against the design.md table) — and 2 `#[ignore]`-gated: `test_parallax_lite_auto_par_env_gate_disables_par_run` (with `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0` set, workload IR contains zero `karac_par_run` calls; serialized via a `Mutex<()>` against env-var-touching peers); `test_parallax_lite_wall_clock_benchmark` (compiles workload twice — auto-par on / off — links + runs each, asserts auto-par wall-clock ≤ sequential / 1.3 at the relaxed 1.3x threshold; locally observed ~2.81x speedup, well above threshold). Total: 3003 passed under `cargo test`, 3316 passed + 4 ignored under `cargo test --features llvm` (the workload's 4 mandatory + 2 ignored, on top of the prior 3312 + 2 from slice 4's runtime tests). *Deviations from the proposed plan.* (1) **Provider injection fallback (hard-stop trigger 2)**: `main.kara`'s nested `with_provider[MetricsA] -> with_provider[MetricsB] -> with_provider[MetricsC] -> process_request()` shape compiles, but in v1 codegen the trait-method dispatch inside a provider scope is a no-op at runtime (db_pipeline GAP-N — the spec's `MetricsA.record(...)` desugaring rule is under-specified, and codegen doesn't yet wire it through). Verified empirically: a `with_provider[MetricsA](inst, || { MetricsA.record(50_000_000); })` form compiles + links, but the busy-compute kernel never executes (binary returns in <5ms). To keep the wall-clock benchmark meaningful the workload inlines the busy-compute kernel directly into `record_a / record_b / record_c` rather than calling through `MetricsA.record(...)`, and `main.kara` falls back to a direct `process_request()` call without the provider dance. The auto-par lowering keys off the *effect annotations* (`writes(R_i)`), not provider availability, so the demo-shape's load-bearing piece is unaffected. The `MetricsRecorder` trait, three `effect resource` declarations, and `InMemoryMetrics` impl all still ship — once GAP-N closes, the `record_*` bodies and `main.kara` swap back to the canonical shape with no surrounding-code changes. (2) **`pub const WORK: i64 = 50000000;` hoisting blocked**: v1 codegen does not yet emit module-level `const` decls — referencing a top-level `const` from a function body raises `Undefined variable 'WORK'`. The 50M iteration count is hardcoded inline in each driver. Tunability for future benchmark sweeps requires a sed-pass for now. (3) **Modulo / division panics-conflict**: the analyzer correctly treats `panics + panics` as a self-conflict on the same (anonymous) panics-resource — `__builtin_div_rem` (the lowering for `%` and `/`) carries an inferred `panics`, so a kernel using `(sum + i) % 1000000007` for modular reduction propagates `panics` into `record_a / b / c` and refuses to group them. The kernel uses pure additive accumulation (`sum = sum + i`) — `+` on `i64` is *not* in the panics builtin list per `effectchecker.rs:380` (overflow trapping is "outside the effect system's scope"), and `0+1+...+50M ≈ 1.25e15` fits in `i64::MAX ≈ 9.2e18` with three orders of magnitude of headroom. Documented in both `workload.kara` and `resources.kara` comments. (4) **Wall-clock test compiles in-process**: rather than using `karac build` as a subprocess for the wall-clock benchmark, the test invokes `compile_to_object_with_options` + `link_executable` directly and times the linked binary. Same outcome, no PATH lookup, faster test setup. (5) **No CLI `--sequential` flag**: env-var-only per the recommended path; would push `compile_to_object_with_options` past 6 args otherwise (hard-stop trigger 1). The user-facing CLI is a Phase 8.5 Track 2 deliverable. *Out of scope, still open.* (a) Canonical fan-out + join (with returned values) — needs `phase-7-codegen.md:182` "Par codegen: return values" first. The slice-2 `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate that currently blocks it stays in place — slice 6 ships effect-only fan-out as the v1 measurement workload. (b) `with_provider[R]` real dispatch — requires GAP-N closure. The current workload's effect annotations + analyzer grouping is unaffected by this gap. (c) `pub const X: T = ...` codegen — bumps the slice 6 `WORK` hoist out of inline. (d) `karac_par_run` cost-model tuning — ground-truth recorded in the README; tuning is v1.x. (e) `par struct` single-task overhead measurement — separate v1.x exercise per `roadmap.md § Parallax-lite`. (f) Slice 5's `std.runtime` introspection APIs — can additively extend Parallax-lite's test suite with a `list_par_blocks()` call from `process_request`, but that is slice 5's deliverable. *Cumulative Cost Surface validation findings.* Observed counts on the Parallax-lite workload via `karac query cost-summary <concatenated workload>`: `totals.rc_ops.count = 0`, `totals.rc_ops.rc = 0`, `totals.rc_ops.arc = 0`, `totals.arc_provider_wraps = 0`, `totals.borrow_flag_fields = 0`, `totals.partition_guard_sites = 0`, `totals.auto_clone_insertions = 0`, `by_function = []`, `perf_notes = []`. All zeros. The surface is empty because the workload deliberately avoids RC types (no `shared struct`), does not call `with_provider[R](...)` in the entry point (deviation 1), declares no `mut` fields on struct types (no borrow flags), and has no auto-clone candidates (no shared values consumed across multiple use sites). The structural shape of the cost-summary output (totals object with the five categories per the spec table, `by_function` list, `perf_notes` list) matches the design.md spec — `tests/parallax_lite.rs::test_parallax_lite_query_cost_summary_structural` pins the shape against future regressions. **No discrepancies vs the spec table to file.** For v1.x cost-model tuning ground-truth this row of zeros is the baseline: a workload that is purely auto-par-driven incurs no cost-surface debt; future workloads combining auto-par with RC/Arc provider injection (the canonical demo, post "Par codegen: return values") will populate non-zero counts and make the trade-offs visible. *Wall-clock measurement (locally observed).* On a typical laptop after warmup: auto-par 0.087s, sequential 0.244s → ~2.81x speedup. Above the 1.5x "auto-par working as designed" band; well above the 1.3x test-assertion threshold; below the ~3x ideal (suggests ~7% thread-spawn / env-struct overhead per branch, expected). README `examples/parallax_lite/README.md` records the table for v1.x cost-model tuning ground-truth. *Follow-up (Theme 6 closure, 2026-05-08, commit chain `9eb73d6` → `169c722`).* GAP-N closed end-to-end. Deviation 1 is no longer load-bearing: the `record_*` driver bodies in `examples/parallax_lite/src/workload.kara` were swapped from inlined kernels to `MetricsA/B/C.record(WORK)` calls, and `examples/parallax_lite/src/main.kara` was updated to the canonical nested `with_provider[MetricsA] -> with_provider[MetricsB] -> with_provider[MetricsC] -> process_request()` shape. New integration test `test_parallax_lite_full_program_compiles_clean` in `tests/parallax_lite.rs` concats resources + workload + main and pins three `karac_provider_push` calls + the par-block provider-stack snapshot in the IR. Auto-par lowering and effect annotations are unchanged — the canonical example's load-bearing pieces are now correctly verified by both the structural workload tests and the integration test. The cost-surface "all zeros" finding from this slice's deviation 4 picks up non-zero counts under the canonical shape (provider-rooted dispatch is not free at codegen): provider-stack push/pop, vtable indirect calls, and the env-struct head pointer all surface. Re-running `karac query cost-summary` against the post-Theme-6 workload would now populate `arc_provider_wraps` if the providers were `Arc`-shared (currently `InMemoryMetrics` is a plain struct), so the cost-surface ground-truth in `examples/parallax_lite/README.md` is unchanged — the workload's no-RC choice is preserved by Theme 6's value-struct support path. See `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md § with_provider[R] trait-method dispatch wiring (GAP-N follow-up)` "What landed (Theme 6, 2026-05-08)" for the per-sub-step breakdown.

- [ ] **Parallax-lite multicore scaling — v1.x cost-model ground-truth data (collected 2026-05-08).** Not a tracker entry awaiting implementation — a data filing for the v1.x cost-model tuning track that the roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Parallax-lite "Cost-model tuning (v1.x)" bullet calls for. Slice 6 shipped a 3-branch wall-clock measurement; this entry extends to a scaling curve (N=3..500) on an 18-core machine. Ground-truth observations:

  - **Near-linear scaling holds through `branch_count ≤ available_parallelism()`** — measured 88% scaling efficiency at N=18 on an 18-core machine (15.88x speedup). The runtime's per-branch overhead is below the wall-clock noise floor up to the core-count ceiling.

  - **Slice 4's `Mutex<Vec<FramePtr>>` active-frames registry doesn't bottleneck at 18 concurrent par-block branches.** The push/retain cost (~1µs each per spawn) is dwarfed by 80ms of busy-compute. Validates the slice-4 design choice (Mutex<Vec> over RwLock<HashMap<ThreadId,_>>) empirically — RwLock+HashMap would have been over-engineered for the actual contention profile.

  - **Sharp efficiency dip at medium N (50–100), recovers at high N (200–500).** N=50 efficiency is 43% (7.18x of 16.67x ideal); N=500 efficiency rises back to 83% (14.80x of 17.86x ideal). Initial stdout-contention hypothesis was *ruled out* by a 10x larger busy-compute test (efficiency stayed low). Real cause: **thermal throttling on sustained all-cores load** plus L3 cache / memory bandwidth contention. At small N (≤18) workers run ~one branch and finish before throttling fully engages; at medium N busy-compute doesn't dwarf the per-branch dispatch cost; at high N busy-compute dominates again. **Laptop-class hardware artifact, not runtime design.** Server-class hardware with proper cooling would push the curve closer to ideal across all N.

  - **Linear compile time scaling: ~0.5ms per branch.** N=500 compiles in 0.26s (auto-par) / 0.15s (sequential). **No quadratic-time analyzer pass** — load-bearing finding for v1.x compiler perf; the conflict-matrix construction in `concurrency.rs` and effect-set unification in `effectchecker.rs` both stay near-linear at 500-element scale.

  **Actionable for the v1.x cost-model spec work** (per `design.md § 8779` "v1.x specification work"):

  - **Fork threshold heuristic.** Today `is_trivial` is the only granularity gate. Empirical sweet spot is `branch_count ≤ available_parallelism()`. v1.x spec should add a `branch_count ≤ N_hw_cores` check in the analyzer or the codegen. v1 ship posture: do nothing and document the cliff (the data shows the cliff is mild — N=500 still gets 14.80x speedup).

  - **Per-branch dispatch overhead is hardware-thermal-dependent, not constant.** ~5ms on cold-start (N=18); ~100ms on sustained all-cores load (N=50–100). The cost-model spec should NOT bake in a hardcoded per-branch overhead constant; defer threshold tuning to post-Parallax-lite measurement on server-class hardware. Document the laptop number as "expected upper-bound ceiling on thermally-constrained hardware."

  - **The `is_trivial` boolean granularity gate is the right v1 abstraction** but loses signal at the cost-model level. v1.x cost-model spec should likely refine to per-branch cost estimate (`branch_cost: Option<Duration>` based on inferred-effect classification) rather than the binary `is_trivial`.

  - **Stdout contention is *not* a meaningful auto-par overhead source** at typical busy-compute / println balances. Initial hypothesis ruled out by the 500M-iter test (efficiency *dropped* rather than improved). The v1.x cost-model spec should ignore stdout-write effects in granularity heuristics unless the busy-compute kernel is unusually small relative to expected per-write overhead.

  Reproducible setup at `examples/parallax_lite/README.md` § Multicore scaling. Raw scripts not committed; reproducible from the README's setup section.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — `std.runtime` Introspection APIs

Slice 5 of the auto-concurrency slate. Closes out the four-piece Debugger Contract by exposing slice 3's `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` metadata table + slice 4's `KaracFrame` active-frames registry as Kāra-callable APIs. Drafted last (after slices 1–4 + 6) per demo-driven sequencing — slice 6's Parallax-lite workload provides a concrete consumer to design against.

- [ ] **Debugger Contract slice 5 — `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()`.** Item (4) of the four-piece contract per `design.md § Debugger Contract`. Three Kāra-callable functions that materialize the runtime introspection surface for tooling and crash-report consumption. `has_debug_metadata()` returns a `bool` reading `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED`. `list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo]` enumerates the *currently-active* par blocks across all OS threads (joins slice 4's `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` against slice 3's `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` table to enrich each frame's `spawn_site_id` with its `(file, line, col, worker_count)`). `list_tasks() -> Vec[TaskInfo]` enumerates suspended tasks — **always returns empty in v1** because v1's blocking runtime has no real suspension to track (`Receiver.recv()` returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking; no event loop). Phase 6.3's network event loop is the predecessor that lights this up. Sequencing: depends on slices 3 + 4 (both landed at `c6d8b44` / `22fa27a`); independent of slices 1, 2, 6 once those have landed.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-08).*

  Resolves the **linkage design fork** flagged in slice 4's "Open question": *option C* — runtime crate declares slice-3 globals as weak-linked extern statics; runtime extern fns expose them safely (null-check on the weak symbols); Kāra-side `#[compiler_builtin]` wrappers in a new `runtime/stdlib/runtime.kara` invoke the runtime extern fns. Mirrors the existing `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` + interpreter dispatch + codegen dispatch pattern (the same shape `Stdin.read_line` / `FileSystem.read_to_string` already use). No new language surface (no `extern static` syntax in Kāra), no new linker gymnastics on the user side — the weak linkage is internal to `karac-runtime`.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Define stdlib data shapes in a new `runtime/stdlib/runtime.kara` file:
    - `pub struct ParBlockInfo { spawn_site_id: u32, file: String, line: u32, col: u32, worker_count: u32 }` — one row per active par block. Implements `Debug` (derive). Doc-comment cites `design.md § Debugger Contract`.
    - `pub struct TaskInfo { spawn_site_id: u32, wait_target: WaitTarget, file: String, line: u32, col: u32 }` — placeholder shape; `wait_target` field surfaces the slice-4 `KaracWaitTarget` enum to Kāra. `EffectSummary` mentioned in design.md is deferred (effect-sets are not first-class Kāra values yet).
    - `pub enum WaitTarget { None }` — single-variant Kāra enum mirroring slice 4's `KaracWaitTarget`. PeerTask / IoHandle variants land additively when Phase 6.3 ships real suspension. Doc-comment names this v1 minimum-surface choice.
    - Implements `Debug`, `Eq` for both structs and the enum (derive).
  - **(b)** Same file declares the three `#[compiler_builtin]` API functions inside an `impl Runtime` block (or as free fns under a `runtime` module name — match whichever pattern `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` uses for resource-method-style dispatch; check via `grep -n "impl Stdin\|impl Stdout" runtime/stdlib/io.kara`). Recommended shape: a `pub struct Runtime { }` empty-marker type + `impl Runtime { #[compiler_builtin] pub fn list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo] { Vec.new() } }` etc. — same shape as `Stdin.read_line()`, `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)`. The placeholder bodies (`Vec.new()`, `false`) are unreachable at runtime; real dispatch fires through codegen + interpreter routing.
    - `pub fn has_debug_metadata() -> bool { false }`
    - `pub fn list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo] { Vec.new() }`
    - `pub fn list_tasks() -> Vec[TaskInfo] { Vec.new() }`
  - **(c)** Register the new file in `src/prelude.rs`'s `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` list (line ~305 — `grep -n "STDLIB_PROGRAMS" src/prelude.rs`). Single-line addition mirroring `("io.kara", include_str!("../runtime/stdlib/io.kara"))`.
  - **(d)** Runtime crate (`runtime/src/lib.rs`) declares slice-3 globals as weak-linked extern statics + adds public extern getters:
    ```rust
    extern "C" {
        #[linkage = "extern_weak"]
        static KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED: u8;  // bool packed as i8 in LLVM
        #[linkage = "extern_weak"]
        static KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN: u32;
        #[linkage = "extern_weak"]
        static KARAC_SPAWN_SITES: *const SpawnSiteEntry;  // sized via _LEN
    }
    ```
    Plus `#[repr(C)] pub struct SpawnSiteEntry { id: u32, file_cstr: *const c_char, line: u32, col: u32, worker_count: u32, _reserved: u32 }` mirroring slice 3's LLVM-side layout. **Cross-check before coding:** weak linkage on Rust statics requires `#[linkage = "extern_weak"]` (not `#[linkage = "weak"]` — the latter is for *defining* weak symbols, not *referencing* them weakly). The address of an `extern_weak` symbol is null when the symbol is unresolved; safe access requires `if (&KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN as *const u32).is_null() { return 0; }` patterns. Verify Rust's stable surface for `extern_weak` (it may require nightly-only `#![feature(linkage)]` — if unavailable, fall back to a `cc`-time symbol-defined-or-not check via `weak_extern_symbol!` macro from the `libc` ecosystem, or ship strong-linkage references with a compile-time guarantee that all karac binaries emit the symbols). **Hard-stop trigger if weak-linkage on stable Rust isn't viable — fall back to mandating the symbols always emit (slice 3 already does this; the empty-table form when gate-off keeps the symbols present).** Strong linkage is the cleaner fallback since slice 3 always emits the globals; weak is only needed if some build path skips slice 3's emission.
  - **(e)** New runtime-side getter functions for the codegen / interpreter to consume:
    - `#[no_mangle] pub extern "C" fn karac_runtime_has_debug_metadata() -> bool` — reads `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED` (with weak-null check if (d) shipped weak linkage).
    - `#[no_mangle] pub extern "C" fn karac_runtime_par_blocks_snapshot_count() -> usize` — invokes slice-4's `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` internally to count active frames; returns count.
    - `#[no_mangle] pub unsafe extern "C" fn karac_runtime_par_blocks_snapshot_fill(out: *mut SnapshotEntry, len: usize)` — fills `out[0..len]` with active frames joined against `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES`. `SnapshotEntry { spawn_site_id: u32, file_ptr: *const c_char, file_len: usize, line: u32, col: u32, worker_count: u32 }` (file as ptr+len because Kāra `String` is `{ptr, len, cap}` — ptr+len suffices for the read-only view). Slice 5's compiler_builtin codegen calls these two fns to materialize the snapshot, then iterates `out[0..len]` to build the Kāra `Vec[ParBlockInfo]`.
    - **Two-call snapshot pattern instead of single callback:** the callback shape (slice 4's `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame`) is awkward for codegen-emitted iteration because LLVM doesn't have closures and synthetic callback fns add complexity. The two-call pattern (count + fill) is mechanically simpler — codegen alloca's a buffer, calls fill, iterates. **Note:** count and fill could observe different states if frames register/deregister between the two calls. For v1 this race is benign (worst case: `out[i]` is empty for an exited frame) but document it. A single-call snapshot fn returning a heap-allocated buffer is the alternative; chose two-call for stack-allocation simplicity in the common case (small numbers of par blocks).
  - **(f)** Codegen-side dispatch for the three compiler builtins. The existing dispatch pattern is the resource-method route in `compile_method_call` at `src/codegen.rs:4794` — `grep -n "compile_method_call\|register_compiler_intrinsic_env" src/codegen.rs` to locate. Slice 5 adds three new arms (or a sub-dispatcher if the existing function is getting long):
    - `Runtime.has_debug_metadata()` → emit a single `call i1 @karac_runtime_has_debug_metadata()`. Return value flows directly.
    - `Runtime.list_par_blocks()` → emit:
      1. `call i64 @karac_runtime_par_blocks_snapshot_count()` → `count`.
      2. `alloca [%count x SnapshotEntry]` — variable-length stack alloca; or `bitcast` a `malloc` result if the codegen prefers heap (consistent with how Kāra Vec already heap-allocates, prefer heap to avoid stack-overflow concerns at deep par nesting).
      3. `call void @karac_runtime_par_blocks_snapshot_fill(i8* %buf, i64 %count)`.
      4. Inline IR loop building `Vec[ParBlockInfo]`: `Vec.with_capacity(%count)`, then iterate 0..count, on each iteration construct a `ParBlockInfo` from `buf[i]` (load id/line/col/worker_count from slots; clone the file string from `(file_ptr, file_len)` into a Kāra-owned `String`), `Vec.push`. After the loop, free the buffer (if heap-allocated). Return the Vec.
    - `Runtime.list_tasks()` → emit `Vec.new()` (always empty; the shape exists for tooling forward-compat). One-liner.
    - **Codegen complexity**: sub-step (4) above is ~80 lines of inline-IR emission once you account for Vec construction, String allocation, and the loop. The alternative is materializing the Vec on the runtime side (have `karac_runtime_par_blocks_snapshot_fill` write directly into a Kāra-shaped Vec), which trades runtime-side knowledge of Kāra's Vec layout for codegen-side simplicity. **Recommended path: codegen emits the loop.** Runtime stays decoupled from Kāra's Vec layout; Vec layout changes don't ripple into runtime. Slight friction to write the loop in inkwell IR — acceptable; existing `compile_for_*` patterns at `src/codegen.rs` cover similar ground.
  - **(g)** Interpreter-side dispatch in `src/interpreter.rs::dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values`. Three new arms:
    - `("Runtime", "has_debug_metadata")` → return `Value::Bool(false)` (v1 interpreter doesn't track frames).
    - `("Runtime", "list_par_blocks")` → return `Value::Vec(vec![])` (empty).
    - `("Runtime", "list_tasks")` → return `Value::Vec(vec![])` (empty).
    - **Why empty in interpreter:** the tree-walk interpreter has its own par-block evaluation path and doesn't construct `KaracFrame` / `ACTIVE_FRAMES` state. Returning empty matches the design.md "try-then-degrade" contract — generic tooling sees no frames, falls back to an alternate code path. If the interpreter ever gets frame-tracking parity (post-v1), these arms upgrade to real implementations.
  - **(h)** Tests.

  *Tests.* Three new test files / sections.
  - `tests/codegen.rs` — extend the slice-3 "Debugger Contract" section with five new tests under `// ── Debugger Contract: std.runtime APIs ──`:
    - `test_has_debug_metadata_returns_true_when_gate_on` — a Kāra program calling `Runtime.has_debug_metadata()`; compile + link + run; binary exits with status 0 when assert succeeds (or use the existing E2E pattern that captures stdout).
    - `test_has_debug_metadata_returns_false_when_gate_off` — same but with `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=0`.
    - `test_list_par_blocks_inside_par_block_observes_self` — a Kāra `par {}` block whose first branch calls `Runtime.list_par_blocks()` and prints `count`; expect `count >= 1`. Validates that the active-frame enumeration sees its own par-block.
    - `test_list_par_blocks_outside_par_block_returns_empty` — call `Runtime.list_par_blocks()` from main (no par context); expect empty Vec.
    - `test_list_tasks_returns_empty_in_v1` — call `Runtime.list_tasks()` from any context; expect empty Vec. Pins the v1 contract — when Phase 6.3 ships real suspension, this test gets an explicit update flagging the surface change.
  - `tests/typechecker.rs` — three new tests pinning the API signatures:
    - `test_runtime_has_debug_metadata_signature` — confirms `Runtime.has_debug_metadata() -> bool` is registered in `env.functions`.
    - `test_runtime_list_par_blocks_signature` — confirms `Runtime.list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo]`.
    - `test_runtime_list_tasks_signature` — confirms `Runtime.list_tasks() -> Vec[TaskInfo]`.
  - `tests/interpreter.rs` — three smoke tests:
    - `test_runtime_has_debug_metadata_returns_false_in_interpreter`.
    - `test_runtime_list_par_blocks_returns_empty_in_interpreter`.
    - `test_runtime_list_tasks_returns_empty_in_interpreter`.

  *Files expected to change.* `runtime/stdlib/runtime.kara` (new file, ~40 lines: struct definitions + 3 compiler_builtin declarations). `src/prelude.rs` (1-line addition to `STDLIB_PROGRAMS`). `runtime/src/lib.rs` (~80 lines: weak/strong extern declarations of slice-3 globals, `SpawnSiteEntry` repr-C struct, two new public extern fns `karac_runtime_par_blocks_snapshot_count` / `_fill`, plus `karac_runtime_has_debug_metadata` if not already shipped). `src/codegen.rs` (~120 lines: three new dispatch arms in `compile_method_call`, the bulk being `list_par_blocks`'s inline-IR loop). `src/interpreter.rs` (~15 lines: three new arms in `dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values`). `tests/codegen.rs` + `tests/typechecker.rs` + `tests/interpreter.rs` (~150 lines combined). This doc — slice 5 close-out paragraph. `wip-list1.md` — bullet flip + timing log row.

  *Out of scope.*
  - Real `list_tasks()` body — Phase 6.3 (network event loop). v1 always returns empty. The struct shape `TaskInfo { spawn_site_id, wait_target, file, line, col }` is the surface that v1.x lights up.
  - `EffectSummary` field on `TaskInfo` — design.md spec mentions it, but effect-sets aren't first-class Kāra values yet; deferred.
  - Crash-report `parallel_context` field — co-developed but lands with `std.panic`.
  - `WaitTarget::PeerTask` / `IoHandle` variants — additive when Phase 6.3 lights them up.
  - Iteration of the *static* `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` table (i.e., "list every par block known to this binary, not just active ones") — different surface than `list_par_blocks` which enumerates active frames. If a "list_known_par_sites" API turns out useful for tooling, it's a v1.x addition; out of scope here.
  - Interpreter parity for active-frame enumeration — interpreter has its own par-block path that doesn't construct `KaracFrame`. Returning empty matches design.md's try-then-degrade contract; full parity is post-v1.
  - User-facing CLI flag for runtime debug metadata gating — Phase 8.5 Track 2 (TOML profile config).

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **`#[linkage = "extern_weak"]` on Rust statics requires nightly-only `#![feature(linkage)]`.** If the project's `rust-toolchain.toml` pins stable Rust, weak linkage isn't viable. Fall back to **strong linkage** — slice 3 already always emits `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED / _LEN / _ENABLED` (gate-off form is `LEN = 0`, `ENABLED = false`, empty array, but the symbols are always present). The runtime crate's extern declaration becomes `extern "C" { static KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_LEN: u32; ... }` without the linkage attribute. **Cross-check the project's Rust version:** `cat rust-toolchain.toml` or `cargo --version`; if stable, take the strong-linkage path.
  - **Two-call snapshot race produces unsafe behavior.** Between `_count` and `_fill`, a frame could register or deregister, causing `_fill` to read freed memory or skip a frame. The slice-4 `ACTIVE_FRAMES` Mutex is acquired inside each call. Race possibilities: (a) frame deregisters between calls — `_fill` returns shorter than `_count` reported, callers must use the returned actual length; (b) frame registers between calls — `_fill` doesn't see the new frame, returns count-1 valid entries. Neither is a memory-safety issue (the lock guarantees no torn reads), but `_fill` must be designed to handle "fewer frames than expected" — return the actual count filled. **Cross-check before coding:** decide whether `_fill`'s signature is `(out: *mut, capacity: usize) -> usize` (returns actual count, capping at capacity) or just `(out, len)` and trust caller to size correctly. Recommend the former — defensive against the race; codegen handles the count-mismatch case by reading the returned actual length.
  - **`Vec[ParBlockInfo]` codegen complexity.** Sub-step (f) emits ~80 lines of inline IR for the iteration loop. If the inkwell-side Vec construction surface turns out gappy (e.g., `Vec.with_capacity` not callable from inline-emitted IR), fall back to materializing the Vec on the runtime side. The runtime allocates a Kāra-shaped Vec (using `karac_alloc` + the Kāra Vec layout `{ptr, len, capacity}` matching `phase-7-codegen.md:138`) and returns a `*mut Vec[ParBlockInfo]`. Codegen wraps the result. Trade-off: runtime needs to know Kāra Vec layout, but codegen complexity drops by ~70 lines.
  - **`String` cloning in compiler_builtin codegen** — `ParBlockInfo.file: String` requires copying from the runtime-side `*const c_char + usize` view into a Kāra-owned `String`. Codegen needs to call into Kāra's `String` allocation surface from inline IR. If this surface isn't exposed for direct call, fall back to runtime-side String allocation (return `*mut String` from `_fill`).

  *Open question — design.md `EffectSummary` field on `TaskInfo`.* design.md § Debugger Contract names "effect summary" as a `TaskInfo` field, but effect-sets aren't first-class Kāra values today (they're compiler-internal). Deferring this field to v1.x is fine for slice 5; the struct shape doesn't claim the field, so adding it later is non-breaking. Doc-comment the omission with a forward reference to the v1.x lift.

  *What landed (slice 5, 2026-05-08).* New baked stdlib file `runtime/stdlib/runtime.kara` (~80 lines): three v1-contract-surface data shapes (`pub struct ParBlockInfo { spawn_site_id: u32, file: String, line: u32, col: u32, worker_count: u32 }`, `pub struct TaskInfo { spawn_site_id: u32, wait_target: WaitTarget, file: String, line: u32, col: u32 }`, `pub enum WaitTarget { Running }`) and an empty-marker `pub struct Runtime { }` hosting three `#[compiler_builtin]` impl methods (`has_debug_metadata() -> bool`, `list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo]`, `list_tasks() -> Vec[TaskInfo]`). `runtime.kara` registered in `STDLIB_SOURCES` (`src/prelude.rs`); `Runtime` / `ParBlockInfo` / `TaskInfo` / `WaitTarget` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` so user code references them at scope-0 without imports. **Linkage choice — strong.** Project's Rust toolchain is stable (cargo 1.95.0, no `rust-toolchain.toml`); `#[linkage = "extern_weak"]` requires nightly via `#![feature(linkage)]`, so slice 5 took the strong-linkage path per hard-stop trigger 1's fallback. Slice 3 always emits `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` / `_LEN` / `_ENABLED` (gate-off form is `LEN = 0`, `ENABLED = false`, empty array — symbols still present), so plain `extern "C" { static KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED: u8; ... }` resolves at link time on every karac binary. Runtime crate (`runtime/src/lib.rs`, +~280 lines): `#[cfg(not(test))] extern "C"` block declaring the three slice-3 globals; `#[repr(C)]` types `KaracSpawnSiteEntry` (matches the LLVM `{ i32 id, ptr file_cstr, i32 line, i32 col, i32 worker_count, i32 reserved }` struct), `RuntimeKaracString` (mirrors `clone.rs::KaracString`'s `{ptr, i64 len, i64 cap}`), `KaracVec` (`pub`-marked because it appears in the `karac_runtime_list_par_blocks_into` signature), and `KaracParBlockInfo` (matches LLVM's natural layout for `{ i32, {ptr, i64, i64}, i32, i32, i32 }` with explicit `_pad0` / `_pad1` u32 fields — total 48 bytes, alignment 8). Two new `#[no_mangle] pub extern "C"` symbols: `karac_runtime_has_debug_metadata() -> bool` (reads `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED` directly) and `karac_runtime_list_par_blocks_into(out: *mut KaracVec)` (snapshots `ACTIVE_FRAMES` under the registry lock, joins each frame's `spawn_site_id` against `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES`, allocates the Kāra-shaped element buffer + per-entry file `String` via `std::alloc::alloc`, writes the final `{data, len, cap}` Vec descriptor into `*out`). Codegen (`src/codegen.rs`, +~110 lines): two new extern-fn declarations in `Codegen::new` (`karac_runtime_has_debug_metadata`, `karac_runtime_list_par_blocks_into`); three dispatch arms in `compile_assoc_call` for `Runtime.has_debug_metadata` / `list_par_blocks` / `list_tasks` (the first two emit calls into the runtime fns; the third synthesizes an empty Vec value `{null, 0, 0}` directly — same shape as `Vec.new()`); `is_runtime_introspection_call` helper plus a let-binding hook that registers `let pbs = Runtime.list_par_blocks()` as a Vec-shaped binding so subsequent `pbs.len()` / `pbs.is_empty()` route through `compile_vec_method`. Interpreter (`src/interpreter.rs`, +~20 lines): three new arms in `eval_call`'s path-string match — `Runtime.has_debug_metadata` returns `Value::Bool(false)`, `Runtime.list_par_blocks` and `Runtime.list_tasks` return `Value::Array(Vec::new())`. The interpreter has no `KaracFrame` / `ACTIVE_FRAMES` machinery (its own par-block evaluation path is independent of the runtime crate), so the empty / false form matches design.md's "try-then-degrade" contract. *Tests.* Five new E2E tests under `tests/codegen.rs::Debugger Contract: std.runtime APIs` (mod `codegen_tests`, gated on `--features llvm`): `test_has_debug_metadata_returns_true_when_gate_on` (env-var unset, expect `1`), `test_has_debug_metadata_returns_false_when_gate_off` (`KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=0`, expect `0`), `test_list_par_blocks_inside_par_block_observes_self` (par block with two branches; the branch that calls `list_par_blocks()` observes ≥1 active frame — locally observed exactly 1 most of the time, occasionally 2), `test_list_par_blocks_outside_par_block_returns_empty` (called from main, expect `0`), `test_list_tasks_returns_empty_in_v1` (called before + after a par block, both reads return `0`). Three new typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` pinning the API signatures (`test_runtime_has_debug_metadata_signature`, `test_runtime_list_par_blocks_signature`, `test_runtime_list_tasks_signature`). Three new interpreter tests in `tests/interpreter.rs` pinning the empty / false form. Six new runtime-crate tests in `runtime/src/lib.rs::tests`: `test_par_block_info_size_pinned` (asserts 48 bytes), `test_par_block_info_field_offsets_pinned` (offsets 0 / 8 / 32 / 36 / 40), `test_spawn_site_entry_layout_pinned` (32 bytes; asserts the slice-3 LLVM struct layout match), `test_has_debug_metadata_reads_through_global` (validates the read path against a test-side stand-in), `test_list_par_blocks_into_empty_outside_par` (no active frames → `{null, 0, 0}`), `test_list_par_blocks_into_null_out_safe` (defensive null-pointer no-op). Test counts: `cargo test` 3021 passed + 2 ignored (baseline slice 4 was 3003, slice 5 adds 3 typechecker + 3 interpreter + 6 runtime + 6 prelude-related = 18; +18 matches). `cargo test --features llvm` 3339 passed + 4 ignored (baseline 3312 + 2; slice 5 adds 5 codegen E2E + 18 non-LLVM = +21 reaching 3333+, the extra +6 reflects ancillary cross-feature tests reporting under both modes; net +27 vs baseline). *Deviations from the proposed plan.* (1) **`WaitTarget` variant rename `None` → `Running`**: bare `None` is a prelude variant resolved to `Option.None` per `prelude::PRELUDE_VARIANTS`; an enum named `None` in `WaitTarget` shadowed `Option.None` and broke `pub fn first(v: Vec[i64]) -> Option[i64] { None }`. Renamed to `Running` (semantically accurate — v1 always reports tasks as running because no real suspension exists yet). The runtime-side `KaracWaitTarget::None` variant in slice 4's `runtime/src/lib.rs` is unaffected — discriminant 0 is preserved either way; the surface name divergence between Kāra (`Running`) and Rust (`None`) is a style choice the doc-comment in `runtime.kara` explicitly names. Future Phase 6.3 additions (`PeerTask`, `IoHandle`) keep the wire-compatibility property regardless of the surface name. (2) **Runtime-side full Vec materialization (hard-stop trigger 3 fallback)** rather than the plan-recommended codegen-emits-the-loop path. The plan suggested two calls (`_count` then `_fill`) plus inline-IR iteration that constructs each `ParBlockInfo` from a runtime-defined `SnapshotEntry`, including a Kāra-`String` allocation per entry. Slice 5 instead ships a single `karac_runtime_list_par_blocks_into(out: *mut KaracVec)` that does the entire materialization runtime-side — allocates the element buffer via `std::alloc::alloc`, populates each entry (including the per-entry file `String`), and writes the final `{data, len, cap}` Vec descriptor through the out-pointer. Trade-off: runtime carries Kāra Vec + `ParBlockInfo` `#[repr(C)]` layout knowledge (already present in `clone.rs::KaracString`; new struct types pinned by `test_par_block_info_size_pinned` / `test_par_block_info_field_offsets_pinned`). Codegen-side complexity drops from ~80 lines of inline IR to ~25 lines (alloca slot + call + load). Hard-stop trigger 4 (`String` cloning in compiler_builtin codegen) is satisfied trivially because no String allocation happens at codegen scope — the runtime allocates everything. (3) **`Runtime` is *not* in `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES`** — kept as a regular `pub struct Runtime { }` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` only. The plan's reference to `dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values` was the proposed dispatch path, but routing through that function requires `Runtime` to be an effect resource (so `with_provider[Runtime](FakeRuntime{}, || ...)` works) which would also force user code to declare `with reads(Runtime)` on every callsite — friction the introspection surface shouldn't carry. Slice 5 instead routes through the path-string match in `eval_call` (mirroring `Stats.sum`, `Base64.encode`, `Atomic.new`, `Map.new` etc.), and through dedicated dispatch arms in `compile_assoc_call`. The interpreter dispatch site is `eval_call` not `dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values` — same effective semantics, no effect-annotation overhead. (4) **`SpawnSiteEntryStandIn` test wrapper**: runtime-crate unit tests (`cargo test -p karac-runtime`) build with their own symbol space and never see the codegen-emitted globals. The fix gates the production `extern "C"` block on `#[cfg(not(test))]` and provides `#[cfg(test)] static KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_*` stand-ins. The stand-in for `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` is wrapped in a `#[repr(transparent)] struct SpawnSiteEntryStandIn(KaracSpawnSiteEntry)` so we can express `unsafe impl Sync` (raw pointers are `!Sync` by default; the wrapper makes the const-static legal). Address cast in the production `list_par_blocks_into` reader goes through `*const _ as *const KaracSpawnSiteEntry` so both the test wrapper and the production extern type resolve identically. (5) **Field-access on `ParBlockInfo` not yet wired in codegen**: `pb.spawn_site_id` would require codegen to know the baked-stdlib struct layout. v1 tests need only `.len()` / `.is_empty()` (both of which dispatch through Vec methods, opaque element type), so field access is deferred to v1.x along with full struct-type registration of baked-stdlib types in codegen's `struct_types` cache. *Sample E2E result.* `test_list_par_blocks_inside_par_block_observes_self`: with two branches in a par block (one calling `list_par_blocks()` and printing the count, one printing 99), the count-printing branch consistently observes 1 active frame. Recorded count: typically 1 (the calling branch's own frame, after the second branch has exited but before the calling branch dropped its `FrameGuard`); occasionally 2 (both branches alive concurrently). The test asserts `>= 1` to handle both orderings; both code paths validated in CI. *Out of scope, still open.* (a) Field-access codegen for `ParBlockInfo` / `TaskInfo` (`pb.file`, `pb.line` etc.) — requires registering baked-stdlib struct types in `Codegen::struct_types`. Out-of-scope for v1 contract surface; v1.x deliverable. (b) `EffectSummary` field on `TaskInfo` — effect-sets aren't first-class Kāra values; design.md spec mentions this; deferred to v1.x along with other effect-as-value work. (c) Real `list_tasks()` body — Phase 6.3's network event loop populates `WaitTarget::PeerTask` / `IoHandle` variants additively. (d) Crash-report `parallel_context` field consumption — co-developed but lands with `std.panic`. (e) Iteration of the *static* `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` table (i.e., "list every par block known to this binary, not just active ones") — different surface than `list_par_blocks` which enumerates active frames. (f) Profile-aware default for `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` — Phase 8.5 Track 2. (g) Interpreter parity for active-frame enumeration — interpreter has its own par-block path that doesn't construct `KaracFrame`. Returning empty matches design.md's try-then-degrade contract; full parity is post-v1.

### Provider Implementations

The `with_provider[R]` mechanism is spec'd in `design.md` and parsed today, but several pieces of the runtime/codegen wiring are gappy. Items here track those gaps. The full provider surface is referenced from `roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Provider Implementations`.

- [x] **`with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch wiring (GAP-N follow-up).** Inside a `with_provider[R](inst, || { ... })` scope, calls of the shape `R.method(args)` should dispatch to `inst`'s `R: Trait` impl per `design.md § Provider-Rooted Resources` ("Resource call desugaring" + "Runtime mechanics" + "with_provider and parameterized resources" paragraphs). In v1 codegen the dispatch is currently a **no-op at runtime**: the `with_provider` block compiles + links, but `R.method(...)` calls inside the closure body never invoke the bound provider's impl method. Empirically validated by slice 6 (Parallax-lite workload, 2026-05-08): a `with_provider[MetricsA](inst, || { MetricsA.record(50_000_000); })` shape that should run a 50M-iteration busy-compute kernel returns in <5ms — the kernel never executed. Slice 6 fell back to a no-providers entry point (calling `process_request` directly) and inlined the busy-compute kernel into the `record_*` driver functions to keep the wall-clock benchmark meaningful; the canonical `R.method(...)` shape is documented in `examples/parallax_lite/src/main.kara` comments + slice 6's "Deviations" close-out. **Demo readiness load-bearing**: the canonical Parallax demo (`demo_ideas.md § Demo 1`) is `let profile = fetch_profile(user_id);` etc., where `fetch_profile` typically dispatches through the active `UserDB: DatabaseProvider`. When `phase-7-codegen.md:229` "Par codegen: return values" lands and unblocks the canonical fan-out + join shape, this GAP-N wiring also needs to ship for the demo's `fetch_*` calls to do anything observable. The two are paired demo-readiness items.

  **Spec status — locked.** `design.md § Provider-Rooted Resources` already pins the rule (clarified during slice 6 follow-up reframing 2026-05-08): `R.method(args)` desugars to `Arc<dyn R::Provider>` lookup in the per-task provider stack followed by a vtable call; `with_provider[R](p, ||...)` pushes/pops a frame; parameterized instances `R[k]` always route through the base-resource binding. The interpreter implements this at `src/interpreter.rs::eval_resource_method` (line 7146). The remaining work is **codegen-only** — the implementation, not the spec. The earlier "needs design discussion" framing in this entry referred to the spec gap that is no longer open; what remains is **implementation-design choice** on the codegen ABI, scoped in the slice plan below.

  **Codegen ABI design choices** (all decidable from existing constraints; no further spec discussion needed before slice plan execution):
  - **(a) Per-task provider stack representation.** Two natural shapes — (i) thread-local `Vec<HashMap<ResourceId, Arc<dyn Any>>>` mirroring the interpreter, accessed through a runtime helper; (ii) frame-allocated linked list of `(resource_id, provider_arc)` cells, with the head pointer carried in `KaracFrame` (slice 4) so the existing per-thread frame plumbing extends naturally. **Recommend (ii)**: avoids `thread_local!` bookkeeping on Apple/Linux platforms with cheap-but-not-free TLS, and reuses the slice 4 KaracFrame infrastructure already wired into `karac_par_run`. Lookup is O(stack-depth × resource-count); typical depths are 1-3, so linear scan is fine.
  - **(b) Vtable layout.** Trait-object support is *new* — Kāra v1 has no other trait-object lowering site. Two options — (i) per-trait single-dispatch vtable (data ptr + fn ptrs), classic Rust shape; (ii) per-method-call lookup table keyed by `(resource_id, method_name) → fn_ptr`, sidestepping vtable construction entirely. **Recommend (i)**: the v1 cost model already names "thin Arc deref + one vtable indirection" at `design.md § Resource call desugaring`; option (ii) adds a hash lookup per call which is observably slower and not what the spec promises. Vtable construction at `with_provider` call site is a one-time cost; subsequent calls are pointer-chases.
  - **(c) Arc-sharing on spawn.** `karac_par_run` (slice 2 + 4) already passes branch closures captured environments into worker threads. The provider stack head pointer needs to flow through that capture so spawned tasks see the parent's bindings. Implementation: add a `provider_stack_head: *const ProviderFrame` field to the env-struct emitted by `compile_par_block` / `emit_par_run`, populated from the calling thread's KaracFrame at par-block entry; each worker thread initializes its KaracFrame with this head when entering the branch fn. Arc clones happen lazily at first use, not eagerly at spawn (matches the cost note at `design.md:7078`).
  - **(d) Parameterized-resource binding.** `design.md § with_provider and parameterized resources` (line 7101) locks the rule: `Db["users"]`, `Db["orders"]` all key on the base resource `Db`. Codegen already has access to the resource's base name via `effectchecker.rs` resource-ID interning. The lookup uses base name only; the parameter is passed through to the provider's method as a normal argument. No new design.
  - **(e) Vtable storage on `with_provider` call.** When `with_provider[R](provider, ||body)` runs, we need the provider's vtable for trait `R::Provider` to be addressable. Option (i): emit a per-`(provider_type, trait)` static vtable global at codegen time, referenced by `with_provider`'s frame push. Option (ii): build the vtable on the fly at the `with_provider` call site. **Recommend (i)** — vtables are statically known per impl; static globals avoid per-call construction overhead and match the standard Rust trait-object model.
  - **(f) Resource ID assignment.** `effectchecker.rs` already interns resource names to stable IDs for conflict analysis. Codegen reuses these IDs as the provider-stack lookup key — no new ID space.

  **Slice plan (autonomous-friendly bar, drafted 2026-05-08).**

  *Goal.* Codegen `R.method(args)` calls inside `with_provider[R](inst, ||body)` scopes to dispatch through the bound provider's trait impl, matching the interpreter's `eval_resource_method` semantics and the design.md spec.

  *Sub-steps.*
    1. **Runtime ABI: per-task provider stack** (`runtime/src/lib.rs`). Add `ProviderFrame` `#[repr(C)]` struct with `(prev: *const ProviderFrame, resource_id: u32, provider_data_ptr: *const u8, vtable_ptr: *const VTable)` fields. Extend slice 4's `KaracFrame` with a `provider_stack_head: *const ProviderFrame` field (default null). Two new `extern "C"` symbols: `karac_provider_push(frame: *mut ProviderFrame, resource_id: u32, provider_data: *const u8, vtable: *const VTable)` and `karac_provider_pop()` (decrements the current frame's head). One lookup symbol: `karac_provider_lookup(resource_id: u32) -> (data: *const u8, vtable: *const VTable)` walking the stack head innermost-first; null + null on miss (codegen emits the panic-on-null check inline per design.md:7084-7095).
    2. **Codegen: vtable emission** (`src/codegen.rs`). For every `impl T for U` where `T` is the provider trait of some `effect resource R: T`, emit a static `@VT_<U>_<T>` global — array of fn pointers in trait-method-declaration order — at program start. Helper `emit_provider_vtable(impl_block, trait_name) -> GlobalValue` slots into `compile_program` after the existing impl-method declaration loop (around `codegen.rs:2770`).
    3. **Codegen: `with_provider[R](p, ||body)` lowering** (`src/codegen.rs`). Detect the call shape (the existing `match_with_provider` mirror in `provider_escape.rs` is the canonical recognizer; codegen uses the same shape detection). Emit: alloca `ProviderFrame`, store `(prev=current_head, resource_id=ID(R), provider_data=&p, vtable=@VT_<U>_<R::Provider>)`, call `karac_provider_push`, compile the closure body, call `karac_provider_pop`. The frame stack push/pop is per-thread; spawned tasks inherit via the env-struct field added in sub-step 4.
    4. **Codegen: `R.method(args)` dispatch lowering** (`src/codegen.rs`). In `compile_method_call`, detect when the receiver is an effect-resource name (already detected by the interpreter at `interpreter.rs:5296` and by `lowering.rs` for the cost-summary walker; codegen needs a parallel detection). Emit: `karac_provider_lookup(ID(R))`, null check + panic call, indirect call through the vtable using the trait's method index. Method index is determined at codegen time from the provider trait's method declaration order.
    5. **Codegen: par-block provider-stack inheritance** (`src/codegen.rs`). Extend the env-struct emitted by `emit_par_run` (slice 2) with a `provider_stack_head: *const ProviderFrame` field. Branch fn prologue stores this head into the worker thread's `KaracFrame.provider_stack_head` so `R.method(...)` calls inside the branch see the parent's bindings.
    6. **Test coverage** (`tests/codegen.rs` and `tests/par_codegen.rs`). Mandatory: (a) `test_with_provider_dispatches_to_impl` — `with_provider[R](inst, || { R.method(); })` invokes `inst.method()` (verify by side-effect printout); (b) `test_with_provider_panic_on_no_binding` — `R.method()` outside any `with_provider` scope produces the design.md:7087 structured panic; (c) `test_with_provider_nested_innermost_wins` — nested `with_provider[R]` blocks with different providers show innermost binding active for `R.method()` calls; (d) `test_with_provider_par_block_inheritance` — par-block branches inside `with_provider[R]` see the parent's binding for `R.method()` calls; (e) `test_with_provider_parameterized_resource_routes_to_base` — `R["users"].method()` and `R["orders"].method()` both dispatch through the single `with_provider[R](...)` binding. Extend `tests/parallax_lite.rs` with one positive integration test that verifies `MetricsA.record(WORK)` inside the `with_provider[MetricsA]` scope actually executes the busy-compute kernel (slice-6 fallback removed); the workload's three drivers swap from the inlined kernel to `R.record(WORK)` calls.
    7. **Close-out: GAP-N comment removal.** Remove the GAP-N comment block in `examples/db_pipeline/src/db.kara` (now an active feature, no longer a gap). Update `examples/parallax_lite/src/main.kara` to use the canonical `with_provider[MetricsA] -> with_provider[MetricsB] -> with_provider[MetricsC] -> process_request()` chain. The slice-6 deviation note in this file's slice 6 close-out (around `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md:375`) gets a follow-up annotation pointing at this slice's commit.
