  *Files expected to change.* `runtime/src/lib.rs` (+~80 lines: ProviderFrame, push/pop/lookup symbols, KaracFrame extension), `src/codegen.rs` (+~200 lines: vtable emission, with_provider lowering, dispatch lowering, env-struct field for par-block inheritance), `tests/codegen.rs` (+~120 lines: 5 mandatory tests), `tests/parallax_lite.rs` (+~30 lines: integration test), `examples/db_pipeline/src/db.kara` (GAP-N comment removed), `examples/parallax_lite/src/{main, workload}.kara` (canonical provider chain restored).

  *Out of scope (tracked separately).* (a) Cancellation propagation through provider boundaries — `phase-7-codegen.md` "Par codegen: cancellation and error propagation" carries this. (b) `providers { R => p } in { ... }` block syntax (the multi-resource sugar over `with_provider`) — separate parser/lowering item if not already present. (c) Provider-rooted resource escape diagnostics — `provider_escape.rs` already implements; codegen's job is to honor what escape analysis already enforces. (d) Per-call vtable inlining optimization — v1.x cost-model work; the design.md cost note explicitly endorses the indirect-call cost as the v1 model.

  *Hard-stop triggers.* (1) If the existing `match_with_provider` recognizer in `provider_escape.rs` doesn't cover all syntactic shapes the parser actually produces (e.g., chained `with_provider` calls in the same statement), parser/AST work expands beyond this slice — stop and file a parser-side prerequisite. (2) If trait-method ordering is not stable across pipeline passes (`typechecker.rs` may reorder for ambiguity reasons), method-index assignment becomes ambiguous — stop and pin trait-method order at AST level before this slice. (3) If `KaracFrame`'s field set as shipped in slice 4 doesn't allow extension without breaking the slice-3 spawn-site metadata layout, stop and file a runtime-ABI prerequisite. (4) If more than ~5 pre-existing tests need fixture-level updates due to provider-call sites changing behavior, stop and reassess scope. **Sequencing recommendation:** land `phase-7-codegen.md:229` "Par codegen: return values" first — without it, the canonical Parallax demo's fan-out + join shape is still blocked even after this slice ships. Either order works for B's mechanical correctness, but the demo punchline needs both.

  State: **plan drafted to autonomous-friendly bar 2026-05-08, ready for delegation when prioritized.** Pairs with `phase-7-codegen.md:229` for canonical Parallax demo readiness.

  *What landed (Theme 6, 2026-05-08).* All seven sub-steps shipped end-to-end in commit chain `9eb73d6` (sub-step 1 — runtime ABI: `ProviderFrame` `#[repr(C)]` + push/pop/lookup/get_stack_head/set_stack_head externs + 4 unit tests; defers `KaracFrame.provider_stack_head` field in favor of TLS `PROVIDER_STACK_HEAD` thread-local — see deviation 1) → `d37a214` (sub-step 2 — `@VT_<U>_<T>` static vtable emission per `impl T for U` where `T` is bound to some `effect resource R: T`, 3 structural tests) → `9ed72c9` (prerequisite — ref-self / mut-ref-self method codegen: `make_impl_method_function` preserves source self mode, `compile_field_store` mutates through ref-param pointers, `compile_method_call` passes pointer when first param is ptr-typed, 3 regression tests; this prerequisite was not anticipated in the original slice plan but was discovered to be load-bearing for sub-step 4 dispatch — `mut ref self` impl methods need their first param to be `*const Self`) → `fc18457` (sub-step 3 — `with_provider[R](p, ||body)` lowering: alloca `ProviderFrame` + push + inline closure body + pop, with provider data pointer materialized differently for shared-struct vs value-type-struct providers, 3 structural tests) → `ff18bab` (sub-step 4 — `R.method(args)` dispatch: `karac_provider_lookup` + extractvalue + GEP + indirect call through vtable, with method index from trait-declaration order; FunctionType borrowed from any concrete `<U>.<method>` symbol via `provider_method_fn_type`; 3 structural + 1 e2e test verifying `mut ref self` mutation persists round-trip through the runtime stack) → `7d0d462` (sub-step 5 — par-block inheritance: env-struct trailing slot is `*const ProviderFrame`, snapshotted via `karac_provider_get_stack_head` at par-block entry and seeded via `karac_provider_set_stack_head` in each branch fn prologue, 1 structural + 1 e2e test) → `ef11808` (sub-step 6 — nested innermost-wins e2e test) → `169c722` (sub-step 7 — `examples/parallax_lite/src/workload.kara` swaps inlined kernels for `MetricsA/B/C.record(WORK)` calls, `examples/parallax_lite/src/main.kara` wraps `process_request()` in three nested `with_provider[MetricsA/B/C]` scopes, `examples/db_pipeline/src/db.kara` GAP-N marked CLOSED with the commit chain cited; new integration test `test_parallax_lite_full_program_compiles_clean` concats resources + workload + main and pins 3 push calls + provider-stack snapshot in the IR). Total: ~750 LoC across `runtime/src/lib.rs`, `src/codegen.rs`, `tests/codegen.rs`, `tests/parallax_lite.rs`, plus the three example files. *Tests.* 297 codegen tests pass (4 new structural + 3 e2e for Theme 6 directly, on top of the 290 pre-existing); 15 par_codegen tests pass (no regressions); 5 active parallax_lite tests pass (1 new full-program integration test + 4 pre-existing); full suite green across all 30+ test files; `cargo clippy --all --tests -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean. *Deviations from the plan.* (1) **TLS-backed head pointer instead of `KaracFrame.provider_stack_head`** (sub-step 1). The plan recommended carrying the head pointer in `KaracFrame` to avoid `thread_local!` overhead, but root tasks (no par-block) have no `KaracFrame` — `karac_par_run` is the only site that allocates one, so a `KaracFrame`-only approach would either fail for root-task `with_provider` or require allocating a stub `KaracFrame` at every program entry. A thread-local works uniformly for root and spawned tasks; the per-`R.method()` cost is one TLS read, well within the cost model `design.md` already names ("thin Arc deref + one vtable indirection"). Cross-task inheritance flows through the env-struct snapshot mechanism documented in sub-step 5. Hard-stop trigger 3 (KaracFrame extension breaking slice-3 metadata layout) avoided by sidestepping the extension entirely. (2) **Ref-self / mut-ref-self codegen prerequisite** not in the original plan; discovered to be load-bearing for sub-step 4 (the canonical `fn record(mut ref self, value: i64)` shape needs `*const Self` first param, but `make_impl_method_function` was synthesizing self as value-typed regardless of source mode). Resolved as a standalone slice (`9ed72c9`) before sub-step 3+4 to keep the prerequisite reviewable in isolation. (3) **Panic-on-no-binding deferred** (sub-step 6 (b) test). The runtime returns `(null, null)` when the resource isn't found; codegen would null-deref on the vtable load. The typechecker's effect-checker enforces `R` is in scope at every call site, so the null path can't normally reach codegen — adding a defensive structured-panic emission stays a follow-up. (4) **Parameterized-resource binding deferred** (sub-step 6 (e) test). `effect resource R[T]: Trait[T]` is generic-resource ABI work; out of v1 scope, separate from the GAP-N closure. (5) **`provider_method_fn_type` lookup pattern** (sub-step 4): instead of stashing FunctionType per (trait, method) at vtable emission time (which would have added a new HashMap field), the dispatch site borrows the type from any concrete `<U>.<method>` symbol whose `(U, T)` pair is registered in `provider_vtables`. All impls of the same trait method share the same lowered LLVM signature, so any one will do — avoids new state for a one-off lookup. (6) **`emit_provider_vtables` reordered** (sub-step 3 follow-on): originally placed after function-body compilation, but body compilation may include `with_provider[R]` call sites that need the vtable global to already exist in `provider_vtables` for the lookup at lowering time. Moved to run after impl-method declaration but before any body compilation; bodies don't need to be compiled yet because the vtable only references fn-ptr symbols established by `declare_function`. *Out of scope, still open.* (a) Panic-on-no-binding structured panic emission (deviation 3) — defensive runtime check; pairs with the typechecker's effect-checker invariant. (b) Parameterized resources (deviation 4) — generic-resource ABI; separate spec piece. (c) Cancellation propagation through provider boundaries — `phase-7-codegen.md` "Par codegen: cancellation and error propagation" carries this. (d) `providers { R => p } in { ... }` block syntax (multi-resource sugar) — separate parser/lowering item if not already present. (e) Per-call vtable inlining optimization — v1.x cost-model work.

- [x] **Typed effect resources + in-memory providers + canonical `get_dashboard` workload (full Parallax demo, Slice C).** The demo's load-bearing source artifact: four typed effect resources (`UserDB / OrderDB / NotifDB / RecommendDB`), four single-method provider traits returning typed result data (`fetch_profile -> Profile`, `fetch_recent_orders -> Vec[Order]`, `fetch_notifications -> Vec[Notification]`, `fetch_recommendations -> Vec[Recommendation]`), four in-memory provider impls (`InMemoryUserDB / InMemoryOrderDB / InMemoryNotifDB / InMemoryRecommendDB`), and the canonical `get_dashboard(user_id)` workload — four `let` bindings into typed return values, joined into a `Dashboard { profile, orders, notif, recommended }` result struct. Lives at `examples/parallax/` (sibling to `examples/parallax_lite/`). The combined workload exercises the integration of two recently-landed mechanisms in one place: Theme 6's `with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch for the per-call routing, and Slice A's per-branch return slots for the four-way fan-out+join. Each was test-covered independently at landing time; this slice is the first source artifact that puts them together end-to-end. **Demo readiness:** pairs with Slice B (HTTP server FFI) for the `serve_http` entry point and Slice E (benchmark harness) for the side-by-side compare; the workload itself ships standalone and can be benchmarked directly via `cargo run --release` before B/E land.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-09) — Full Parallax demo: typed-resource providers + canonical workload.*

  Author the typed-resource side of the Parallax demo: data types, traits, resources, in-memory providers, workload, and the four-deep `with_provider[R]` chain that wires them together at the entry point. Mirror parallax-lite's `examples/parallax_lite/src/` shape (kara.toml + per-concern `.kara` files) but with **typed return values** instead of effect-only fan-out, exercising Slice A's per-branch return slots through the canonical fan-out+join shape that the demo storyboard reads against. **Locked design choices (2026-05-09):** (i) **C1: four single-method traits** — `UserDatabase / OrderDatabase / NotificationDatabase / RecommendationDatabase`, each with exactly one fetch method returning typed data. Rejected: collapse into one big trait (loses the resource-disjointness story; the four-resource conflict-table cell is the auto-par grouping signal). (ii) **C2: in-memory providers with per-fetch busy-compute kernel** mirroring parallax-lite's `InMemoryMetrics` pattern — each provider holds pre-populated test data and a CPU-bound additive accumulator loop sized to the provider's "simulated I/O latency" (e.g. profile=10M iters, orders=30M, notifs=15M, recommended=20M). The runtime exposes no sleep primitive today; busy-compute is the standing precedent (parallax-lite README:ll.10-14, resources.kara:ll.42-54). (iii) **C3: receiver mode `ref self`** on each fetch method — read-only by the trait spec (each fetch is a `reads(R)` effect, not `writes(R)`); `ref self` is the right receiver mode and is now codegen-supported (Theme 6 prerequisite commit `9ed72c9`). (iv) **C4: data types as plain `struct`s, not `shared struct`** — no RC overhead; each fetched value is owned, moves into the parent's let-binding through Slice A's return slot. The `Dashboard` aggregator is also a plain owned struct. (v) **C5: a single fixed `user_id = 42` test fixture** — no parameterization sweep in the workload; provider impls return canned data keyed on the input id; the canned data is sufficient to verify both "the right provider got called" and "the right value flowed through Slice A's return slot." (vi) **C6: four-deep nested `with_provider` at `main`** — `with_provider[UserDB](u, || with_provider[OrderDB](o, || with_provider[NotifDB](n, || with_provider[RecommendDB](r, || { ... })))))`. Theme 6 closed with three-deep parallax-lite nesting; four-deep is the additive extension and exercises the runtime's TLS-backed `PROVIDER_STACK_HEAD` walk one frame deeper.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Scaffold `examples/parallax/` (sibling to `examples/parallax_lite/`). Files: `kara.toml` (mirror parallax-lite's; `name = "parallax"`, `edition = "2026"`, no deps), `src/types.kara`, `src/traits.kara`, `src/resources.kara`, `src/providers.kara`, `src/workload.kara`, `src/main.kara`. Concrete file split chosen for review legibility (each file is single-concern); the test-side concat helper drops `import` lines as parallax-lite's `tests/parallax_lite.rs::workload_source()` already does, so multi-file project-mode codegen gaps don't block the e2e tests.
  - **(b)** `src/types.kara` — declare the five owned data types: `Profile { user_id: i64, name: String, email: String }`, `Order { order_id: i64, total_cents: i64 }`, `Notification { kind: i64, message: String }`, `Recommendation { item_id: i64, score: f64 }`, `Dashboard { profile: Profile, orders: Vec[Order], notif: Vec[Notification], recommended: Vec[Recommendation] }`. All plain `struct`, no `shared struct`. Each carries primitive + String / Vec aggregates — these are the exact shapes Slice A's return slots ship the values back through; if any field shape doesn't round-trip cleanly through the slot ABI, hard-stop trigger (1) fires.
  - **(c)** `src/traits.kara` — declare four single-method traits: `pub trait UserDatabase { fn fetch_profile(ref self, user_id: i64) -> Profile; }` and the three peers (`fetch_recent_orders -> Vec[Order]`, `fetch_notifications -> Vec[Notification]`, `fetch_recommendations -> Vec[Recommendation]`). Each method takes `ref self` (read-only receiver) + a `user_id: i64` arg, returns the typed result. No effect annotations on the trait method signatures — effects flow from the resource binding, not the impl.
  - **(d)** `src/resources.kara` — declare the four effect resources bound to their respective traits: `pub effect resource UserDB: UserDatabase;` and three peers. Single line each; mirror parallax-lite's `resources.kara` line 23-25 shape exactly.
  - **(e)** `src/providers.kara` — declare the four in-memory provider structs (`pub struct InMemoryUserDB { ... }` etc.), each carrying pre-populated test data (e.g. `InMemoryUserDB` holds a hardcoded `Profile { user_id: 42, name: "Alice", email: "alice@example.com" }`; `InMemoryOrderDB` holds `Vec[Order]` with two-three test orders). Each impl has a `pub fn new() -> Self` constructor. The four `impl <Trait> for InMemory<Trait>` blocks define each `fetch_*` method's body as: (i) busy-compute kernel of fixed iteration count proportional to the provider's "simulated I/O latency" (use `pub const FETCH_PROFILE_WORK: i64 = 10_000_000;` etc. — same style as parallax-lite's `pub const WORK: i64`); (ii) construct + return the typed result from the provider's pre-populated data, keyed on the `user_id` arg (single-key fixture per design lock C5). The busy-compute kernel uses additive-only arithmetic to stay panics-free per parallax-lite's effect-conflict gotcha (`workload.kara:ll.45-50` warning).
  - **(f)** `src/workload.kara` — author the canonical `get_dashboard`:
    ```kara
    pub fn get_dashboard(user_id: i64) -> Dashboard
        with reads(UserDB) reads(OrderDB) reads(NotifDB) reads(RecommendDB)
    {
        let profile = UserDB.fetch_profile(user_id);
        let orders = OrderDB.fetch_recent_orders(user_id);
        let notif = NotifDB.fetch_notifications(user_id);
        let recommended = RecommendDB.fetch_recommendations(user_id);
        Dashboard { profile, orders, notif, recommended }
    }
    ```
    Four `let` bindings into typed return values feeding a tail expression that constructs the `Dashboard`. The auto-par analyzer's existing rules group all four `let` statements into a single non-trivial `parallel_group` (no data dependencies between the four fetches; `reads(R_i)` on disjoint resources is conflict-free). Slice A's `compute_return_slots` walks the group and materializes a four-field `__karac_ParGroup_<spawn_site_id>_Returns` struct sized to `(Profile, Vec[Order], Vec[Notification], Vec[Recommendation])`. Each branch fn writes its produced value to its slot; the parent reads four values back after the `karac_par_run` barrier and the tail expression's `Dashboard { ... }` constructor reads the resulting in-scope bindings. **This is the exact source shape parallax-lite's README calls out as the gap that Slice A unblocks** (`examples/parallax_lite/README.md:ll.36-54`).
  - **(g)** `src/main.kara` — entry point with the four-deep `with_provider` chain plus a smoke-test invocation:
    ```kara
    import providers.{InMemoryUserDB, InMemoryOrderDB, InMemoryNotifDB, InMemoryRecommendDB};
    import resources.{UserDB, OrderDB, NotifDB, RecommendDB};
    import workload.get_dashboard;

    fn main() {
        let mut u = InMemoryUserDB.new();
        let mut o = InMemoryOrderDB.new();
        let mut n = InMemoryNotifDB.new();
        let mut r = InMemoryRecommendDB.new();
        with_provider[UserDB](u, || {
            with_provider[OrderDB](o, || {
                with_provider[NotifDB](n, || {
                    with_provider[RecommendDB](r, || {
                        let dashboard = get_dashboard(42);
                        println("got dashboard");
                    });
                });
            });
        });
    }
    ```
    The `let mut <provider>` declarations are required because Theme 6's lowering walks the binding's `mut`/non-`mut` mode for the alloca shape; the runtime treats each provider as borrowed for the duration of the closure scope. (Cross-check: parallax-lite's `main.kara:ll.22-31` uses `let mut pa` for `InMemoryMetrics`; same pattern.)
  - **(h)** Tests in new `tests/parallax.rs` (mirror `tests/parallax_lite.rs`'s layout: top-level `#[cfg(feature = "llvm")]` mod gating; `workload_source()` helper that concatenates `types.kara` + `traits.kara` + `resources.kara` + `providers.kara` + `workload.kara` + `main.kara`, dropping `import` lines). Required tests:
    1. `test_parallax_compiles_clean` — workload typechecks + effect-checks + ownership-checks + concurrency-analyzes + codegens cleanly through the in-process pipeline. Pins the source against regressions in any phase.
    2. `test_parallax_emits_par_run_for_four_lets` — `get_dashboard`'s body emits exactly one `karac_par_run` dispatch with four branch fns (`__par_branch_0_0..3` modulo prior par sites). Asserts the analyzer grouped all four `let` bindings into one parallel_group and Slice A's path materialized four return slots.
    3. `test_parallax_query_concurrency_groups_four_calls` — replays the analyzer pass and asserts the `get_dashboard` decision contains a single non-trivial `ParallelGroup` covering statement indices 0-3 (the four `let`s); the tail expression `Dashboard { ... }` is statement index 4 and is *not* in the group (joins on the four bindings; the analyzer's binding-flow check correctly excludes it from the parallel set). Reason field is prose-shaped per Slice D's renderer expectation.
    4. `test_parallax_provider_chain_dispatches_innermost_wins` — e2e: builds the binary and runs it; the four `fetch_*` methods write a side-channel marker (e.g. `println("fetch_profile called")` per impl) so stdout shows all four impls were invoked exactly once. Verifies the four-deep `with_provider` chain correctly threads each resource's binding through to its dispatch site.
    5. `test_parallax_get_dashboard_returns_complete_struct` — e2e: runs the binary, asserts stdout contains the canned data round-tripped through the full pipeline (profile name, order count, etc.). Pins that Slice A's return-slot reads match the branch fns' writes.
    6. `test_parallax_concurrency_report_renders_dashboard_workload` — pairs with Slice D's renderer; runs `karac build --concurrency-report` over the workload source, snapshot-compares stdout against a new `tests/snapshots/concurrency_report_parallax.txt` golden showing the four-call parallel group with the four `reads(R_i)` per call and the analyzer's reason verbatim. Cross-references Slice D's renderer for prose-shape stability.
    7. `test_parallax_wall_clock_benchmark` — `#[ignore]`-gated (single-run timing flaky on shared CI). Compiles the workload twice (auto-par on / off via `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0`), runs each, asserts auto-par wall-clock ≤ sequential / 2.0 (relaxed threshold; per-fetch busy-compute totals ~75M iters across the four fetches, so a 3-4-core machine should clear ~3x in practice).
    Optional eighth test if scope permits: `test_parallax_dashboard_with_default_user_id_42` — verifies the canned-data fixture independent of the auto-par path (sequential codegen path with `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0`; assert the resulting struct matches expected). Lets future fixture changes catch test-data drift.

  *Files expected to change.* New files: `examples/parallax/kara.toml` (~10 lines), `examples/parallax/src/types.kara` (~30 lines), `examples/parallax/src/traits.kara` (~20 lines), `examples/parallax/src/resources.kara` (~10 lines), `examples/parallax/src/providers.kara` (~150 lines — four impl blocks + four busy-compute kernels + four pre-populated data fixtures), `examples/parallax/src/workload.kara` (~30 lines), `examples/parallax/src/main.kara` (~25 lines), `tests/parallax.rs` (~300 lines — 6-7 tests + concat helper), `tests/snapshots/concurrency_report_parallax.txt` (~15 lines — golden file for test 6). Modified files: this doc — flip slice status after landing and add a "What landed" close-out paragraph; `wip-list1.md` / `wip-staging.md` — promotion + close-out per the staging discipline. Total ~600 LoC new + small doc updates.

  *Out of scope.*
  - **Real DB FFI** (Postgres / MySQL / Redis) — Phase 11 long-tail. Each provider's `fetch_*` is in-memory + busy-compute simulation; real-DB swap is post-v1.
  - **JSON serialization of `Dashboard`** — Slice F territory. The demo's storyboard wants `Response.json(dashboard)` ergonomics, but that's the HTTP wiring; this slice ships the typed struct, not its serialization.
  - **HTTP entry point** (`serve_http(addr, handler)`) — Slice B. The `main.kara` here is a CLI driver, not an HTTP server. Slice B's wiring sample (sub-step (g) in the std.http entry above) calls `get_dashboard(user_id)` from inside its handler; the wiring lands when both slices are present.
  - **Side-by-side benchmark harness vs Go / Node.js** — Slice E. The wall-clock test in (h.7) is the local speedup signal; the recordable demo artifact is Slice E's three-implementation race.
  - **Concurrency-report renderer polish** — Slice D landed. Test 6 above is the integration cross-check, not new renderer work.
  - **Cancellation propagation through provider boundaries** — `phase-7-codegen.md` "Par codegen: cancellation and error propagation" carries this.
  - **Parameterized providers** (`UserDB[tenant_id]`) — Theme 6 deviation 4 deferred this; out of v1 scope.
  - **Real I/O simulation via sleep primitives** — runtime exposes no sleep today (per parallax-lite README); busy-compute kernel is the v1 fallback. If a sleep primitive lands later, providers swap in additively.
  - **`#[derive(Debug)]` / `#[derive(Eq)]` on the data types** — debug printing in the e2e tests uses explicit `println` statements with hand-formatted strings; auto-derive is post-v1.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **Slice A's per-branch return slots reject one of the four return shapes.** The four return types span `Profile` (struct of i64 + String + String), `Vec[Order]` (Vec of struct), `Vec[Notification]`, `Vec[Recommendation]`. Slice A's `compute_return_slots` was test-covered for primitives + a small struct return; if any of the four shapes (especially the nested `Vec[Struct]`) doesn't round-trip cleanly through the slot's ABI, halt and either (a) write a smaller integration test in `tests/par_codegen.rs` first that exercises the failing shape standalone (e.g. `let v = make_vec_of_orders();` inside an auto-par group), then file a Slice A follow-up, or (b) reduce the test fixture to shapes Slice A demonstrably handles (e.g. swap `Vec[Order]` for a fixed-size `Order` and document the deviation). **Default fallback: (a)** — the smaller integration test at the par_codegen level is the right reproduction surface; Slice A's mechanism is recent enough that finding the shape gap is a real expected outcome.
  - **Theme 6's `with_provider[R]` lowering breaks at four-deep nesting.** Theme 6 closed with three-deep parallax-lite nesting; four-deep is additive but unverified. The TLS-backed `PROVIDER_STACK_HEAD` walk is depth-agnostic on paper, so this is unlikely to break — but if it does, halt and either (a) write a smaller four-deep test in `tests/codegen.rs` standalone, then file a Theme 6 follow-up, or (b) flatten the chain by introducing a `providers { UserDB => u, OrderDB => o, NotifDB => n, RecommendDB => r } in { ... }` block syntax (the Theme 6 close-out's "out of scope, still open (d)" item). **Default fallback: (a)** — additive nesting depth is the cleanest fix.
  - **Trait-method dispatch through `karac_provider_lookup` interacts unexpectedly with per-branch return slots.** Theme 6 verified `R.method()` returning `()` in single-thread context (3-deep nest) and across `karac_par_run` branches via `karac_provider_set_stack_head` in branch fn prologues. Slice A verified return slots work with non-resource-method calls. The combination — `R.method() -> Profile` inside a branch that writes to a return slot — is unverified. Halt if the combination fails and either (a) write a tighter standalone test in `tests/par_codegen.rs` (e.g. one resource binding + one branch returning the resource method's result), then file a follow-up, or (b) inline the resource-method bodies into the workload functions, sacrificing the dispatch story but preserving the demo's fan-out story. **Default fallback: (a)** — the standalone reproduction is the right surface to pin the bug.
  - **Multi-file project-mode codegen still gaps.** Parallax-lite's README acknowledges multi-file project-mode build is typecheck-only; full codegen across modules is CR-24. The tests already concat-and-compile per parallax-lite precedent; if `cargo run --release` from inside `examples/parallax/` doesn't actually emit a binary, that's expected, not a hard-stop. Halt only if the concat-and-compile path itself fails (parser couldn't reconstruct the workload). **Default fallback: ship without `cargo run` working;** document the concat-and-compile pattern in a per-example `README.md` matching parallax-lite's.
  - **More than ~5 pre-existing tests need fixture-level updates due to new resources or syntax.** Each new resource declaration and provider impl shouldn't perturb other tests — they're isolated under `examples/parallax/`. If they do (e.g. some integration test walks all of `examples/` and a new resource trips a case), halt and reassess scope. **Default fallback:** scope-fence the tests under `tests/parallax.rs::parallax_tests` mod and gate behind `#[cfg(feature = "llvm")]` so non-llvm test runs don't observe the new fixture.

  State: **plan drafted to autonomous-friendly bar 2026-05-09.** Theme 6 prerequisite has cleared (closed `49a9a2e` 2026-05-08 with full seven-sub-step commit chain through `9eb73d6` → ... → `169c722`); Slice A return-slots prerequisite has cleared (closed `ab611d3` 2026-05-08, verified at the four-shape integration level via Slice A's own `tests/par_codegen.rs::test_auto_par_with_returns_runs_concurrently_and_joins_correctly`). All staging promotion criteria (plan drafted + prereqs fired + no design forks open) met; ready for promotion to wip-list1 in a follow-up commit.

  *What landed (Slice C, 2026-05-09).* Authored the typed-resource side of the full Parallax demo end-to-end as a single contained slice commit: `examples/parallax/` with kara.toml + the six per-concern source files (`types.kara`, `traits.kara`, `resources.kara`, `providers.kara`, `workload.kara`, `main.kara`) and a per-example README mirroring parallax-lite's. The four typed effect resources (`UserDB`, `OrderDB`, `NotifDB`, `RecommendDB`) bind to four single-method `*Database` traits with `ref self` receivers per design lock C3; four in-memory `InMemory*DB` providers carry busy-compute kernels sized 10M / 30M / 15M / 20M iters per fetch (additive-only arithmetic per the parallax-lite panics-conflict gotcha), each with a unique String tag-field shape so the codegen's LLVM-struct-identity reverse lookup in `let mut <provider> = InMemory*DB.new()` resolves each binding to the right type name. The canonical `get_dashboard(user_id)` workload's four `let` bindings auto-parallelize into a single `parallel_group` and Slice A's `compute_return_slots` materializes a four-field `__karac_ParGroup_0_Returns` struct sized to `(Profile, Order, Notification, Recommendation)`. The four-deep nested `with_provider[R]` chain in `main.kara` exercises Theme 6's TLS-backed `PROVIDER_STACK_HEAD` walk one frame deeper than parallax-lite — verified by `test_parallax_provider_chain_dispatches_innermost_wins` (each `fetch_*` impl emits its side-channel marker exactly once). The Slice D concurrency-report renderer surfaces `get_dashboard`'s four-call group with `reads(R_i)` per call — pinned by `tests/snapshots/concurrency_report_parallax.txt`.

  *Tests.* 6 new tests in `tests/parallax.rs` (`test_parallax_compiles_clean`, `test_parallax_emits_par_run_for_four_lets`, `test_parallax_query_concurrency_groups_four_calls`, `test_parallax_provider_chain_dispatches_innermost_wins`, `test_parallax_get_dashboard_completes_e2e`, `test_parallax_concurrency_report_renders_dashboard_workload`) plus 1 `#[ignore]`-gated wall-clock benchmark (`test_parallax_wall_clock_benchmark`) — all behind `#[cfg(feature = "llvm")]`. One follow-up regression test in `tests/par_codegen.rs` (`test_auto_par_vec_return_undefined_var_repro`, `#[ignore]`-gated) reproduces the Slice A Vec-return shape gap. Aggregate counts: `cargo test` → ~3300+ pass / 0 fail / 8 ignored (existing); `cargo test --features llvm` → all green incl. all parallax tests, no regressions in existing suites; `cargo clippy --all --tests -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean.

  *Deviations from the plan.* (1) **C2/C5 fixture shape — Vec[T] returns reduced to single-row struct returns.** The plan called for `Vec[Order] / Vec[Notification] / Vec[Recommendation]` returns. Verified at the par_codegen level that a `Vec[T]` typed return through Slice A's per-branch return slots fails codegen with `Undefined variable '<binding>'` — the slot ABI classifies `Vec` shapes correctly via `llvm_type_for_type_expr` but the parent-side rebinding from `slot_values` doesn't surface the slot binding for downstream stmts in some Vec shape path. Per hard-stop trigger 1 fallback (b), the demo fixture uses single-row struct returns (`fetch_latest_order -> Order`, `fetch_top_notification -> Notification`, `fetch_top_recommendation -> Recommendation`). The demo's fan-out+join shape is preserved; the row-vs-rows shape change is fixture-level only. The smaller standalone reproduction landed at `tests/par_codegen.rs::test_auto_par_vec_return_undefined_var_repro` per fallback (a) so the gap closes back to the plan-shape additively when the underlying mechanism is fixed. (2) **Provider type-discriminator fields.** The plan didn't anticipate that providers with identical LLVM struct shapes (`{ i64 }`) collide with each other and with user-facing data types (`Order { i64, i64 }`) in the codegen's `var_type_names` reverse lookup at `with_provider[R]` lowering. Added a unique `*_tag: String` first-field on each provider so the four LLVM types stay distinct (and incidentally so the busy-compute kernel can consult a non-eliminable value). Inline-fix; documented at the top of `providers.kara` and in this close-out for future maintainers. (3) **Wrapper-fn pattern for `get_dashboard` body.** The plan's example body called `R.fetch_*(user_id)` directly inside `get_dashboard`. Verified the analyzer's `add_function_effects` looks up free-fn callee effects by name, and `R.method(...)` dispatch through the `karac_provider_lookup` doesn't propagate effects to the call-site stmt's effect set — so the four-call group ended up trivial. Wrapping each `R.fetch_*` in a `fetch_*(user_id) with reads(R) { R.fetch_*(...) }` driver fn (mirroring parallax-lite's `record_a/b/c` pattern) gives the analyzer the declared-effect signal it needs. (4) **`main.kara` — single `dashboard.profile.name` println dropped.** Verified a pre-existing codegen bug where chained-field println of a moved-in struct's field (`d.profile.name`) emits a load that resolves to `0` at runtime regardless of the actual value — the bug reproduces on a minimal three-line standalone test outside Slice A's path entirely. Single-level field access works fine; the e2e tests verify dashboard correctness via the side-channel `fetch_* called` markers each provider emits. The dashboard is constructed and the post-join "got dashboard" line confirms the join completed. Out of slice scope to fix the chained-field println bug.

  *Out of scope, still open.*
  - **Real DB FFI** (Postgres / MySQL / Redis) — Phase 11 long-tail.
  - **JSON serialization of `Dashboard`** — Slice F territory.
  - **HTTP entry point** (`serve_http(addr, handler)`) — Slice B.
  - **Side-by-side benchmark harness vs Go / Node.js** — Slice E.
  - **Cancellation propagation through provider boundaries** — `phase-7-codegen.md` "Par codegen: cancellation and error propagation".
  - **Parameterized providers** (`UserDB[tenant_id]`) — Theme 6 deviation 4 deferred this; out of v1 scope.
  - **Real I/O simulation via sleep primitives** — runtime exposes no sleep today; busy-compute kernel is the v1 fallback.
  - **`#[derive(Debug)]` / `#[derive(Eq)]` on the data types** — debug printing in the e2e tests uses explicit `println` statements with hand-formatted strings.
  - **`Vec[T]` return through Slice A's per-branch return slots** — open as `tests/par_codegen.rs::test_auto_par_vec_return_undefined_var_repro` (`#[ignore]`-gated regression). Once the gap closes, Slice C's fixture can grow back to `Vec[T]` returns additively.
  - **Chained-field println on a moved-in struct's nested field** (`d.profile.name` returns `0`) — pre-existing codegen bug surfaced by Slice C, reproducible standalone outside Slice A; out of slice scope.
  - **Multi-file project-mode codegen** — `cargo run --release` from inside `examples/parallax/` doesn't emit a binary today (parallax-lite ships in this state too); use the concat-and-compile pattern documented in `examples/parallax/README.md`.

 **Phase classification:** all items below ship in Phase 11 (long-tail) per roadmap.md, except `std.json` which is floor (Phase 8) and is tagged inline. See `design.md § Numerical Types (Tensor, Column, DataFrame)`, `design.md § Numeric Semantics > Literal-involved promotion`, and `design.md § Entry Point > Script mode` for semantics; `syntax.md § 2 Program Structure`, `§ 6.2 Type Syntax`, and `§ 6.4 Generic Parameters` for grammar.

**Type system — forcing functions (Q1–Q4).**

- [ ] **Shape as a new generic-parameter kind.** Extend `src/typechecker.rs` to track dim-kinded and shape-variadic (`...S`) generic params alongside existing type and const-expr params. Kind inference: a param appearing only in shape position is inferred `Dim`-kinded; explicit `: Dim` and `...` annotations also accepted. Unification rules: two `Dim` params unify if one is unbound or both resolve to the same const expr; `?` unifies with any `Dim` and degrades the result position to `?`. Shape-dim mismatch produces `E_SHAPE` diagnostic naming both sides and where the conflicting bindings were introduced.

- [ ] **Shape literal grammar (parser + AST).** Extend `src/parser.rs` and `src/ast.rs` to accept shape literals `[const_expr_or_? { , const_expr_or_? }]` in type-argument position, plus `...IDENT` variadic splice inside a shape literal. `?` is a new `AstNode::ShapeDimDynamic`; existing expression-`?` usage is unaffected (context disambiguates). Outside shape-argument slots, `?` parsing is unchanged.

- [ ] **`Tensor[T, Shape]` stdlib type.** Generic struct with compile-time shape parameter. Stdlib `impl`: `zeros` / `ones` / `full` constructors, `from` literal constructor, `shape()` runtime accessor, multi-dim `t[i, j, k]` indexing via `Index` / `IndexMut`, `iter_axis(n)` for axis iteration, reshape / permute / slice / squeeze operations with shape-preservation in the type where statically known. Codegen: contiguous C-order buffer in Arrow layout; bounds-check elision when all dims are static const exprs. Interpreter parity: tree-walk implementation tracks shape at runtime for `Tensor[T, Shape]` values regardless of static/dynamic dim mix.

- [ ] **Arithmetic traits on `Tensor[T, Shape]`.** `Add`/`Sub`/`Mul`/`Div` operator-trait impls that require *exact shape match* between tensor operands and accept scalar operands via the Q4 literal-promotion rule (+ operator dispatch for scalar-tensor). `Neg` for negation. Shape mismatch between two tensors produces `E_SHAPE` with both shapes printed and a pointer to `broadcast_add` / `broadcast_mul` methods. Reduce ops (`sum`, `mean`, `prod`, `min`, `max`) return `T`; axis-reduce variants (`sum_axis(n)`, `mean_axis(n)`) return a tensor of rank-1 lower.

- [ ] **Explicit broadcasting methods.** `broadcast_add`, `broadcast_sub`, `broadcast_mul`, `broadcast_div` on `Tensor[T, Shape]`. Arguments accept tensors whose shape is elementwise broadcast-compatible with `self.shape()` (singleton dims expand). When both shapes are fully static at call site, compatibility checked at compile time; else checked at runtime. Typed broadcasting (where the type system rejects incompatible broadcasts statically, Q3's 3D option) is a v2 research target, not in v1.

- [x] **Literal-involved promotion in numeric binary operators (Q4).** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `infer_binary` computes `eff_left_ty`/`eff_right_ty` via suffix-free literal detection; when one side is an unsuffixed literal and the other is a concrete numeric type T, re-records the literal's span as T in `expr_types` (so `rewrite_binary` in lowering sees a homogeneous pair). Float literals are not promoted to int types. 8 typechecker tests added covering int-right, int-left, float-right, int-to-float, comparison, equality, non-numeric (still errors), string+int (still errors). ~~Extend `src/lowering.rs` / typechecker binary-op handling: when one operand is a typed expression of numeric type `T` and the other is a literal, the literal takes type `T` before the operator is resolved. Scope: `+ - * / % < <= > >= == !=`. Function-call arguments, struct-field assignment, and pattern matching retain the strict "literal matches declared type" rule.~~

**Data types — Arrow commitment (Q5, Q6).**

- [ ] **`Column[T]` — nullable 1D column with Arrow bitmap layout.** Struct with `{ data, null_bitmap, len, capacity }`; Apache Arrow conformance per `design.md § Memory Layout Commitments`. Stdlib methods: `new`, `with_capacity`, `from_vec` (all-valid), `from_iter_nullable`, `null_count`, `is_null(i)`, `valid_count`, `push` / `push_null`, `fillna(val, treat_nan_as_null=false)`, `dropna`, indexing (`c[i] -> Option[T]`), `iter` (yields `Option[T]`), `iter_valid` (yields `T`, skipping nulls). Arithmetic with SQL null propagation: `null + x = null`, `null == null = null` (three-valued logic). All operator impls maintain the bitmap through the result.

- [ ] **`DataFrame` — schema-bearing table of columns.** Struct with named-column dispatch, schema carrying column-name-to-type mappings. Minimum API surface: construction from a map of named columns, `column(name)` lookup returning `ref Column[T]` with type erasure via an internal `AnyColumn`, `row_iter` yielding struct views (mechanism: compile-time row-struct synthesis from schema), `schema()` accessor, basic `filter(predicate)` / `select(cols)` operations. Heavier query planning (joins, groupby with custom aggregations) is explicit v1.5+ work.

- [ ] **Arrow IPC and Parquet.** `Tensor.from_arrow_ipc(bytes)` / `arr.to_arrow_ipc()`; `Column.from_arrow_ipc(bytes)` / `col.to_arrow_ipc()`; `DataFrame.read_parquet(path) with reads(FileSystem)` / `df.write_parquet(path) with writes(FileSystem)`; `DataFrame.read_csv(path)` / `df.write_csv(path)` matching the same effect pattern. IPC implementation uses the Arrow C Data Interface for zero-copy where feasible.

**Script mode (Q7).**

- [ ] **Script mode — files without `fn main`.** Parser change: when `src/parser.rs` encounters a top-level statement (`let`, expression, assignment) *before* any `fn main` declaration, switch to script mode and synthesize `fn main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` wrapping all top-level statements in file order. Items (fn, struct, enum, trait, impl, use) remain at module scope and hoist as today. Mix of top-level statements and an explicit `fn main` is a parse error with a diagnostic pointing at both. Resolver / typechecker treat the synthesized main exactly as they would a user-written `fn main()` with `Result[Unit, Error]` return type — effect inference applies, `?` works, existing entry-point rules apply.

**Scripting-critical stdlib (Q10 10B surface).**

- [ ] **`std.regex`.** Compile regex patterns to an NFA/DFA state machine; `Regex.compile(pattern) -> Result[Regex, RegexError]`, `rx.is_match(s)`, `rx.find(s) -> Option[Match]`, `rx.find_all(s) -> Vec[Match]`, `rx.captures(s)`, `rx.replace_all(s, replacement)`. Use a tested regex crate as the initial backend; eventually replace with a Kāra-native implementation. Pure (no effects).

- [ ] **`std.http` (client only).** `Client.new()`, `client.get(url)`, `client.post(url, body)`, chained builders for headers / body / timeout. `Request.send() -> Result[Response, HttpError] with sends(Network), receives(Network)`. Response exposes `status_code`, `headers`, `text()`, `bytes()`. TLS via stdlib-adjacent crate. Server is v1.5+; client is enough for scripting and the common data-ingestion pattern.

- [ ] **`std.http` server — minimal surface (pulled forward from v1.5 for Parallax demo).** Server-only minimal stdlib surface: `Server::bind(addr) -> Result[Server, HttpError]`, `server.serve(handler) -> Result[(), HttpError]`, `Request { method, path, query, headers, body: Bytes }`, `Response::new(status) -> ResponseBuilder` chained with `.header(k, v)` / `.body(bytes)` / `.json(value)` → `Response`. The `serve` call is blocking on the bound thread; the handler is invoked synchronously per-request from the runtime's hyper-driven request loop. **Roadmap deviation flagged:** [`roadmap.md:743`](roadmap.md) and [`roadmap.md:798`](roadmap.md) place `std.http` server at v1.5; this entry pulls it forward to v1 because the **full Parallax demo** ([`docs/demo_ideas.md` § Demo 1](demo_ideas.md)) is the broadest-appeal Tier-1 v1 demo and requires a real HTTP entry point (the `get_dashboard(user_id)` endpoint). Pull-forward scope is *minimal* — no client (the existing client entry above ships the client surface separately if needed), no middleware, no TLS, no HTTP/2 negotiation tuning, no WebSocket upgrade. v1.5's full server entry consumes this entry's surface and extends it; nothing here gets reverted.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-09) — Full Parallax demo: HTTP server FFI.*

  Ship the minimal `std.http` server surface that lets the Parallax demo's `get_dashboard(user_id)` endpoint serve real HTTP requests. Backed by Rust `hyper` linked from `karac-runtime` via FFI; Kāra-side `std.http` is type wrappers + thin extern decls. **Locked design choices (2026-05-09):** (i) **B1: server-only minimal** — `Server`, `Request`, `Response`, `serve()`; no client, no middleware, no TLS; (ii) **B2: hyper backing** through karac-runtime FFI; (iii) **B3 conditional:** polymorphic-handler-effects *happens* (handler signature is `fn(Request) -> Response with <handler-effects>`; `serve` propagates the handler's effect set through), exact polymorphism shape (effects-bubble-up vs `Server[E]` parameterization vs effect-erased-at-FFI-boundary-with-call-site-discharge) is **TBD pending Theme 6 (`with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch) close-out** — once Theme 6 lands, the precise shape is whatever composes most naturally with `with_provider[R]` chains; (iv) **B4: two-layer concurrency** — hyper runs its own tokio runtime in karac-runtime; per-request hyper invokes the Kāra handler synchronously; inside the handler, slice A's `karac_par_run` does fan-out+join; (v) **B5: one smoke test** — bind on `127.0.0.1:0`, GET `/dashboard/1`, assert 200 + JSON body matching expected fields. Effect-propagation correctness is covered by Slice C's typed-provider tests + Theme 6's dispatch tests; concurrent-request benchmarks are covered by Slice E.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Add `hyper = { version = "1", features = ["server", "http1"] }` and `tokio = { version = "1", features = ["rt-multi-thread", "net"] }` to `runtime/Cargo.toml`. Both crates are widely adopted, well-maintained, FFI-stable (no `#[no_mangle]` collisions). Run `cargo build -p karac-runtime --release` to confirm the runtime crate still builds with the added deps.
  - **(b)** Add `karac_runtime_serve_http(addr_cstr: *const c_char, handler_fn_ptr: extern "C" fn(*const KaracHttpRequest, *mut KaracHttpResponse) -> i32) -> i32` extern in `runtime/src/lib.rs`. Body: parse the addr cstring, build a hyper `Server` bound to it, spin up a tokio multi-thread runtime, register a service that for each incoming request: (i) translates the hyper `Request<Body>` into a `KaracHttpRequest` C struct on the stack, (ii) `alloca`-style allocates a `KaracHttpResponse` C struct, (iii) calls the handler fn ptr synchronously (the handler returns when done), (iv) translates the populated `KaracHttpResponse` back into a hyper `Response<Body>`. Return code: 0 = served gracefully, non-zero = bind failure / runtime construction failure. **Critical:** the handler call is synchronous from the runtime's perspective — tokio's tasks block in a `tokio::task::block_in_place` or equivalent so the handler can do whatever it wants (including sleep, which is what the demo's in-memory provider sleep_ms simulation does) without breaking the runtime. Cross-check: hyper's per-request task blocking is well-supported via `block_in_place`; verify the multi-thread executor handles it.
  - **(c)** Define the C-ABI structs `KaracHttpRequest` and `KaracHttpResponse` in `runtime/src/lib.rs` with `#[repr(C)]`. Fields:
    ```
    KaracHttpRequest {
        method: *const c_char,        // null-terminated, owned by runtime
        path:   *const c_char,        // null-terminated, owned by runtime
        query:  *const c_char,        // null-terminated, owned by runtime (empty string if no query)
        headers_keys: *const *const c_char,
        headers_vals: *const *const c_char,
        headers_len: usize,
        body_ptr: *const u8,
        body_len: usize,
    }
    KaracHttpResponse {
        status: u16,                  // initialized to 200
        body_ptr: *mut u8,            // handler writes; runtime owns lifecycle
        body_len: usize,
        body_cap: usize,
        headers_keys: *mut *mut c_char,
        headers_vals: *mut *mut c_char,
        headers_len: usize,
        headers_cap: usize,
    }
    ```
    Memory ownership: request-side fields are owned by the runtime (handler reads, must not free); response-side body / header buffers are owned by the runtime (allocated via `karac_runtime_alloc` so the GC / RC can manage them — same pattern slice 5's `list_par_blocks` uses). The handler writes the buffers; the runtime translates back to hyper and frees the buffers after sending.
  - **(d)** Add the Kāra-side `std.http` module in `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` (peer to `io.kara` / `runtime.kara`). Declare:
    - `pub struct Server { handle: i64 }` (opaque handle wrapping the runtime-side server state).
    - `pub fn bind(addr: String) -> Result[Server, HttpError]` — externs to `karac_runtime_http_bind`.
    - `pub struct Request { ... }` — direct mapping of `KaracHttpRequest` fields, with helper methods `method() -> String`, `path() -> String`, `query() -> String`, `header(key: String) -> Option[String]`, `body() -> Bytes`.
    - `pub struct Response { ... }` — peer struct with builder methods.
    - `pub fn ResponseBuilder.new(status: u16) -> ResponseBuilder` + `.header(k, v) -> ResponseBuilder` + `.body(bytes: Bytes) -> Response` + `.json[T: ToJson](value: T) -> Response`.
    - `pub fn Server.serve[E](handler: fn(Request) -> Response with E) -> Result[(), HttpError] with E, sends(Network), receives(Network)` — externs to `karac_runtime_serve_http`. **The polymorphic shape `with E` is the B3-locked premise; exact instantiation/dispatch shape settles when Theme 6 lands. Plan-drafting note: if Theme 6's `with_provider[R]` chooses a specific syntactic form for effect-set parameterization, slice B's `serve` signature adopts that form verbatim.** New `Network` effect resource declaration if not already present.
  - **(e)** Codegen / typechecker integration. The `serve` call is a regular FFI call — most of the work is type-level (the `with E` polymorphism — which, if it's exactly the same shape as Theme 6, requires no slice-B-specific typechecker work; otherwise it requires a small typechecker extension to admit effect-set parameters on free fns). The handler fn pointer is just a fn-ptr value at the LLVM IR level; codegen passes it through as `i8*`. Cross-check: existing FFI calls to `karac_runtime_alloc` / `karac_runtime_free` etc. take fn-ptr-returning args via the same mechanism — verify no new codegen path needed.
  - **(f)** Error handling. `HttpError` enum: `BindFailed(String)`, `RuntimeFailed(String)`, `HandlerPanicked`. Each maps to a non-zero return from the runtime extern; the Kāra-side `bind` / `serve` calls translate the i32 return into a `Result`. Handler panics propagate via the standard panic-unwind mechanism; the runtime catches at the request-handling task boundary and returns `HandlerPanicked` to the user (the request gets a 500 from the runtime).
  - **(g)** Demo wiring sample. Add `examples/parallax/` (sibling to `examples/parallax_lite/`) with at minimum: a `main.kara` binding to `127.0.0.1:8080` and serving a hardcoded handler that parses `path`, dispatches to `get_dashboard(user_id)` (placeholder calling four `sleep_ms`-shaped fns since slices A + C aren't required for this slice's smoke test), returns a JSON response. Smoke test in `tests/codegen.rs` or new `tests/http_server.rs` builds and runs this against `127.0.0.1:0`.

  *Tests.*
  - All existing `cargo test` and `cargo test --features llvm` suites must remain fully green. New deps (`hyper`, `tokio`) must not introduce build regressions for non-llvm test paths (the runtime crate is `cdylib` / `staticlib`; hyper sits behind it).
  - One smoke test (B5) in a new `tests/http_server.rs` (or extending `tests/codegen.rs`'s LLVM-gated section): `test_http_server_serves_hardcoded_handler` — builds the demo wiring sample from sub-step (g), spawns the binary as a subprocess bound to `127.0.0.1:0` (port 0 lets the OS pick), reads back the bound port from the binary's stdout, performs a `GET /dashboard/1` via `reqwest` or `ureq` from the test process, asserts 200 + JSON body matches a hardcoded expected payload. Subprocess + port-from-stdout pattern: precedent in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`'s subprocess invocation. **Critical:** ASAN-gated; skip if ASAN is unavailable (runtime test infrastructure already has the skip pattern).
  - One regression pin: `test_http_server_handler_effects_propagate` — handler with explicit `with reads(MockResource), writes(MockResource)` annotations gets typechecked through `serve[E]` without the typechecker complaining about effect-set mismatch. **Conditional on Theme 6 landing**: if Theme 6 hasn't shaped the effect-set polymorphism syntax yet, this test stays as a `#[ignore]` placeholder until Theme 6's pattern is settled.

  *Files expected to change.* `runtime/Cargo.toml` — add `hyper` + `tokio` deps. `runtime/src/lib.rs` — `KaracHttpRequest` / `KaracHttpResponse` structs, `karac_runtime_http_bind` extern, `karac_runtime_serve_http` extern, request translation logic (~200 lines net new). `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` — new file, ~80 lines (`Server`, `Request`, `Response`, `ResponseBuilder`, `bind`, `serve`, `HttpError` enum). `src/typechecker.rs` — only if Theme 6's effect-set polymorphism shape requires slice-B-specific extension; otherwise zero changes. `examples/parallax/` — new directory with `kara.toml` + `src/main.kara` (~50 lines). `tests/http_server.rs` — new file, ~80 lines (1 smoke test + 1 effect-propagation pin). This doc — flip slice status after landing and add a "What landed" close-out paragraph.

  *Out of scope.*
  - **`std.http` client** — separate entry above (`std.http (client only)` at line 559); slice B does not bundle client work.
  - **Middleware / `before_handler` / `after_handler`** — out of scope per B1 lock; v1.5 layer.
  - **TLS** — out of scope per B1 lock; Phase 11 long-tail or v1.5.
  - **HTTP/2 negotiation tuning** — hyper supports HTTP/2 via separate features; slice B sticks to HTTP/1.1 only (`features = ["server", "http1"]`).
  - **WebSocket upgrade** — out of scope per B1 lock; v1.5.
  - **Routing DSL** — slice B's `serve(handler)` takes a single handler that does its own routing via `request.path()` matching. No `Server.route("/path", fn)` machinery. v1.5 layer (or out-of-stdlib helper crate).
  - **Real database FFI** — Phase 11 long-tail; demo uses `sleep_ms` providers per parallax-lite pattern.
  - **Slice A integration** — slice B's smoke test handler doesn't need slice A's auto-par; can dispatch four `sleep_ms` calls sequentially. Slice E's benchmark is what exercises slice A through slice B.
  - **Theme 6 dispatch shape work** — slice B *consumes* Theme 6's outcome; does not reshape it.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **Theme 6 hasn't landed and the `serve[E]` signature requires its dispatch shape.** If sub-step (d)'s effect-set parameter syntax is rejected by the typechecker because Theme 6 is still in flight, halt and either (a) wait for Theme 6, (b) skip the polymorphic surface for slice B and ship a non-polymorphic `serve(handler: fn(Request) -> Response)` that erases effects at the FFI boundary with a follow-up to add polymorphism once Theme 6 lands. **Default fallback: (b)** — erased-at-FFI is additive-compatible with later polymorphism (existing handlers stay valid). This makes slice B independent of Theme 6's timeline. *(Cross-check: when slice B begins, grep `wip-list2.md § Theme 6` for the close-out flip; if not yet flipped, take the (b) path.)*
  - **Hyper / tokio dep adds noticeable build time to non-llvm test paths.** Both deps are large; if `cargo test` (no llvm feature) goes from sub-second compile to multi-minute, halt and either (a) gate the entire `std.http server` machinery behind a `feature = "http_server"` flag in `runtime/Cargo.toml`, defaulting off (only enabled for the parallax demo build), (b) skip the deps if they're already transitively available via some other crate. *(Cross-check: time `cargo test --quiet` before sub-step (a) and again after; if delta > 30s, halt.)*
  - **Hyper's blocking-handler pattern doesn't compose cleanly with multi-thread tokio.** The synchronous handler-call from a hyper service would break tokio's executor if mishandled. *(Cross-check: hyper docs explicitly support `block_in_place` inside a `multi_thread` runtime; verify with a minimal test before committing to the integration approach.)*
  - **Subprocess port-discovery from stdout proves flaky for the smoke test.** If reading the bound port from the binary's stdout has timing issues (process not yet listening when the test connects), halt and either (a) use a pre-bound socket passed as an env var instead of port 0, (b) add a retry-with-backoff in the test. *(Likely workable; flagging as a hard-stop only because subprocess timing tests have historically been flaky and this is a reasonable failure mode.)*
  - **Demo handler in `examples/parallax/src/main.kara` runs into the multi-file project mode codegen gap.** Parallax-lite's README documents this exact gap (codegen across modules is a CR-24 follow-up); the workaround is single-file concatenation. Slice B's smoke test should follow the same workaround pattern — the binary the test runs is a single concatenated `.kara` file, not a multi-file project build. The `examples/parallax/` directory holds the source-of-truth multi-file form for human readers; the test rebuilds via concat for now. `Command.new(program)`, chained builders for args / env / working_dir / stdio, `cmd.spawn() -> Result[Child, IoError] with writes(ProcessTable)`, `cmd.output() -> Result[Output, IoError]` (synchronous convenience). `Child` supports `wait`, `kill`, `stdin` / `stdout` / `stderr` handle access. New effect resource `ProcessTable` alongside existing `FileSystem`, `Env`, etc. — covers spawning/waiting/killing.

- [ ] **`std.json`.** `Json` enum (Null, Bool, Number, String, Array, Object). `Json.parse(s) -> Result[Json, JsonError]`, `json.stringify() -> String`. Typed (de)serialization via `FromJson` / `ToJson` traits — v1 ships the Json enum and parse/stringify; derived impls for structs are a v1.5 follow-up coupled with `Serialize` / `Deserialize` trait work. **Surfaced as Parallax-demo prerequisite 2026-05-09** — Slice B's `Response.json[T: ToJson](value: T)` builder depends on a `ToJson` trait that hasn't shipped, and the demo's `Dashboard` response body is JSON-serialized.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-09) — Full Parallax demo: `std.json`.*

  Ship the v1 `std.json` surface: `Json` enum, `parse` / `stringify`, manual `ToJson` / `FromJson` traits. Derived impls (`#[derive(ToJson)]`) are v1.5; v1 ships hand-written impls only. Backing implementation is `serde_json` via Rust FFI from `karac-runtime`, mirroring Slice B's `hyper` FFI pattern. **Locked design choices (2026-05-09):** (i) **Number representation: `Json.Number(f64)`** matching JSON spec verbatim — no split Int/Float; (ii) **Object key ordering: insertion order** via `Vec<(String, Json)>` backing the `Json.Object` variant — matches Python dict / JS object iteration; (iii) **Backing impl: `serde_json` via FFI** through karac-runtime — no hand-rolled Kāra parser; (iv) **Error reporting: `JsonError { line, col, msg }`** with line + column surfaced from `serde_json::Error`'s line/column accessors; (v) **`ToJson` / `FromJson` manual-impl-only in v1** — derived in v1.5; (vi) **Minimal test surface** — round-trip on representative shapes + error-reporting smoke + manual ToJson impl test.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Add `serde_json = "1"` to `runtime/Cargo.toml`. Run `cargo build -p karac-runtime --release` to confirm clean build.
  - **(b)** Add `karac_runtime_json_parse(input_cstr: *const c_char, error_out: *mut KaracJsonError) -> *mut KaracJsonValue` extern in `runtime/src/lib.rs`. Body: parse the cstring via `serde_json::from_str::<serde_json::Value>(...)`; on success, allocate a `KaracJsonValue` via the runtime's existing alloc path (mirroring slice 5's `list_par_blocks` pattern); on error, populate `*error_out` with `{line, column, message_cstr}` (message owned by runtime, freed by Kāra-side after read). Return null on error.
  - **(c)** Add `karac_runtime_json_stringify(value: *const KaracJsonValue) -> *mut c_char` extern. Body: walk the `KaracJsonValue` tree, build a `serde_json::Value`, call `serde_json::to_string()`, return the C-string (runtime owns; Kāra-side reads + frees via existing string-FFI path).
  - **(d)** Define the C-ABI structs in `runtime/src/lib.rs`:
    ```
    KaracJsonValue (#[repr(C)] enum-tagged via discriminant + payload union):
      tag: u8                     // 0=Null, 1=Bool, 2=Number, 3=String, 4=Array, 5=Object
      payload: union {
        bool_val: bool,
        num_val: f64,
        str_val: { ptr: *mut c_char, len: usize },
        arr_val: { items: *mut *mut KaracJsonValue, len: usize },
        obj_val: { keys: *mut *mut c_char, vals: *mut *mut KaracJsonValue, len: usize },
      }
    KaracJsonError (#[repr(C)]):
      line: usize
      column: usize
      message: *mut c_char        // null-terminated, owned by runtime
    ```
    Use a discriminant + per-variant payload struct; `#[repr(C)]` unions are unsafe and fiddly — easier path is six variant payload structs and a single `tag` byte selecting which is valid. Tradeoff documented as a possible deviation.
  - **(e)** Add Kāra-side `std.json` module in `runtime/stdlib/json.kara`. Declare:
    - `pub enum Json { Null, Bool(bool), Number(f64), String(String), Array(Vec[Json]), Object(Vec[(String, Json)]) }` — note Object backed by `Vec[(String, Json)]` per insertion-order lock.
    - `pub fn Json.parse(s: String) -> Result[Json, JsonError]` — externs to `karac_runtime_json_parse`, walks the returned `KaracJsonValue` tree to build a Kāra `Json` enum recursively. Free the runtime-side tree after copy.
    - `pub fn Json.stringify(self) -> String` — methods on the enum; walks the Kāra tree, builds a `KaracJsonValue` tree via runtime alloc, calls `karac_runtime_json_stringify`, returns the resulting String. Free the runtime-side tree after.
    - `pub struct JsonError { line: u32, column: u32, message: String }` — populated from runtime-side `KaracJsonError`.
    - `pub trait ToJson { fn to_json(self) -> Json }` — manual-impl trait per design lock (v).
    - `pub trait FromJson { fn from_json(j: Json) -> Result[Self, JsonError] }` — peer trait.
    - Builtin `ToJson` impls for `i32` / `i64` / `f32` / `f64` (lossless f64 promotion) / `bool` / `String` / `Vec[T: ToJson]` / `Option[T: ToJson]` (Some → inner, None → Null).
    - Peer `FromJson` impls.
  - **(f)** Tree-walk codegen for the Kāra↔runtime translation. The recursive `Json → KaracJsonValue` walk is straightforward but non-trivial — ~80 lines of Kāra. Pattern: each variant emits the matching tag + populates the matching union field. Allocations via `karac_runtime_alloc` for arrays / objects / strings.
  - **(g)** Wire into Slice B's `Response.json[T: ToJson](value: T) -> Response` builder once Slice F lands. The wiring: `Response.json` calls `value.to_json().stringify()`, sets `body` to the stringified bytes, sets `Content-Type: application/json` header. **Out-of-scope-but-noted:** Slice B can be drafted/implemented before Slice F lands — its `.json()` builder is gated behind a "Slice F prerequisite" hard-stop trigger, with `Response.body(bytes)` as the fallback.

  *Tests.*
  - All existing `cargo test` and `cargo test --features llvm` suites must remain fully green.
  - 6 new tests under a new `tests/json.rs` (or extending `tests/stdlib.rs`):
    - `test_json_parse_roundtrip_object` — `'{"a": 1, "b": "hello", "c": [true, null]}'` parses to the equivalent Json tree, stringifies back to byte-equivalent (modulo whitespace) output.
    - `test_json_parse_roundtrip_array` — top-level array of mixed types.
    - `test_json_parse_roundtrip_primitives` — each scalar type round-trips (number, string, bool, null).
    - `test_json_parse_error_surfaces_line_col` — malformed input `'{"a": }'` yields `JsonError` with the right line + column.
    - `test_json_object_preserves_insertion_order` — `'{"z": 1, "a": 2, "m": 3}'` parses + stringifies in input order, not alphabetical.
    - `test_to_json_manual_impl` — hand-written `ToJson` impl on a `struct Point { x: i32, y: i32 }` produces the expected JSON object.

  *Files expected to change.* `runtime/Cargo.toml` — add `serde_json` dep. `runtime/src/lib.rs` — `KaracJsonValue` / `KaracJsonError` C-ABI structs (~50 lines), `karac_runtime_json_parse` extern (~40 lines), `karac_runtime_json_stringify` extern (~40 lines), tree-walk helpers (~80 lines). `runtime/stdlib/json.kara` — new file, ~150 lines (`Json` enum, `parse` / `stringify`, `ToJson` / `FromJson` traits, builtin impls, runtime-side bindings). `tests/json.rs` — new file, ~80 lines (6 tests). This doc — flip slice status after landing and add a "What landed" close-out paragraph.

  *Out of scope.*
  - **`#[derive(ToJson)]` / `#[derive(FromJson)]`** — v1.5 follow-up per design lock (v) and the existing entry's prose.
  - **Canonical-form JSON output (alphabetical keys, no whitespace)** — post-v1; users who need canonical output write a `to_canonical()` helper.
  - **Streaming parse / serialize** — v1 builds the full Json tree in memory. Streaming is post-v1.
  - **JSON Schema validation** — separate stdlib track.
  - **`Number` precision beyond f64** — JSON spec is f64; users needing arbitrary-precision arithmetic use `Json.String` and parse client-side.
  - **Pretty-printed output** — v1 is single-line stringify only; pretty-printing (`stringify_pretty(indent: u32)`) is a v1.x additive.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **`#[repr(C)]` union for `KaracJsonValue` payload turns out fiddly enough that the variant-payload-struct alternative (sub-step d) is needed.** Acceptable; document as a deviation. The variant-struct approach is heavier on memory (every value carries the largest payload size) but ABI-stable and easier to reason about. *(Cross-check: `KaracJsonValue` size with all six variant fields = ~32 bytes; the union-vs-struct decision is ~16 bytes per node; for the demo's typical tree of ~20 nodes, that's ~320 bytes — negligible.)*
  - **`serde_json` adds noticeable build time to the runtime crate.** Same hard-stop pattern as Slice B's hyper dep. Halt if `cargo build -p karac-runtime --release` adds > 30s, gate behind feature flag if needed.
  - **The Kāra-side recursive tree-walk for stringify hits codegen edge cases.** Recursive Kāra functions are well-supported (the `Json` enum's `stringify` calls itself through `Vec[Json]` iteration), but the tree-walk's mutual recursion through `to_json` could surface monomorphization bottlenecks on deeply nested generics. *(Cross-check: parallax-lite's `InMemoryMetrics` uses similar generic-method dispatch and compiles cleanly.)*
  - **`Vec[(String, Json)]` for `Json.Object` interaction with the typechecker turns out odd.** Tuple-typed `Vec` elements are common (`Vec[(K, V)]` is the explicit-pair shape used in many places). If the typechecker rejects pattern-matching the tuple inside the enum variant, halt and either (a) split into `Vec[String]` keys + `Vec[Json]` vals (paired by index — uglier API), (b) introduce a `JsonObjectEntry { key: String, value: Json }` struct. *(Cross-check: `Vec[(K, V)]` is exercised in the existing test suite; if it works there, it works here.)*

- [ ] **`std.stats` — basic statistics.** `mean`, `sum`, `prod`, `variance`, `stddev`, `percentile(p)`, `median`, `min`, `max`, `argmin`, `argmax`, `sort`, `argsort`. Trait-dispatched via `Reduce`, `ElementwiseMap`, `ElementwiseOrd` traits so `Tensor`, `Column`, and future `GpuTensor` implement the same surface without API break. Free-function forms in `std.stats` (`stats.mean(v)`) and method forms on `Tensor` / `Column` (`v.mean()`).

**GPU call-site backend — deferred to post-Phase-10.**

- [ ] **(Deferred.) Revisit GPU call-site dispatch once Phase 10 codegen has ground truth.** Expected shape: `GpuTensor[T, Shape]` mirroring `Tensor[T, Shape]` with device memory; `.on(gpu)` / `.to_cpu()` boundary ops matching CuPy / PyTorch / JAX semantics. Revisit the lazy-evaluation design alongside — whole-pipeline visibility is load-bearing for GPU kernel fusion.

**Lazy evaluation (Q8) — v1.5 feature, not v1.**

- [ ] **(Deferred to v1.5.) `.lazy()` method on `Vec`, `Tensor`, `Column` returning `LazyColumn[T]` / `LazyTensor[T]` / `Iterator[T]` specializations.** Fused filter/map/reduce pipelines with effect composition from closures. Build on top of the existing `Iterator[T]` language-level primitive. Revisit when Phase 11 stdlib is stable.

**Fallback plan:** if Phase 11 schedule slips, `regex` and `http` are the most at-risk items (real network + state-machine work); pushable to v1.1. Tensor / Column / DataFrame / stats / script mode are cheap enough to keep as v1 non-negotiables.

- [ ] **G23 — Trait coherence / orphan rules**. Decide and enforce: can you implement a foreign trait for a foreign type? Recommendation: Rust's orphan rule (must own either the trait or the type). Document the newtype workaround. Not relevant until multi-package support exists — moved from Phase 3.

- [ ] **G14 — FFI effect annotation completeness**. Create comprehensive syscall-to-effect mapping table. Review POSIX/Linux syscall man pages for composite effects (e.g., `sendfile()` needs both `reads(FileSystem)` and `sends(Network)`). Build integration tests that validate effect annotations against actual syscall behavior.

- [ ] **FFI — Kāra-to-C exports.** Enable Kāra functions to be callable from C. Requires: `#[export]` or `pub extern "C"` annotation, compiler generates C-compatible calling convention, restrictions on parameter/return types (must be C-representable). Needed for shared libraries, plugins, and embedding Kāra in C/C++ applications.

- [ ] **FFI — C header generation.** Tooling to auto-generate `.h` header files from `extern "C"` Kāra exports (like Rust's `cbindgen`). Maps Kāra types to C equivalents. Needed for C consumers of Kāra libraries.

- [ ] **FFI — `#[repr(C)]` struct layout.** Attribute to guarantee C-compatible memory layout for structs passed across FFI boundaries. Without this, Kāra's compiler is free to reorder/pad fields (especially with layout blocks). `#[repr(C)]` pins layout to match C's rules.

- [ ] **FFI — `#[repr(transparent)]` for distinct-type FFI.** Spec lives at design.md § `#[repr(transparent)]` for distinct-type FFI (v60 item 23). Sub-steps: (1) Parser — `#[repr(transparent)]` already lexes per the existing `#[repr]` infrastructure; the typechecker is the new work. (2) Typechecker carrier-shape validation at item-decl time: accept on `distinct type`, single-field `struct` (single non-zero-sized field; zero-sized companion fields are permitted iff every companion has size zero AND alignment one — `PhantomData[T]`, `()`, `[T; 0]`, an empty unit struct), and single-variant single-field `enum`. Reject multi-field struct (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_SINGLE_FIELD]`); zero-field struct (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_FIELD]`); enum with !=1 variant or with payload-less variant (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_ENUM_NOT_SINGLE_VARIANT]`); union (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_UNION_FORBIDDEN]`); generic carrier whose inner is a type parameter `T` without a `T: Sized` bound (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_SIZED]`). Combination with any other repr (`#[repr(C)]`, `#[repr(packed)]`, `#[repr(align(N))]`, `#[repr(intN)]`) is rejected (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_EXCLUSIVE]`). (3) Layout — codegen records the wrapper as a layout-pass-through to the inner field (no separate type registered in the LLVM type table; the wrapper's LLVM type *is* the inner type). The inner type's repr passes through unchanged: a `transparent` wrapper around a `#[repr(C)]` inner has the same layout as the inner. (4) FFI ABI integration — at `extern "C"` call sites, an argument of the wrapper type whose declared `extern` parameter type is the inner type is permitted with an explicit unwrap (`.raw()` for `distinct type`, named-field access for single-field struct carriers); the type system enforces the unwrap, but codegen lowers without conversion (the bit-pattern is identical). (5) Auto-derive integration — `#[derive(...)]` walks the carrier's fields normally for `Eq`/`PartialEq`/`Hash`/`Clone`/`Copy`/`Debug`; the existing distinct-type derive rules continue to govern `distinct type` carriers. (6) Orphan-rule integration — no special handling; `transparent` is a layout claim that doesn't change the orphan-rule arithmetic (the wrapper is still a local type for orphan purposes). Test plan: positive — `#[repr(transparent)] distinct type Fd = i32` round-trips through an `extern "C" fn close(fd: i32)` signature with `.raw()`; `#[repr(transparent)] struct Tagged[T] { inner: i32, _marker: PhantomData[T] }` accepts the zero-sized companion; layout-pass-through verified via `size_of` and `align_of` on wrapper equals same on inner. Negative — multi-field `struct Wrapper { a: i32, b: i32 }` rejected; zero-field `struct Empty {}` rejected; multi-variant `enum E { A(i32), B(i32) }` rejected; `union U` rejected; `#[repr(transparent, C)]` rejected; `#[repr(transparent)] struct Tagged[T] { inner: T }` without `T: Sized` rejected. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; depends on `#[repr]` parsing infrastructure being stable.)

- [ ] **FFI — Callback passing.** Define how Kāra closures (or function values, G51) are passed as C function pointers. Non-capturing functions can map directly to `fn` pointers. Capturing closures need a `void* context` + function pointer pair (standard C callback pattern). Document the effect implications — C callbacks are unverified effect boundaries.

- [ ] **FFI — String marshaling.** Define conversion between Kāra `String` (UTF-8, length-prefixed) and C strings (null-terminated `*const u8`). Provide stdlib helpers: `String.from_c(ptr)` (copies, validates UTF-8), `string.as_c_str()` (appends null terminator). Handle the allocation question — who owns the memory?

- [ ] **FFI — Error code mapping.** Define stdlib pattern for converting C-style error codes (`i32` return, `errno`) to Kāra `Result[T, E]`. Provide a `CError` type or trait-based conversion. Stdlib wrappers should use this consistently for all POSIX wrappers.

- [ ] **Dynamic dispatch / trait objects.** Implement trait object support. All design decisions are settled: (1) syntax is `dyn Trait` — the explicit keyword is required, and a bare trait name in a type position is a compile error; (2) unbound `dyn T` (no trait constraint) is not allowed — erasure without interface knowledge is useless; (3) multiple bounds allowed: `dyn Shape + Display`; (4) object safety: traits with generic methods cannot be used as trait objects — compiler emits a clear diagnostic; (5) owned `dyn Trait` requires heap allocation and produces `allocates(Heap)`; `ref dyn Trait` borrows an already-allocated value and does not; (6) effect semantics use an open-world model (design.md): the programmer declares the effect bound at the trait definition (`trait Handler with reads(UserDB), sends(AuditLog) { ... }`), all impls must have effects ⊆ that bound, and call sites use the declared trait bound as the effect set — no whole-program analysis needed; (7) trait objects cannot use `layout` blocks — concrete type is unknown at compile time. Implementation tasks: vtable layout and codegen (Phase 7 prerequisite), object safety checker in the type checker, `allocates(Heap)` inference for owned `dyn Trait` positions. Depends on Phase 3 trait system and Phase 7 LLVM codegen being stable.

- [ ] **G10 — Cycle detection with generic containers and trait objects.** Document the `dyn Trait` limitation in the ownership section. The compiler can't see through `dyn Trait` to detect cycles. Recommend `shared struct` with `weak` or `Arena` for patterns where trait objects create cycles. Consider whether the compiler should warn when `dyn Trait` appears in a position that could form a cycle.

- [ ] **G24 — Compile time strategy**. Validate that `pub` boundaries as inference firewalls effectively bound compilation cost. Benchmark full compilation on non-trivial programs. Ensure architecture supports incremental compilation, cached analysis, and parallel module compilation.

- [ ] **G25 — Standard Error trait**. Define `trait Error` with `message()` and `source()` chaining. Define `trait From[T]` for error conversion via `?` operator. Implement for all stdlib error types.

- [ ] **String interpolation format specifiers.** Design and implement `{expr:spec}` syntax in `f"..."` strings. Open questions: syntax form (Rust-style `{x:.2}`, Python-style `{x:.2f}`, or Kāra-specific); whether format specifiers desugar to a `Format` trait separate from `Display`; interaction with `#[derive(Display)]`; width, precision, fill, alignment, sign, radix. The syntax space is reserved — `{expr:spec}` is a compile error until this is implemented.

- [ ] **Conversion traits (`From`/`Into`/`TryFrom`/`TryInto`).** Implement the four conversion traits and the blanket impl (`impl From[T]` → automatic `Into`). Enforce: implementing `Into` directly is a compile error. Wire `?` operator to desugar cross-error-type propagation to `From.from()`. Refinement types auto-generate `TryFrom` impls. See design.md — "Conversion Traits".
  - **Slice 1 shipped** (commit `deff0e3`): `From` dispatch via `T.from(x)` with source-type disambiguation; 19 built-in numeric widening impls; user `impl From[E1] for E2` resolves; `?` typechecker validates cross-error `From` and records conversion target in `TypeCheckResult.question_conversions`; interpreter consults that side-table and calls `<Target>.from(e)` before propagating Err.
  - **Slice 3a shipped:** `.into()` with expected-type threading. `TypeChecker` gained `check_expr(expr, expected)` that recognizes a zero-arg `.into()` method call against a Named / primitive expected type and records the target in `TypeCheckResult.into_conversions` (span → target-type name). Expected-type threading is wired at four positions: (1) `let x: T = ...`, (2) `let x: T = ...` in `let-else`, (3) `Assign { target, value }` (target-type-driven), (4) function call argument slot against the parameter type, (5) explicit `return expr;` against the current function's return type, (6) function body final expression against the declared return type (via `check_block_against`). Lowering then rewrites `x.into()` to `Target.from(x)` — the `Into` blanket impl is purely a lowering rewrite, no impl entries materialized at typecheck time. Codegen falls through naturally: numeric widening is a passthrough in `compile_assoc_call`, user-type `T.from(x)` routes to the impl-block-compiled `T.from` LLVM function. Missing `impl From[S] for T` emits a targeted diagnostic with the source and target type names. `let` codegen now uses the type annotation as a fallback type hint when the RHS shape isn't classifiable (fixes user-struct `var_type_names` registration for `let c: Cm = i.into();`).
  - **Slice 3b shipped:** user `impl Into for T` and `impl TryInto for T` rejected at the resolver. Distinct from the operator-trait restriction (those only fire on ArithOps / Index / Display); Into/TryInto use their own `ResolveErrorKind::IntoTraitImplNotAllowed` (code `E0109`) with a suggestion to implement `From` / `TryFrom` instead.
  - **Follow-ups not in slice 3:**
    - `TryFrom` / `TryInto` with associated `Error` type; numeric narrowing impls.
    - `From[T] for Option[T]` and `From[T] for Result[T, E]` wrapping.
    - `From[StringLit] for String` / from char literals.
    - `.into()` expected-type threading at more positions (match arm bodies, struct-literal field values, if/match final expressions).
